## Aal Salma

Tags: state

Inhabited by humans, Qord'ik. Democracy, but struggling with crippling drug problem. Huge cartels.

## Adron

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Monarchy

**Primary Inhabitants**: Naga

**Population**: 500,000

**Stability**: Very Stable

**Core Values**: Honor, intelligence, dignity

- The Adrak nobility are famously powerful, well mannered, knowledgeable, and agreeable. They can also be condescending toward non-Naga outsiders, though rarely to the point of rudeness.
- Descendants of the first dragon, Naga have upheld their ancestors' values for eons. "A Naga without honor is no Naga at all" is a famous saying among Naga elders.
- Three major ley lines cross Adron—water, time, and dark—creating numerous intersections that produce an unusually high number of elementally attuned citizens.

### Economy

**Size**: Large

**Tech**: Very Developed

**Primary Exports**: Cultural artifacts, financial services, food, ships, iron, luxury goods, magic

**Primary Imports**: Animal products, luxury goods

- The Adrak economy relies heavily on the Royal Adrak Bank, famous for funding both sides of foreign wars and coming out on top regardless of the victor.
- A steady stream of red gold mined out of the Gozwin and Majesty Mountains has provided insane wealth to the nobility of Adrak, and is the source of the famous Adrak jewelry. Red gold is the most valuable currency in Alaria.
- The shipyards of Shipmarsh are among the finest in the Middle Sea, producing both merchant vessels and warships.

### Military

**Size**: Large

**Quality**: High

**Enrollment**: Mandatory

- Most Adrak citizens are enthusiastic to join the military, due to its prestige and honor. All Naga citizens are drafted at 19, where they serve until they are 23.
- The nobility generally are trained from a younger age to become leaders of the Adrak army, and it is customary for the king or queen of Adron to lead the charge into major battles.

### Geography

**Location**: Easternmost state on the Middle Sea, where the Kharvorn Mountains terminate

**Biomes**: Mediterranean coastline, temperate forests, mountain ranges, salt marshes, river valleys

**Climate**: Mediterranean—warm, dry summers and mild winters

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Adrak

**Cities**: Shipmarsh, Greyport

**Towns**: Numerous small towns scattered throughout, particularly along the Tenori River and around the western lakes

### Primary Conflicts

- The Dwarf King continues to steal from travelers through the Majesty Mountains. He is descendant of the dwarves who used to live there, believes the resources of the mountains belong to him.
- The Royal Adrak Bank is rumored to be funding all three sides of the War of Three Kingdoms.
- A large influx of Danaki refugees from the Danak-Atyeska war is angering citizens of the northern settlements.
- The dragon Chavux raids ships near The Blades, but killing a dragon is sacrilege—merchants in Greyport would pay handsomely to have the problem "solved" quietly.

### History

Adron was once the land of dragon riders. For centuries, Naga warriors bonded with dragons through sacred rituals at the Maw of Chao, blessed by Damasaki Edara herself. The Adrak dragon cavalry dominated the Middle Sea.

Roughly four centuries ago, the Waterdark conspiracy ended this golden age. The secret order—masters of water and darkness magic who had long resented draconic dominance—performed a coordinated ritual that severed every dragon-bond in Adron simultaneously. The dragons, suddenly feeling nothing for their riders, simply flew away. Many riders died from the psychic shock. Those who survived found they could no longer pass through Oblivion to reach the Maw of Chao.

The royal family preserved their dragon eggs and bred smaller, domesticated dragons—beautiful but nothing like the war-beasts of old. The art of true binding was lost. Modern Naga feel deep pride in their draconic heritage alongside quiet shame that they are no longer dragon riders. Some believe the old bond could be restored; others think attempting it would be an abomination.

Before the Naga, Tritons inhabited this land. Their exodus left drowned ruins beneath the western lakes—remnants of a civilization that departed for the Alrock Ocean eons ago.

## Aldriktch Trade Alliance

Tags: faction

### Overview

The Aldriktch Trade Alliance is an agreement between Erasnus, Watar, Myorna, Camaran, Bestacia, and Ubrik that dictates open trade routes between the countries. It sets limits on maximum tariffs for ports and foreign trade, and gives member nations more favorable trading rights.

Currently, the entie alliance is under threat, as tensions between Myorna and its neighbors continue to rise. Allowing Myorna into the trade alliance was only barely permitted (spear headed by phenomenal diplomats from both Myorna, Ubrik, and Bestacia), and now it's causing trouble.

It is also threated by the massive silvertongue outbreak in Ubrik, which has driven half the country into a canabalistic frenzy, terrorizing the nearby countryside. Erasnus is desperately trying to hold the alliance together (it is most profitable for them of all the countries), but it is difficult to hold on.

Camaran has become more isolationist recently as well, which spells trouble, and the Watari and Bestacians relations are getting worse as tension over control of the Telphineas Strait escalates. 

### History

Echea was vetoed by Camaran. Myorna was partially let in because people wanted access to the incredible quanities of silver in those mountains. Bestacian diplomats also hoped that it would deter war.

## Anarak

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Dictatorship

**Primary Inhabitants**: Anori, Oznak, Tikhaya (Humans)

**Population**: 300,000

**Stability**: Very Stable (through oppression)

**Core Values**: Patriotism, might, revenge

- Anarak is ruled by the black dragon Tepheranos, brother of Rothogomos. He is manipulative, greedy, and patient.
- The population has been brainwashed over a century to see Tepheranos as a savior rather than a tyrant. People are proud citizens; few choose to leave despite poor living conditions.
- The culture emphasizes martial prowess, loyalty to the state, and hatred of Argysis.

### Economy

**Size**: Small

**Tech**: Developed

**Primary Exports**: None

**Primary Imports**: None

- The Anarak economy is largely self-contained. Tepheranos restricts travel in and out of the country.
- Heavy taxation funds the military while most people live in poverty.
- The basin produces enough food to sustain the population, barely.

### Military

**Size**: Large

**Quality**: Medium

**Enrollment**: Mandatory

- The Anarak military is brutally strict, powerful, and filled with some of the cruelest, most ferocious soldiers anywhere.
- Everyone serves. The military is the path to status and escape from poverty.
- The army is ready for war—Tepheranos just needs a target he can hit without Rothogomos striking while he's exposed.

### Geography

**Location**: Great basin between the Crags of Geth (south) and the Kharvorn Mountains/Argysis (north)

**Biomes**: Basin grasslands, farmland, the Black Hills

**Climate**: Continental—harsh winters, hot summers

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Tephrakus (at the base of the Black Hills, near Tepheranos's lair)

**Cities**: Tephrakus, Nidzhoni (center of the basin)

**Towns**: Scattered agricultural settlements across the basin

### Primary Conflicts

**The Argysis Standoff**

Tepheranos and his brother Rothogomos are locked in a generations-long feud. Long ago, they came together to conquer Argysis and steal the dwarven treasure. Rothogomos betrayed Tepheranos, taking everything for himself. Tepheranos retreated to Anarak, built it into a regional power, and has plotted revenge ever since.

Neither dragon can commit forces elsewhere while the other lives. Argysis is weaker but fortified in the mountains; Anarak is stronger but has hundreds of miles of burnable farmland. The standoff continues.

**Expansionist Hunger**

Tepheranos is greedy. He wants more wealth, more territory, more everything. Anarak will invade whoever they can reach—Erasnus, Hephake, anyone who looks weak. But the Argysis situation ties their hands.

**The Goblin Raids**

Griselian goblins from the Crags of Geth terrorize southern villages. Whether genuine aggression or theatrical spillover is unclear. Either way, villagers suffer and the military can't fully respond while watching the northern border.

**Underground Dissent**

Not everyone believes the propaganda. Resistance cells exist, fragmented and frightened. Tepheranos's agents hunt them constantly, but dissent spreads anyway.

### History

Anarak used to be a free nation—unremarkable but peaceful. A century ago, Tepheranos arrived, secretly killed the king, and subjugated the people. Over the following decades, he brainwashed the population, transforming their understanding of history until they believed he was their savior, not their conqueror.

Now Anarak is a military state waiting for war. The only question is who Tepheranos can attack without leaving himself vulnerable to his brother's revenge.

## Argysis

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**:

**Primary Inhabitants**: Shyka

**Population**: 20,000

**Stability**: Stable

**Core Values**: Killing, vengeance

- Argysis is ruled over by the black dragon Rothogomos, enemy brother of Tepheranos. 
- The population worships Rothogomos as patron in their journey to destroy Tepheranos in the south, towards whom Rothogomos has swayed everyone's animosity. 


### Economy

**Size**: Very Small

**Tech**: Developed

**Primary Exports**: None

**Primary Imports**: None

- The Argysisean economy is totally isolated from the world, as few are willing to trade with the greedy, cutthroat traders of Argysis.


### Military

**Size**: Medium

**Quality**: High

**Enrollment**: Mandatory

- Everyone is enrolled in the military, and trained to a high level of proficiency. You do not leave the military until you reach late middle age.


### Geography

**Location**: 

**Biomes**: 

**Named Entities**:

**Rivers & Lakes**: 

**Adjacent Waters**: 


### Political Geography

**Capital**: 

**Cities**: 

**Towns**: 

**Villages**: 


### Primary Conflicts

- Argysis is locked in a currently bloodless war of vengeance with Anarak. Neither can commit to a full war against any other neighbor till the other is removed, but neither is strong enough to remove the other. Argysis is weaker, but is fortified in the mountain, so cannot be pried out. Anarak is stronger, but hundreds of miles of burnable farmland.
- Argysis wants to take over Hephake, which used to be its sibling kingdom, but cannot leave Argysis ungaurded.

## Astrelle

Tags: state

Home to the Stravlar goblins, though a fairly even mix of human/mish-mash and the Stravlar. The Stravlar lived here first, but they were conquered by Tarkhon relatively early in the Tarkon Wars.

## Atriik

Tags: state

pronounced "at-try(spanish "r")-**ike**"

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Confederation of monarch city-states

**Primary Inhabitants**: Kor, Sharabha

**Population**: 70,000

**Stability**: Stable

**Core Values**: Courtesy, policy, law, appearances, calmness

- Four royal families rule Atriik, each governing a different city-state
- Kor culture dictates politeness to levels viewed as absurd by outsiders—elaborate greeting rituals, indirect speech, and elaborate formal titles for every social interaction
- Social capital and one's standing in society is everything; public loss of face can end political careers
- Three city-states are Kor monarchies; one (Byonowidi) is Sharabha, and despite cultural similarity, is the source of persistent tension

### Economy

**Size**: Medium

**Tech**: Somewhat developed

**Primary Exports**: Furs, animal products, hardwoods from Sprenwood and Fatiik Forest

**Primary Imports**: Metal, weapons, finished goods from desert traders

- Forest industries dominate the west (Sprenwood, Fatiik Forest); hunting and animal husbandry in the central savanna
- Trade routes run north to Kura's glass markets and east toward the Kunagi Desert caravans

### Military

**Size**: Small

**Quality**: Medium

**Enrollment**: Voluntary

- Each city-state maintains its own militia; no unified Atriik army exists
- Sharabha cavalry from Byonowidi are considered the finest mounted warriors
- Chronic border skirmishes with Naruaghin raiders from the south

### Geography

**Location**: Southwestern Westrim, between the Milras Forest (north), the Dunes of Kunagi (east), the Bloodlands/Ishnit Jungles (south), and Shark Bay (west)

**Biomes**: Savanna-woodland transition, coastal forests, semi-arid scrubland

**Named Entities**: Milras Forest, Sprenwood, Fatiik Forest, Kunagi Hills, Mykala (colossal tree ruin)

**Rivers & Lakes**: Sha Puniki, Sha Ulokoni, Sha Kariki, Sha Sonisst

**Adjacent Waters**: Shark Bay (west)

### Political Geography

**Capital**: None (confederation of equals)

**City-States**:
- **Lupuno**: Northwestern city-state near Milras Forest, controls Sha Puniki river trade
- **Byonowidi**: Western city-state, the Sharabha monarchy, major fur trading hub
- **Shinii**: Eastern city-state, gateway to desert trade, borders Kunagi Hills
- **Wykakas**: Southern city-state, controls Sha Sonisst, buffer against Bloodlands

**Notable Sites**:
- **Mykala**: Ruined fortress at the base of a colossal tree (30-mile canopy, 2-mile trunk diameter), sacred site for all city-states, contested by a druid and an Elnor

### Primary Conflicts

- Three Kor city-states versus one Sharabha monarchy (Byonowidi): despite shared values, racial tensions occasionally flare into trade disputes and border arguments
- Naruaghin raids from the south across the Bloodlands keep southern cities on constant alert
- The Mykala situation: an Elnor attempting to take control of the sacred tree from its resident druid threatens the religious stability of all four city-states

### History

## Atyeska

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Sedentary tribes

**Primary Inhabitants**: Enti

**Population**: 90,000

**Stability**: Somewhat stable

**Core Values**: Raw strength, dominance, athleticism

- Dozens of enti tribes live across Atyeska, in constantly shifting territories. Battle is not uncommon, and taking prisoners is customary.
- Prisoners become slaves to the tribe, and are treated not inhumanely. They grow up in a tribe, and die in the tribe, and have relatively safe lives.


### Economy

**Size**: Very small
**Tech**: Very undeveloped
**Primary Exports**: Pelts, animal products
**Primary Imports**: Technology

- The Atyeska economy is primarily centered around trade. Lianthan Currency is worth very little here.
- Will leave on boats, sail for hundreds of miles, and perform massive raids on the neth who live even further north.
- Food come from fishing in Geshwin Passage

### Military

**Size**: Medium

**Quality**: Medium

**Enrollment**: Voluntary

- Although a significant portion of Atyeskans are members of the military, since they are not under one cohesive nation, that military is not united, and therefore significantly less powerful.
- Joining the military is not mandatory, but expected


### Geography

**Location**: 

**Biomes**: 

**Named Entities**:

**Rivers & Lakes**: 

**Adjacent Waters**: 


### Political Geography

**Capital**: 

**Cities**: 

**Towns**: 

**Villages**: 


### Primary Conflicts

- Although Atyeskan tribes are always at war with each other, the enti along the western border are stuck fighting a second war against the Danaki.ddddf.

## Avalon

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Theocracy

**Primary Inhabitants**: Temptari

**Population**: 200,000

**Stability**: Very Stable

**Core Values**: Relgion, truth, sacredness, seasons, the cycle of time, duty, fate, determinism

- Avalon is ruled over by the Grand Imperial Ecclesiarch, believed to be a walking god. They have not blinked or left their throne for their entire life, and they are said to be able to see the future.
- Multiple fiefdoms are each controlled by a local religious leader. These are all overseen by the Solum Impervium—the hand of the Ecclesiarch. 
- Many time attuned people live in Avalon. 


### Economy

**Size**: Large

**Tech**: Developed

**Primary Exports**: 

**Primary Imports**: None

- Tithes are collected by the church yearly, as foreseen to best suit the needs of Avalon by the Ecclesiarch in dreams.


### Military

**Size**: Small

**Quality**: Extremely High

**Enrollment**: Voluntary

- As with most careers, a career in the military starts at age 8, after being brought before the local priest, who declares their future expertise. Soldiers are chosen for special skill in the forces of time, and are raised and trained in isolation from their families for a decade before entering the force. They are machine-like in their skill, never make mistakes, and are utterly unpredictable and deadly.


### Geography

**Location**: Central-western Ve, north of the Widebarrow Mountains, south of Sestros

**Biomes**: Temperate grasslands, mixed forests

**Named Entities**: Goldwood (west), Pathanul (north), Promisewood (south), Shorolyn Forest (east), Honor Moss (central wetland)

**Rivers & Lakes**: Honor River (central), Honor Creek (northeast branch), Pale Run (south)

**Adjacent Waters**: Munari Inlet (west coast)


### Political Geography

**Capital**: Tarolin (central, on Honor River)

**Cities**: Ismail (west coast, Honor River outlet), Karahoroz (east)

**Major Towns (West to East)**: Mekenk, Micitlar, Orenonu, Zindi, Incebolu, Daralan, Kenzek, Burga, Maral, Sukanli, Yasyan, Taylilar

**Towns (South)**: Makavla, Ayni

**Towns (Northeast)**: Civicvler, Sarihalliler, Kochisar


### Primary Conflicts

- Corruption in more minor religious roles is common, and a frequent cause of strife.
- People's partners in life are chosen for them, but not always correctly.


### History

## Azawahasi

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Independent nomadic tribes

**Primary Inhabitants**: Sharabha

**Population**: 10,000

**Stability**: Stable

**Core Values**: Honor, duty, self-sufficiency, gift-giving

- Sharabha tribes function like lion prides—a strong male and his brothers lead a tribe of up to 50 people. Everyone knows their role, their place in the Pride Circle, and their obligations to the group.
- The Sharabha are descendants of Shara Bolasi, the great lion father who died fighting the titan Hykravones. His blood transformed the land and the people who settled upon it. This shared ancestry creates deep bonds across tribal lines.
- Honor is paramount. "My honor before my life" isn't a saying—it's how Sharabha actually live. Oaths are taken seriously, debts are remembered, and reputation matters more than wealth.
- The two major Sharabha cultures—Sharakari (Pride Guardians) and Sharadin (Oathspeakers)—both exist here, with different tribes following different traditions.

### Economy

**Size**: Very Small

**Tech**: Very Undeveloped

**Primary Exports**: Beads, furs, animal products, ivory

**Primary Imports**: Furs, textiles, art, metal goods

- The Sharabha have little use for money. Within tribes, everything is shared. Between tribes, gift-giving establishes relationships—you don't trade with strangers, you give gifts to friends and receive gifts in return.
- Hunts occur every few weeks, targeting the massive game that roams Azawahasi: elephants, great cats, enormous antelope. The hunts are communal events involving multiple families working together.
- Outsiders who want to trade must first establish themselves as friends through gift exchange. Merchants who try to conduct business without this social foundation are viewed with suspicion or contempt.
- The Sharabha produce exceptional leather goods, bone carvings, and beadwork. These items are valued trade goods for the few merchants who've learned how to work with Sharabha customs.

### Military

**Size**: None

**Quality**: High

**Enrollment**: N/A

- The Sharabha have no standing army because they don't need one. Every adult can fight. Every adult has trained since childhood. Every adult can transform into a lion-like form with fangs and claws.
- Tribal conflicts are resolved through ritual combat, negotiation, or (rarely) small-scale skirmishes. Full warfare between tribes is almost unknown—the shared honor code makes atrocities unthinkable.
- When external threats arise, tribes coordinate rapidly. The goblin broods learned long ago that raiding Sharabha territory invites devastating retaliation. A coordinated Sharabha response is terrifying—dozens of lion-warriors hunting as a single pride.
- Individual Sharabha warriors are among the most dangerous fighters in the region. The combination of honor-driven fearlessness and lion transformation makes them lethal opponents.

### Geography

**Location**: Eastern portion of the transition zone between Ofrenia and southern Rimihuica

**Biomes**: Savanna, grassland, scattered forest, coastal plains

**Named Entities**: Plains of Eregnar, Forest of Esperanza, the Central Hills

**Rivers & Lakes**: Seasonal rivers, scattered watering holes that determine tribal movement patterns

**Adjacent Waters**: The Middle Sea (east)

### Political Geography

**Capital**: None (nomadic)

**Cities**: None

**Towns**: None permanent

**Villages**: Semi-permanent seasonal camps at reliable water sources

### Primary Conflicts

**The Generational Divide**

Young Sharabha increasingly leave their tribes to see the wider world. They return (if they return) with foreign ideas, foreign goods, and foreign attitudes. Elders view this as corruption—traditional ways being abandoned for flashy novelty. The young see it as growth and opportunity. The argument plays out in every tribe, with no resolution in sight.

**The Goblin Nuisance**

Scalawag goblins from the western plains occasionally raid Azawahasi territory. The raids are more annoying than threatening—the goblins can't stand against Sharabha warriors—but they disrupt hunts, steal supplies, and require responses that take warriors away from productive work.

**The Honor Paradox**

Sharabha honor code makes them excellent warriors but complicated diplomats. They struggle with societies that don't share their values—where oaths are broken, where gift-giving is seen as bribery, where reputation counts for nothing. Navigating the outside world without compromising their principles is an ongoing challenge.


### History

The Sharabha emerged on this land after Shara Bolasi's final battle against the titan Hykravones. The great lion father died, but his blood transformed the earth where it fell. Generations later, humans who settled this transformed land found themselves changing—becoming something new, something more.

The first Sharabha discovered their lion forms during times of great emotion—protecting loved ones, defending against predators, facing impossible odds. They learned to channel Shara Bolasi's legacy, to transform at will, to carry his courage in their blood.

For centuries, the Sharabha have lived as their ancestors did. Tribes follow the herds. Pride Circles define loyalty and obligation. Honor governs everything. The system works—Azawahasi has been stable while kingdoms rise and fall around it.

But stability isn't stagnation, and the Sharabha are changing whether the elders like it or not. Young warriors return from foreign lands with new ideas. Traders from the United Free Nations bring goods and concepts unknown to traditional culture. The world is getting smaller, and Azawahasi can't stay isolated forever.

The question isn't whether the Sharabha will change, but how—and whether they can preserve what matters while adapting to what's coming.

## Azuros

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Theocracy

**Primary Inhabitants**: Humans

**Population**: 8,000

**Stability**: Very Stable

**Core Values**: Discipline, silence, respect, abstinence from pleasure

- Various subsects of the Shogi Monastery practice here in different monk groups. Each is managed by a head monk, who sits on the Council of the Silent Elders which oversees the mountain. All are taught by a mysterious figure known as the Rhea monk.
- Families are raised in simple stone houses built on the side of the mountain. Life is austere, contemplative, and governed by ritual.
- A large percentage of the population have attunements to air, due to the high altitude and powerful winds that constantly sweep the peaks. The monastery encourages this development.
- The order demands full devotion. Those who achieve mastery become something remarkable—able to walk on air, fly, call forth lightning. The greatest monks are legendary figures, spoken of in hushed tones across Alaria.

### Economy

**Size**: Very Small

**Tech**: Undeveloped

**Primary Exports**: Air elemental masters (who leave to serve or teach elsewhere)

**Primary Imports**: None

- Azuros is little more than a collection of villages surrounding the monastery. There is almost no economy to speak of—the monks grow what they need and want nothing else.
- The monastery produces nothing for trade. Pilgrims occasionally bring gifts, which are accepted with humility and distributed to those in need.
- The only "export" is the monks themselves. Those who complete their training sometimes leave to serve as teachers, advisors, or guardians elsewhere. Their services are never purchased—they go where they feel called.

### Military

**Size**: None

**Quality**: N/A

**Enrollment**: Forbidden

- The Azuros monks forbid violence. To become involved in a physical altercation is deeply shameful. The monastery has no warriors, no guards, no defenses.
- There is little wealth to steal from Azuros, and so no one bothers trying. The difficulty of reaching the monastery, combined with the absence of anything worth taking, makes it secure through irrelevance.
- That said, the most powerful monks could devastate armies if they chose. They don't choose. The threat is never spoken but universally understood.

### Geography

**Location**: Northern Erpeus Island, the highest peaks

**Biomes**: Alpine mountains, wind-scoured peaks, high meadows

**Named Entities**: Shogi Monastery, Devil's Crest (southern border)

**Rivers & Lakes**: Mountain streams, snowmelt pools

**Adjacent Waters**: The Middle Sea (visible from the heights)

### Political Geography

**Capital**: The Shogi Monastery (no formal capital)

**Cities**: None

**Towns**: None

**Villages**: Azur, Pul, and several unnamed settlements clinging to the mountainsides

### Primary Conflicts

**Isolation and Stagnation**

Traveling to Azuros is like traveling back in time. The monastery interacts so little with the outside world that it has fallen behind technologically and culturally. Some younger monks question whether complete isolation serves the order's true purpose—but questioning itself is discouraged.

**The Rhea Monk**

The mysterious figure who teaches the head monks is ancient, powerful, and increasingly absent. Some say the Rhea monk is dying. Others say they have transcended mortality entirely. The uncertainty creates quiet tension among the Council of Silent Elders.

**The Murder Hills**

The path to Azuros passes through Lier's Murder Hills, where bandits and worse prey on travelers. The monastery officially doesn't acknowledge the problem—violence is forbidden, and the monks won't fight even in self-defense. Pilgrims must fend for themselves.

**The World Encroaches**

Despite centuries of isolation, Azuros cannot remain untouched forever. Wars, magical catastrophes, and political upheavals across the Middle Sea send ripples that eventually reach even the highest peaks. Some monks have begun wondering whether withdrawal from the world is sustainable—or responsible.

### History

The Shogi Monastery was founded in an age before reliable records, by monks seeking a place where the wind blew pure and the world's distractions couldn't reach. They found the peaks of northern Erpeus and began building—simple stone structures that have survived centuries.

The monastery developed its techniques for working with air magic over generations, guided by the Rhea monk whose origins are lost to legend. Students learned to feel the wind as an extension of themselves, to ride the currents, eventually to become one with the element.

The order grew slowly. Those who couldn't commit to its demands left; those who remained became something extraordinary. The most powerful monks achieved abilities that looked like miracles—flight, lightning-calling, storm-speaking. They used these abilities only for contemplation and never for conflict.

Modern Azuros is much as it was centuries ago. The same stone houses. The same rituals. The same devotion to discipline and silence. The outside world has changed beyond recognition; Azuros hasn't changed at all. Whether this is wisdom or blindness depends on who you ask—but the monks don't ask, and don't answer.

## Balduahr

Tags: state

Inhabited by gray-stone dwarves. Citadel is to the west is a juicy target, but unattainable, as the hills are chalk full of giants.

## Bestacia

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Democratic republic

**Primary Inhabitants**: Goshwen (Hill Gnomes)

**Population**: 30,000

**Stability**: Stable (deteriorating)

**Core Values**: Freedom, invention, independence, gratitude

- Bestacia boasts one of the happiest populations on Alaria. Plentiful food, rewarding lifestyles, and a culture of gratitude and contentment.
- Notable for producing great scholars in art, philosophy, history, medicine, literature, and law. Education is widely valued; institutions here are among the finest.
- Goshwen are clever, inventive, good-natured. They've never built empires or started wars—they'd rather tinker and abstain from violence.

### Economy

**Size**: Medium

**Tech**: Developed

**Primary Exports**: Research, inventions, trained scholars, legal expertise

**Primary Imports**: A little bit of nearly everything

- Member of the Aldriktch Trade Alliance. Bestacian diplomats helped secure Myorna's membership, hoping it would deter war.
- The economy runs on intellectual output rather than raw materials or manufacturing.

### Military

**Size**: Small

**Quality**: Low

**Enrollment**: Voluntary

- The Bestacian military is pitiful. Most Goshwen want nothing to do with war and would rather stay home working on inventions.
- What Bestacia lacks in military strength, it makes up for in intrigue. They have sharper minds than their neighbors and play the diplomatic game well—spies, information brokers, legal manipulation, and quiet influence.

### Geography

**Location**: Middle Sea coast, between Ubrik (east) and Watar (west), with mountains along the southern border

**Biomes**: Temperate forests, rolling hills, mountain ranges to the south

**Climate**: Mild and pleasant—good growing weather

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Petra

**Cities**: Petra, Kisoy

**Towns**: Pastrova (home to one of the best law schools in Alaria), various small settlements

### The Ghoul Problem

Bestacia's forests are infested with ghouls. These soulless undead—created by ancient wizards, driven by eternal hunger for flesh and magic—lurk in the woodlands and prey on travelers.

The gnomes barely tolerate this. They can't deal with it effectively—their military is too weak, and ghouls are difficult to kill without elemental mages. Ghoul hunters pass through occasionally, but the problem persists. Most Bestacians simply avoid the deep forests and hope the ghouls stay there.

This is not coexistence. Ghouls are monsters. But the gnomes lack the martial strength to exterminate them.

### The Southern Mountains

The mountain range along Bestacia's southern border separates the country from the Telphineas Strait. Kisoy sits just north of these mountains.

The mountains are home to all sorts of interesting creatures—the Goshwen have a fondness for exotic fauna, and the peaks have become something of a menagerie. Some creatures were brought here deliberately; others simply found the mountains hospitable and stayed.

### Primary Conflicts

**The Telphineas Strait**

South of the mountains lies the Telphineas Strait—a crucial trade chokepoint. Whoever controls it can impose tariffs on shipping and effectively win the economic game. Bestacia wants control but has limited access; the mountains block easy passage, and their military can't project force.

Watar also wants the strait. Tensions are escalating. Bestacia is playing the intrigue game—diplomatic pressure, trade agreements, legal maneuvering—while Watar has actual ships.

**The Ubrik Crisis**

Silvertongue incursions from Ubrik are hitting Bestacia's eastern border. Refugees are flooding in. The gnomes are sympathetic but overwhelmed—their tiny military can't stop the silvertongues, and their communities can't absorb unlimited refugees.

**Intellectual Sabotage**

Even in good times, competition for academic acclaim leads to theft and sabotage. Scholars steal research, claim credit for others' work, and undermine rivals. It's ugly, but contained.

**Alliance Strain**

The Aldriktch Trade Alliance is fracturing. Bestacia helped build it, but Camaran is isolating, Ubrik is collapsing, and the Watar tensions are worsening. Erasnus is desperately trying to hold things together.

### History

Bestacia was founded by Goshwen who wanted a peaceful place to think, invent, and live well. They succeeded—for centuries, it's been a quiet, prosperous republic where clever gnomes could pursue their interests without interference.

They never built a military because they never needed one. Neighbors fought each other; Bestacia stayed out of it. The forests acquired a ghoul problem at some point, but the gnomes learned to avoid the deep woods.

Now the peace is ending. Ubrik is vomiting refugees and monsters across the eastern border. Watar is pushing for control of the strait. The alliance is crumbling. Bestacia's greatest asset—its minds—may not be enough to navigate what's coming.

## Bonnetaz

Tags: state, city-state, sandreach, kuzagt

The city of salt and bone. Bonnetaz rises from the blinding white of the Salt Flats like a fever dream—towers of crystallized salt reinforced with ancient fossils, their surfaces carved in geometric patterns that catch the light. Beautiful from a distance. Up close, visitors notice the ornamentation is human bone.

The Kuzagt have ruled here for over a thousand years, since before humans arrived in significant numbers on this continent. They do not consider themselves cruel. They consider themselves practical. Humans breed quickly, die easily, and make excellent raw material. The Flats demand labor. The Kuzagt provide it.

To outsiders, Bonnetaz is a nightmare made functional—a slave state so methodical in its brutality that it has achieved a kind of terrible efficiency. To the Kuzagt themselves, they are simply harvesting a renewable resource.

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Oligarchical council

**Primary Inhabitants**: Kuzagt (Bone Elves), humans (enslaved)

**Population**: ~12,000 Kuzagt; ~3,000 humans (city proper); ~40,000 humans (camps)

**Stability**: Extremely stable (unchanged for centuries)

**Core Values**: Efficiency, hierarchy, self-sufficiency, tradition

#### The Council of Thirteen

Thirteen bloodlines share power in Bonnetaz, each holding a hereditary seat on the ruling council. Succession within bloodlines varies by family tradition—some practice primogeniture, others allow siblings to assassinate each other for position, a few hold internal votes. The council itself operates by consensus; deadlocks are rare because Kuzagt take the long view. A matter that cannot be resolved today may resolve itself in a decade.

The council meets in the Pale Spire, the tallest structure in Bonnetaz. Sessions are closed to non-Kuzagt, and decisions are announced rather than debated publicly. Outsiders attempting to observe council proceedings have historically not been seen again.

The current council has remained stable for nearly a century—unusually long even by Kuzagt standards. Some attribute this to prosperity. Others whisper that certain elder members have discovered methods of extending their already considerable lifespans beyond natural limits.

#### Rank and Display

Kuzagt society is rigidly hierarchical, and rank is literally embedded in the face. All Kuzagt possess distinctive bony protrusions from their cheekbones—the source of their common name. These protrusions serve as mounting points for gems that denote status:

- **Unadorned**: Common citizens, laborers, craftspeople
- **Garnets, amber, jade**: Minor nobility, successful merchants, professional overseers
- **Sapphires, rubies**: Council families and their close relatives
- **Diamonds**: Council members themselves, arranged in patterns denoting specific lineages

Attempting to wear gems above one's station is punishable by death. The Kuzagt take hierarchy seriously.

#### The Human Population

Humans in Bonnetaz fall into three categories:

**The Camps**: Approximately forty thousand slaves labor in the underground warrens radiating outward from the city. They extract salt, maintain tunnels, process raw materials, and die. Life expectancy in the camps averages eight to twelve years.

**City Servants**: Perhaps three thousand humans work within Bonnetaz proper—domestic servants, skilled craftspeople, entertainers, and specialists too valuable to waste on camp labor. Their status falls between slave and citizen: permitted certain freedoms, even paid wages, but never permitted to leave. Many were born in this role; their parents were too useful to send to the camps, and they inherited that usefulness.

**Outsiders**: Foreign merchants, sailors, and traders pass through on business. They are housed in designated quarters, permitted access to trading halls, and forbidden from most of the city. Those who violate the rules are... reassigned.

### Religion & Culture

#### The Long Perspective

Kuzagt live for centuries. This shapes everything about their culture.

They do not rush. A decision that will matter in fifty years receives fifty years of consideration. Their art emphasizes permanence—bone and salt and lacquered stone, materials that endure. Their grudges endure similarly. A Kuzagt offended today may wait three human generations before seeking revenge.

This patience makes them profoundly alien to shorter-lived species. Kuzagt find human urgency amusing, dwarven grudge-keeping amateurish, and elven detachment insufficiently practical. They alone, in their view, have achieved the correct balance: passionate enough to act, patient enough to act correctly.

#### Blood and Bone

The Kuzagt drink fermented blood—not for sustenance but for ritual and pleasure. The best vintages are aged for decades in bone vessels, developing complex flavors that younger races cannot appreciate. Sharing blood wine signifies trust; refusing it signifies either insult or wisdom, depending on context.

Human leather appears throughout Kuzagt material culture: robes for the elite, book bindings, decorative elements. The Kuzagt see nothing wrong with this. Humans die; their materials remain useful. Waste offends them more than death.

#### The Calendar of Bones

The Kuzagt maintain their own calendar independent of Alarian standard, though they are aware of external dating for trade purposes. Their year is divided by the ossification of specific creatures—a cycle based on how long various bones take to properly cure. This makes their ceremonies incomprehensible to outsiders and precisely timed for them.

Major observances include:

- **The Harvest Festival**: Celebrating the annual intake of new slaves, held when the camps' population reaches its annual peak
- **The Rendering**: A ceremony of death and transformation, where the previous year's deceased (Kuzagt and significant humans alike) are processed into materials
- **The Pale Dawn**: A three-day period when the Salt Flats' reflected light creates unusual optical effects, considered auspicious for major decisions

### Economy

**Size**: Medium (regionally significant)

**Tech**: Developed (specialized)

**Primary Exports**: Salt (numerous specialized grades), bone crafts, alchemical compounds, preserved goods

**Primary Imports**: Slaves, food, water, metals, luxury goods

#### The Salt Trade

Not all salt is equal. The Kuzagt have identified dozens of distinct varieties based on mineral content, crystal structure, and depth of excavation:

- **White Salt**: Common table salt, the bulk of exports
- **Preservation Salt**: High mineral content, extends food freshness significantly
- **Ritual Salt**: Specific grades used in magical practices, commands premium prices
- **Poison Salt**: Toxic to specific creatures—fae, certain undead, particular demon types
- **Blood Salt**: Produced through proprietary processes involving human blood; used in Deoric rituals

This specialization represents centuries of accumulated expertise. Competitors can produce salt; they cannot produce the *right* salt for specific purposes. This knowledge base is Bonnetaz's true wealth.

#### The Ivory Hand

Bonnetaz does not acquire slaves directly. The Kuzagt consider such work beneath them—hunting, capturing, transporting, all terribly undignified. Instead, they purchase through the Ivory Hand merchant network.

The Hand maintains permanent representatives in the city, handling logistics while the Kuzagt focus on "productive employment." Several Bonnetaz merchants hold Ivory Hand membership themselves, participating in the organization's broader activities—including supplying sacrificial subjects for Deoric rituals across Alaria.

The Kuzagt officially disapprove of Deoric magic. They accept payment for "specialized inventory" without asking questions.

### Military

**Size**: Small (defensive focus)

**Quality**: High (specialized)

**Enrollment**: Professional only

#### The Salt Guard

Bonnetaz maintains no standing army in the traditional sense. Why would they? The Flats themselves are defense enough. Any invading force must cross a hundred miles of salt—no water, no shade, no shelter—while the Kuzagt simply wait.

The Salt Guard instead focuses on internal security: controlling the slave population, protecting trade routes, and enforcing the council's will. Approximately two thousand Kuzagt serve in this capacity, organized into specialized units:

- **The Pale Watch**: City security and camp oversight
- **The Bone Wardens**: Elite enforcers who handle "sensitive" problems
- **The Salt Sailors**: Naval forces protecting maritime approaches

#### Defensive Doctrine

If enemies somehow reached Bonnetaz, the city would descend into its tunnels. The underground network extends for miles, stocked with supplies sufficient for years. The Kuzagt would wait out any siege while the Flats killed the besiegers.

No one has tested this doctrine. The Kuzagt consider this proof of its effectiveness.

### Geography

**Location**: Salt Flats, northeastern Sandreach

**Biomes**: Salt flat, coastal desert

**Named Regions**: Salt Flats, Bone Hills

**Adjacent Waters**: Gindrik Sea

The city itself stands on the coast where the Salt Flats meet the Gindrik Sea—the only reliable water access in the region. The harbor is modest by continental standards but essential for trade.

Behind the city, the Flats extend south and west for a hundred miles before rising into the Bone Hills and eventually the Luquihn Desert proper. This terrain provides natural defense and natural resources: salt from the Flats, fossils and minerals from the Hills.

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Bonnetaz (city-state, sole settlement)

**Major Facilities**: The Camps (distributed underground network)

**Key Locations**: The Pale Spire (council seat), the Harbor Quarter (trade), the Bone Hills (mining operations)

### Relations

**Ethadia**: Primary trading partner. Ethadian ships carry Kuzagt salt to markets that would never deal with Bonnetaz directly. Both parties profit. Neither discusses the moral implications.

**Gorath**: Mutual contempt. The Kuzagt view Gorathi slavery as crude, wasteful, and vulgar. Gorath views Bonnetaz as too distant and too entrenched to be worth conquering. They ignore each other.

**The Ivory Hand**: Essential partnership. The Hand supplies slaves; Bonnetaz supplies specialized goods and asks no questions about their ultimate use.

**The Free Isles**: Occasional trading, carefully managed. Many Isles populations include escaped slaves, which creates awkwardness. Bonnetaz merchants visiting the Isles do not discuss their city's economy.

### History

The Kuzagt arrived on the Salt Flats over a thousand years ago, fleeing some catastrophe in their original homeland that they do not discuss with outsiders. They found the Flats hostile but habitable—brutal summers, flooding winters, and no competition for resources.

For centuries they were a minor settlement, harvesting salt for their own use and trading small quantities with passing ships. The arrival of humans on the continent changed everything. The Kuzagt recognized a resource: abundant, replaceable, and useful.

The slave camps expanded gradually. First dozens, then hundreds, then thousands of humans labored beneath the salt. Bonnetaz grew wealthy. The council ossified into its current form. The Kuzagt achieved what they consider their ideal state: stable, prosperous, and permanent.

They see no reason to change.

### Hooks & Tensions

**The Council's Secret**: How have the eldest council members survived so long? Rumors suggest the Weeping Vein—a preservative substance from the Bone Hills—can extend elven lifespans indefinitely when properly applied. But the process may require... fresh materials.

**The Underground Railroad**: Slaves occasionally escape despite impossible odds. Someone is running an escape network through the camps. The council wants them found—and made an example.

**Castle Alexandr**: The mysterious fortress on the promontory has defeated every attempt at occupation. The Kuzagt know something about what lies beneath it. They are not sharing.

**The Ivory Hand's Request**: The Hand wants something the council hasn't provided before—a specific type of "inventory" for a specific ritual. The council is debating whether the price is worth the implications.

**The Walking Bones**: Excavations in the Bone Hills sometimes uncover fossils that resist extraction. Bones that move when unobserved. The Kuzagt have learned which sites to avoid. Lately, the avoidance zones are growing.

## Breia

Tags: state

Golden skinned sky-knights. Numerous towers in the sky, interconnected city built on towers. Higher nobility ride on griffin. Harvest water from the clouds (no water down below). Had city Shtaneres until Hermelia burned it to the ground and fled.

Inhabited by the Inavolin.

Noble, intelligent.

### Shtaneres


Once a great city of Breia. However, Hermelia worked there, got pissed, and burned the entire thing down.

## Bynü Island Tribes

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Tribal confederation (barely)

**Primary Inhabitants**: Xicrein elves

**Population**: ~15,000 (scattered across hundreds of islands)

**Stability**: Stable through isolation (outsiders don't survive long enough to cause instability)

**Core Values**: Ancestral territory, twilight sovereignty, the killing of intruders

The Bynü Islands exist in permanent dusk. A magical phenomenon—or curse, depending on who you ask—shrouds this archipelago in eternal twilight. The sun never fully rises here; the stars never fully emerge. The Xicrein elves who call these islands home have adapted to this half-light over millennia.

They've also adapted to defending it.

The Xicrein are not negotiators. They do not trade. They do not allow visitors. Ships that enter Bynü waters without permission are attacked without warning. Survivors are not taken. The islands have earned their reputation through consistent, merciless violence against outsiders.

This isn't xenophobia born of ignorance—the Xicrein know exactly what the outside world offers. They've decided they don't want it.

### The Xicrein

The twilight elves of Bynü are visually distinct from their cousins elsewhere in Alaria. Their skin is pale gray to deep charcoal. Their eyes are enormous, adapted to the perpetual dimness—solid black orbs that unsettle even other elves. They move silently, see in near-darkness, and have spent generations perfecting the art of killing things that don't belong.

Xicrein culture revolves around the islands themselves. Each major island has a tribe; each tribe has territory; territorial boundaries are sacred. Inter-tribal conflicts are resolved through ritual—elaborate negotiations, formal duels, or seasonal wars fought with strict rules. But these rules don't apply to outsiders.

Outsiders have no status. They're not enemies to negotiate with—they're vermin to exterminate.

### The Twilight

No one knows why the Bynü Islands exist in permanent dusk. Theories range from ancient magical catastrophe to deliberate elven artifice to the influence of entities from other planes.

The twilight is real and constant. Ships approaching the islands watch the sun dim as they cross an invisible boundary. The transition takes perhaps an hour; by the time you're among the islands proper, it's perpetual half-night.

This affects everything. The ecology runs on twilight cycles—plants that never need full sun, animals that hunt in eternal dimness. The Xicrein have adapted completely; their eyes, their hunting patterns, their entire way of life assumes the sun will never truly rise.

Visitors (the rare ones who survive) find the twilight disorienting. Humans lose track of time. Sleep cycles collapse. The psychological pressure of endless dusk has broken more than one expedition.

### The Islands

The Bynü archipelago consists of perhaps a hundred significant islands and countless smaller ones. The terrain is dramatic: massive dark rocks with overhanging cliffs, forests of black-leafed palm trees, caves and grottos carved by eternal tides.

The water is dark. Not polluted—just dark, absorbing light rather than reflecting it. Even at the surface, you can't see more than a few feet down. This makes naval combat terrifying. Xicrein warriors attack from beneath, using the darkness as cover.

### The Tribes

Each major tribe controls a cluster of islands and maintains its own traditions within the broader Xicrein culture:

**The Cliffdwellers**: Occupy the northern islands, living in cave complexes carved into sea cliffs. They're the most likely to encounter (and kill) approaching ships.

**The Deeproot**: Central islands, forest-dwelling. Their territory is the most densely vegetated; they hunt from the trees.

**The Tidewatchers**: Southern islands, semi-aquatic. They spend as much time in the dark water as on land. Their warriors can hold their breath for disturbing lengths of time.

**The Stonetongue**: Eastern islands, keepers of oral tradition. They maintain the histories and laws that bind the tribes together.

**The Nightsingers**: Western islands, practitioners of a form of sound-based magic that works best in darkness. Their songs can disorient, terrify, or kill.

### Why So Hostile?

The Xicrein weren't always this violent toward outsiders. Old records from other nations describe occasional trade, diplomatic contact, even alliances.

Then something happened. The Xicrein call it **The Violation**—an event perhaps three centuries ago that they refuse to discuss with outsiders. Whatever occurred, it transformed Xicrein policy from wariness to extermination.

Scholars speculate about slaving raids, magical exploitation, or religious desecration. The Xicrein won't say. They'll only demonstrate, repeatedly, that the Bynü Islands are not for outsiders.

### Economy

**Size**: Small (self-sufficient)

**Tech**: Standard elven craftsmanship, specialized for twilight conditions

**Primary Exports**: None (deliberate isolation)

**Primary Imports**: None (deliberate isolation)

The Xicrein don't trade. They take what they need from the sea, the land, and the rare ships foolish enough to enter their waters. Salvage from wrecked vessels provides metal, cloth, and other materials the islands don't produce.

This isn't poverty—the islands provide abundantly. Fish are plentiful. Twilight-adapted plants yield food and materials. The Xicrein simply don't need or want what outsiders offer.

### Military

**Size**: The entire population

**Quality**: Exceptional in their environment

**Enrollment**: Universal (every Xicrein learns to fight)

Every adult Xicrein can fight. There's no professional military because there's no civilian population—the distinction doesn't exist. Children learn to kill intruders alongside learning to fish and farm.

Xicrein warfare is built around the twilight advantage. They see perfectly in the dimness; their enemies don't. They know every current, every rock, every shadow. They attack silently from unexpected directions. They don't negotiate surrender.

**Tactics:**
- Ships are swarmed by warriors in small boats or simply swimming
- Intruders on land are stalked through the forests, picked off one by one
- The Nightsingers use sonic magic to disorient and terrify
- Bodies are left on the boundary as warnings

### Geography

**Location**: Western Shattered Sea, west of Knova

**Biomes**: Twilight-adapted island ecology

**Climate**: Mild, humid, perpetually dim

**Named Features**: The individual islands aren't named on outsider maps—the Xicrein don't share that information

### Political Geography

**No Capital**: The tribes have no central authority. They cooperate against external threats and resolve internal disputes through tradition, but no one rules the Bynü Islands.

**Tribal Territories**: Each tribe's boundaries are precisely defined and fiercely defended—against other tribes as much as outsiders.

### Primary Conflicts

**The Boundary Debates**

Where does Bynü territory end? The Xicrein claim waters that other nations consider open sea. Ships passing "too close" have been attacked. No one agrees on where the line is—except the Xicrein, who won't say.

**The Memory of Violation**

Whatever happened three centuries ago still shapes Xicrein policy. Some younger elves question whether permanent isolation serves the people. Elders respond that the outside world proved itself untrustworthy. The debate is private—but it exists.

**The Nightsinger Question**

The Nightsinger tribe's magic has been growing stronger. Some other tribes worry about the balance of power shifting. Nightsinger influence could unite the islands—or tear them apart.

### Notable Figures

Outsiders don't know Xicrein names. The tribes don't introduce themselves before killing visitors. Any information about Xicrein leadership comes from old records, prisoner interrogations (rare), or speculation.

**The Cliffdweller Matriarch** — Reportedly the oldest living Xicrein, she supposedly remembers events before the Violation. She doesn't speak to outsiders.

**The Nightsinger Chorus** — The Nightsinger tribe is led by a council of their strongest sonic mages. How many, no one outside knows.

### History

**The Settling**: Xicrein elves arrived in the Bynü Islands in deep antiquity. Whether they caused the twilight or found it, no one outside knows.

**The Open Period**: For most of recorded history, the Bynü had limited but real contact with the outside world. Trade was possible. Diplomacy existed.

**The Violation** (~300 years ago): Something happened. The Xicrein closed their borders and began killing anyone who crossed them. They've maintained this policy ever since.

**The Present**: The Bynü Islands remain isolated, hostile, and mysterious. Ships avoid them. Scholars speculate about them. The Xicrein continue killing anyone who enters uninvited.

### What Players Might Want

- **The Violation's Truth**: What actually happened? Could revealing it change Xicrein policy?
- **Xicrein Artifacts**: The twilight islands produce unique materials. Getting them requires surviving the Xicrein.
- **First Contact**: Could someone actually make peaceful contact? What would it take?
- **The Twilight Source**: What causes the perpetual dusk? Could it be replicated—or ended?

## Camaran

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Republic

**Primary Inhabitants**: Humans

**Population**: 100,000

**Stability**: Very Stable

**Core Values**: Purity, law, order

- The High Camarik Council makes all laws and determines policy. Council seats are technically elected, but in practice controlled by wealthy manufacturing families.
- Camarans are industrious, educated, and deeply suspicious of anything they cannot control—particularly magic that comes from within rather than from the elements.
- Protestant work-ethic culture: idleness is shameful, debt is sin, and success is proof of moral worth. The flip side is a rigid class system where poverty implies moral failing.

### Magic Laws

All varieties of Deoric magic are banned in Camaran. It is seen as corrupting—magic that comes from within the self rather than channeled from external elements is considered spiritually polluting.

- **Hand magic**: If caught practicing, your hand is cut off. Repeat offenders lose the other hand.
- **Elemental magic**: Permitted with a license. Must register at Rathscar or voluntarily quarantine upon arrival by ship until approved.
- **Unlicensed magic**: Enormous fines, or jail time if you cannot pay.

The licensing system is bureaucratic nightmare—forms in triplicate, inspections, annual renewals, restrictions on where and when you can practice. Many mages simply avoid Camaran entirely.

### Economy

**Size**: Very large

**Tech**: Very developed

**Primary Exports**: Manufactured goods, textiles, precision instruments, clockwork

**Primary Imports**: Raw materials, ore, timber, food

- Member of the Aldriktch Trade Alliance, though becoming increasingly isolationist—threatening the alliance's stability.
- Camaran has a highly educated and industrious population. They produce non-magical manufactured goods used across Alaria: tools, furniture, textiles, clockwork mechanisms, weapons.
- Some of the best schools in the world are located here—strict and rigorous, producing skilled craftsmen, engineers, and bureaucrats.
- Vetoed Echea's membership in the Trade Alliance (reasons unclear, likely political).

### Military

**Size**: Medium

**Quality**: Medium

**Enrollment**: Mandatory

- The Camarik military is not particularly powerful, but their population is substantial and they can raise a large army quickly if needed.
- Military service is seen as civic duty—another form of productive labor for the state.

### Geography

**Location**: Northwest of Adron, south of the Kharvorn Mountains, west of the Breidlheiss Basin

**Biomes**: Temperate farmland, rolling hills, river valleys, mountain foothills

**Climate**: Temperate continental—cold winters, warm summers, reliable rainfall

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Rathscar

**Cities**: Rathscar, several manufacturing towns along the rivers

**Towns**: Scattered agricultural and mining settlements

### Primary Conflicts

**The Giant Question**

East of Camaran lies the Breidlheiss Basin, home to giants. The Camarik position is that giants are dangerous, unpredictable, and must be contained. In practice, this means Camaran runs mining operations in the basin's foothills—technically giant territory—extracting ore while insisting the giants have no legitimate claim to land they "aren't civilized enough to develop."

When giants object (sometimes violently), Camaran retaliates with punitive military expeditions. The cycle continues: Camaran encroaches, giants push back, Camaran calls it "unprovoked aggression" and takes more territory as "security buffer."

Some Camarans—particularly those who trade with the Ngül Mountain communities where Kimril and Güli giants coexist peacefully—understand the giants aren't inherently hostile. But acknowledging this would mean admitting Camaran's mining expansion is the problem, which would threaten powerful economic interests.

**Internal Tensions**

- Council members who want to relax or repeal the magic bans, arguing they put Camaran at a competitive disadvantage.
- Massive wealth disparity between manufacturing families and workers. The rhetoric of "moral success" keeps the lower classes blaming themselves rather than the system.
- Growing isolationism straining the Aldriktch Trade Alliance—some council members want to leave entirely.

### History

**The Deoric Ban**

Three centuries ago, Camaran was ruled by a Deoric sorcerer-king named Valdric the Beloved. He was genuinely popular—charismatic, generous, seemingly benevolent. For forty years, he guided Camaran to prosperity.

Then the truth emerged: Valdric had been using psy-magic to manipulate the entire population. Every citizen's loyalty, every feeling of contentment, every memory of his "benevolent" rule—manufactured. When a foreign mage broke the enchantment, Camaran experienced collective psychological trauma on a national scale. People couldn't trust their own memories. Families discovered their relationships had been artificially constructed. The suicide rate spiked for a generation.

The revolution that followed was brutal. Valdric was executed (slowly), and the new republic instituted absolute bans on Deoric magic—any magic that comes from within, that could touch the mind or soul. Elemental magic, which channels external forces, was deemed acceptable because it cannot directly manipulate a person's inner self.

Three hundred years later, the trauma has faded into cultural assumption. Most Camarans don't know *why* Deoric magic is evil—they just know it is. The bureaucratic licensing system has become self-perpetuating, a jobs program for inspectors and a revenue stream from fines.

## Chaal Nazzerox

Tags: state, undead, empire

The undead empire of southern Terrenia, ruled by the lich king Xynoth Azkonor from his rotting capital at Emnatt Nazzerath. Approximately ninety-five percent of the population are undead—shadow-bound corpses with no spirit, no will, and no purpose except what their master commands. The remaining five percent are living collaborators: the cruel, the desperate, and the mad who have chosen service over death.

Chaal Nazzerox was once a prosperous agricultural region, its rivers carrying grain to markets across Terrenia. That ended when Xynoth rose. Now the rivers carry corpses and slave barges, the fields are tended by shambling dead under living overseers, and the cities crumble because no one remembers how to maintain them.

The empire is contained—for now. Sea to the west, mountains to the south, hostile forces to the east, and living nations to the north. Every year, Xynoth probes these barriers. Every year, he comes a little closer to breaking through.

---

### Government

#### The Lich King

**Xynoth Azkonor** rules absolutely. His word is law. His will animates the dead. Without him—or, more precisely, without the fragment of spirit that remains after centuries of death and rebirth—the undead would collapse into purposeless heaps.

Xynoth was human once, a necromancer of considerable power who sought immortality through lichdom. He achieved it, but lichdom is not free. Each time a lich dies and reforms, their spirit fragments—a piece lost, a piece changed. Xynoth has died many times. What remains is barely recognizable as the man he was. Whether he remembers his original motivations is unclear; whether they would matter anymore is doubtful.

The lich king rules from a citadel in Emnatt Nazzerath, emerging rarely but seeing much through the eyes of his dead servants. He does not eat, sleep, or engage in the activities of the living. He plans. He experiments. He waits.

#### The Living Elite

The five percent of living population are not slaves—they are collaborators, elevated above the masses in exchange for service. These are overseers, administrators, specialists whose skills the dead cannot replicate. They manage the living slaves, maintain what infrastructure survives, and compete viciously for the lich king's favor.

The living elite are not organized into formal houses or factions. Alliances form and dissolve based on immediate advantage. Trust is rare; betrayal is expected. The only constant is that everyone serves Xynoth, and everyone fears becoming unnecessary.

Some collaborators are true believers who worship the lich king as a god or see undeath as evolution. Others are pragmatists doing whatever survival requires. A few are biding their time, hoping for an opportunity that may never come. All of them are damned in the eyes of the living world outside.

#### The Undead Mass

Ninety-five percent of Chaal Nazzerox's population are animated corpses—shadows bound to dead flesh, with no spirit to provide consciousness or will. They are tools, not people. They follow commands with literal precision, lack initiative or creativity, and "mill aimlessly when not directed."

The undead hierarchy reflects this. Most are simple laborers or soldiers: shambling corpses capable of basic tasks and basic violence. Above them are the preserved—corpses maintained in better condition, capable of more complex work. At the top are the intelligent undead: revenants who retained their spirits, liches who followed Xynoth's path, and stranger things that serve for reasons of their own.

All undead ultimately answer to Xynoth. Without his will binding them, they would collapse. This makes him both the empire's greatest strength and its critical vulnerability.

---

### Settlements

#### Emnatt Nazzerath

The capital city, seat of the lich king. Once the grandest city in southern Terrenia; now a rotting monument to death's triumph over life.

The streets are choked with shambling dead—soldiers between assignments, laborers awaiting tasks, corpses that simply stopped and never moved again. The buildings decay because no one repairs them; roofs collapse, walls crumble, infrastructure fails. The living elite maintain their own compounds through constant effort, islands of functionality in a sea of rot.

At the city's heart rises Xynoth's citadel, a tower of black stone that predates the empire. Some say he built it; others claim he found it and made it his. The citadel never decays. It never changes. It watches.

The living population clusters in the merchant quarter, where food and goods still change hands. Slaves are bought and sold here. So are services, information, and favors. Everyone is for sale in Emnatt Nazzerath—including the buyers.

#### Gorvul Mkayin

A city on the southern shore of Deadman's Lake, built to control the one body of water where corpses stay dead. The empire disapproves of wasted resources, and every body dropped into Deadman's Lake is a soldier denied.

Gorvul Mkayin processes arrivals from the northern territories—slaves, tribute, captured refugees. The living elite here are particularly brutal; they earned their positions through demonstrated cruelty. The city also serves as a staging ground for campaigns against the holdouts, its position allowing rapid deployment in multiple directions.

The lake's strange property—preventing undead animation—has made Gorvul Mkayin a center for covert disposal. Living residents sometimes pay enormous bribes to have their dead relatives dropped into the lake rather than conscripted. The authorities take the bribes and make no promises.

#### Sklevyurn

A northern city serving as the empire's primary military staging area. Armies mass here before marching south against the holdouts or probing the northern borders. Smithies work slave labor to arm the dead—not that undead need much equipment, but Xynoth believes in overwhelming force.

Sklevyurn is grim, functional, and joyless. Even by the standards of Chaal Nazzerox, the atmosphere oppresses. The living here exist to serve military logistics; there is no pretense of normal life. Rations are distributed, quotas are met, and the war machine grinds forward.

#### Parthemylos

An eastern city that serves as the empire's administrative hub—taxes, census, supply allocation, the bureaucratic machinery that keeps even an undead empire functioning. The living elite here are clerks and accountants, tracking resources that the dead cannot count themselves.

Parthemylos maintains the empire's records, such as they are. Population counts (living and dead), tribute schedules, military deployments, slave inventories. The archives are a mess—the dead make poor record-keepers, and the living have more pressing concerns than organization—but they exist, and occasionally prove useful.

#### Pyaal Faras

A southwestern city near Hagswood, maintaining an uncomfortable proximity to the hag coven. Pyaal Faras serves as the point of contact between the empire and the hags—whatever arrangement exists between them, it's administered here.

The city has an undeserved reputation for commerce. Goods flow through Pyaal Faras that aren't available elsewhere in the empire: hag-brewed potions, items from the Strait of Curses, things better not examined closely. The living elite here are traders and intermediaries, people comfortable dealing with monsters.

#### Eyovlix

A southeastern town on the Melkron River, serving as the empire's forward base for campaigns against the Crystal Mountains. Undead armies stage here before their endless, grinding assaults on the mountain passes.

Eyovlix is less a settlement than a military camp that never disbanded. The living population exists to support operations—healers for the wounded (living soldiers do fight alongside the dead), quartermasters, engineers attempting to solve the problem of moving shambling armies through mountain terrain. Progress is slow.

---

### The Holdouts

Two significant settlements within the empire's claimed territory have never fallen: the Gray Citadel and Melthrayn. Both are under constant pressure but have held for years. Their continued existence is an embarrassment to Xynoth and a symbol of hope for those who resist.

#### Gray Citadel

A fortress in the Steed Hills, originally built to guard against threats from the south. When Xynoth rose, the citadel's garrison refused to surrender. They've been refusing ever since.

The Gray Citadel's survival owes to terrain, construction, and desperation. The Steed Hills are difficult for shambling armies to traverse. The fortress walls were built thick and have been reinforced with everything available. The defenders know that surrender means death or worse—they fight because there is no alternative.

The citadel is overcrowded with refugees, undersupplied by occasional smuggler convoys, and perpetually on the edge of starvation. Commanders debate whether to hold or attempt a breakout. Neither option offers good odds. They hold because holding is all they can do.

#### Melthrayn

A walled city-state in the eastern reaches that has somehow resisted incorporation into the empire. Unlike the Gray Citadel, Melthrayn is not just a fortress—it's a functioning city with farms within its walls, industries, a civilian population living something approaching normal lives.

How Melthrayn has survived is unclear. Theories include powerful wards, alliance with unknown powers, leverage over Xynoth himself, or simply that the lich king hasn't committed the resources to take it. The city's rulers don't explain, and visitors (what few there are) report a population that doesn't discuss the matter.

Refugees who reach Melthrayn rarely leave. Whether this is because they've found safety or because they're not permitted to leave is another question without answers.

---

### Military

The empire's military strength is simple: numbers without limit and soldiers that never tire, never flee, and never stop. An undead army is not particularly skilled or adaptive, but it doesn't need to be. It just keeps coming.

**Shambling hordes**: The bulk of the army. Animated corpses capable of basic weapon use and basic tactics—advance, attack, repeat. They're slow, clumsy, and easily confused by complex terrain. But there are so many.

**Preserved soldiers**: Better-maintained corpses, faster and more durable. These form elite units for specialized tasks.

**Siege forces**: The undead are natural siege troops. They don't need food, don't need rest, and don't care about casualties. They simply assault until the walls fall or they're destroyed.

**Living auxiliaries**: Some living soldiers serve the empire voluntarily—mercenaries, fanatics, those who've chosen the winning side. They provide tactical flexibility the dead lack.

**Command structure**: Intelligent undead and living commanders direct the mindless masses. Without direction, undead armies stall. Kill the commanders, and the assault fragments.

---

### Economy

Chaal Nazzerox produces almost nothing. The empire survives through:

**Slave agriculture**: Living slaves work fields to feed the living population. The undead don't eat, but their masters do.

**Plunder**: What the empire can't produce, it takes. Neighboring regions have been stripped; now the pickings are thin.

**Tribute**: Conquered populations pay in food, goods, and bodies. The Brevldorf Hills communities survive through this arrangement.

**Hag trade**: Whatever the Hagswood coven provides, it has value. Pyaal Faras facilitates exchange.

The economy is unsustainable. Without expansion, the empire will eventually consume itself. This is why Xynoth probes the borders constantly—he needs new resources, new slaves, new corpses.

---

### Travel

Nearly all travel is by river. The ground is soft—waterlogged, unstable, unsuitable for roads. The rivers are Chaal Nazzerox's highways, and whoever controls them controls movement.

The undead can wade through soft ground, but slowly. Living travelers without boat access are effectively immobile. This has shaped the empire's geography, concentrating power along riverbanks and leaving the interior accessible only to those willing to struggle.

Outsiders attempting to enter or leave Chaal Nazzerox face significant challenges. The rivers are patrolled. The overland routes are watched. The borders are guarded by things that don't sleep. Refugees still escape—through the Frowning Forest, down the Yephrenzi River, over the Prowling Hills—but the price is high.

---

### Relations

**Aal Salma**: The merchant nation to the northwest watches the empire with alarm. Refugees cross their border constantly. War seems inevitable, but neither side has struck.

**Windor**: The halfling nation further north has sealed its borders. No trade, no contact, no acknowledgment that the undead exist. This is official policy; unofficially, halfling smugglers make fortunes running goods to holdout forces.

**Poum Titch**: Currently tearing itself apart in civil war, which has distracted Xynoth from northern expansion. The lich king may be waiting for the war to end—whoever wins will be weakened.

**The Crystal Mountains**: Whatever lies beyond is defended. The mountain peoples have held the passes for years. Xynoth's armies assault and die and assault again.

**The Hagswood Coven**: An arrangement of unclear terms. The hags and the lich tolerate each other. No one knows why.

---

### What Makes It Dangerous

- **The dead keep coming**: Every defender who falls becomes an enemy. Attrition favors the empire absolutely.
- **Xynoth sees through his servants**: Surveillance is everywhere. The dead report to their master.
- **No conventional victory**: Kill every soldier, and Xynoth raises more. Destroy every city, and the empire operates from ruins. Only destroying Xynoth himself—and his phylacteries, wherever they are—ends the threat.
- **Containment is failing**: The barriers that hold the empire are weakening. The Crystal Mountain defenders lose ground each year. The northern states are distracted by their own problems.
- **The lich is patient**: Xynoth has been planning for centuries. Whatever he's waiting for, it's coming.

## Chechol

Tags: state

A landlocked state in Central Aboyinzu, wedged between the Deadloop inner sea to the north and the Dalizi Confederation to the south. Chechol is defined by its three river valleys, its significant Rentar minotaur population, and two sites of immense spiritual power: the Pyramid of Five Sides and the School of Summoning.

From a distance, Chechol appears unremarkable—a modest agricultural state, quieter than its neighbors, known for exporting grain and pious mercenaries. Visitors who stay longer notice something harder to name. The Rentar here move with unusual certainty. Decisions are made quickly, without debate, as if everyone already knows the answer. The human population has grown quieter over the past generation, deferential in ways that feel learned rather than natural.

Something is deeply wrong in Chechol. Most of its residents don't know it yet.

### Government

**The River Duchy**

Chechol is officially ruled by **Duke Yelen Vorotny** from the capital of Sevich, the fourth duke of the Vorotny line. The duchy predates the Rentar arrival by centuries, and the ducal institution remains formally supreme—the Duke commands the army, levies taxes, and represents Chechol to foreign powers.

In practice, Duke Yelen makes no significant decision without consulting the **Council of Elders**, a body of senior Rentar spiritual leaders. This has been true for three generations. The Vorotny dukes consider it wisdom—why wouldn't you seek divine guidance when it's available? The Rentar consider it proper—they are vessels of celestial truth, and secular rulers should acknowledge that.

The problem is that the Council's guidance has been subtly corrupted for decades. The Elders don't know this. Duke Yelen doesn't know this. The decisions they make feel right, feel divinely inspired, but they've been steering Chechol toward an end none of them would choose.

**The Three River Councils**

Below the duchy, each river valley maintains its own local council:
- **Chechik Council** (Sevich, Astopol, Pyadrov) — the political heart
- **Stulov Council** (Stulovka, Yeletity) — agricultural backbone
- **Riki Council** (Prozny and surrounding settlements) — closest to the School of Summoning

These councils handle local governance and traditionally sent representatives to the Duke. Now they increasingly defer to whichever Rentar monastery is nearest.

### Culture

**Two Peoples, One Faith (They Think)**

Chechol's population is roughly 60% human, 40% Rentar minotaur, but cultural influence doesn't track with numbers. Humans farm the river valleys and staff the towns. Rentar occupy the highlands between rivers, maintaining monasteries and temples. Over generations, the relationship has shifted from coexistence to hierarchy—humans defer to Rentar on matters of spirit, morality, and increasingly, politics.

This isn't resented, exactly. Most humans in Chechol grew up with Rentar neighbors and genuinely believe in their spiritual insight. The Rentar aren't cruel or exploitative. They simply... know things. They receive guidance. They share that guidance generously.

What the humans have begun to notice—without quite articulating it—is that the Rentar have changed.
