- This arrangement has persisted for over a thousand years—long enough that no one alive remembers it being any other way, but not long enough to resolve the fundamental tension between Rhea idealism and human practicality.
- The Rhea are air-elemental beings: small, unnaturally light, with grayish-blue skin and floating wispy hair. They value focus above all—choosing a single pursuit and mastering it over decades. Their monasteries produce legendary scholars, healers, and martial artists.
- The humans of Vastilin are merchants, craftsmen, and laborers. They value practical results—food on the table, coin in the pocket, goods moving to market. They find Rhea contemplation baffling but respect Rhea skills.

### Economy

**Size**: Small-Medium

**Tech**: Mixed (Rhea scholarship + human craftsmanship)

**Primary Exports**: Education, healing services, scholarly texts, mountain herbs, refined metals

**Primary Imports**: Food (grain, vegetables), cloth, luxury goods, raw materials

- Eynmore's monasteries are famous across Tarkhon. Wealthy families send children to study there. The sick travel miles for Rhea healers. Scholars seek the ancient texts in Rhea archives. This brings money and prestige.
- Vastilin's merchants handle the practical side—buying, selling, transporting, storing. They manage Murth's trade relationships, provision the monasteries, and ensure the state doesn't starve.
- Mt. Arn produces iron and copper; Mt. Disyus produces rare alpine herbs and materials for magical work. Each mountain has what the other lacks.

### Military

**Size**: Small

**Quality**: Specialized

**Enrollment**: Professional (Vastilin guard) + Monastery defenders (Rhea martial monks)

- Murth has no large army. It relies on difficult terrain and Tarkhon's broader protection for security.
- Vastilin maintains a small professional guard (~500) for law enforcement and caravan protection.
- The Rhea monasteries train martial monks—not many, but those who dedicate decades to combat become extraordinarily dangerous. A single Rhea master can defeat a squad of ordinary soldiers.

### Geography

**Location**: Western Tarkhon, in the mountains west of Vogenfeld and northwest of the Kingdoms of Fire

**Biomes**: Alpine mountains, high valleys, thin air at elevation

**Climate**: Cold, dry, with harsh winters at altitude

**Named Features**: Mt. Disyus (north), Mt. Arn (south), the Murthian Tunnels, Lake Stillwater (underground)

### Political Geography

**Dual Capitals**: Eynmore (Mt. Disyus) and Vastilin (Mt. Arn)

**Other Settlements**: Small mining camps, traveler's rest stations, scattered farms in the valleys

### Mt. Disyus and Eynmore

The northern mountain rises high enough that only Rhea find the air comfortable. Human visitors struggle to breathe, to think, to move. This natural barrier keeps Eynmore isolated—and the Rhea prefer it that way.

**Eynmore** is built into the mountain itself: monastery complexes carved from stone, meditation halls open to the sky, libraries that have collected knowledge for a thousand years. The architecture is elegant but austere—beauty in simplicity, function elevated to art.

Perhaps 8,000 Rhea live here, along with a handful of human servants and students hardy enough to adapt to the altitude. The population hasn't changed much in centuries. The Rhea don't need growth. They need focus.

The **High Contemplative** leads Eynmore—currently a Rhea named **Whisper-of-Still-Waters**, who has held the position for forty-seven years. She speaks rarely, thinks deeply, and has forgotten more about philosophy than most scholars ever learn.

### Mt. Arn and Vastilin

The southern mountain is lower, warmer, and richer in minerals. Humans settled here long before establishing contact with the Rhea—miners and traders who found the mountain's resources worth the isolation.

**Vastilin** sprawls across the mountain's southern slopes: a proper city with markets, warehouses, foundries, taverns, and all the mess that humans create. Perhaps 12,000 people live here, mostly human but with representatives of every race who find mountain commerce appealing.

The city is governed by the **Merchant Council**—seven wealthy families who control Vastilin's major industries. The current **First Merchant** is **Aldous Brennan**, a third-generation trader who inherited his position and has proven surprisingly competent.

### Lake Stillwater

Deep beneath both mountains lies **Lake Stillwater**—an underground lake fed by glacial melt, its waters unnaturally calm and clear. The lake is the key to Murth's existence.

A thousand years ago, Rhea from what would become Eynmore began carving tunnels down into Mt. Disyus, seeking water. They found Lake Stillwater—and discovered that humans had carved tunnels from the other direction for the same reason.

Rather than fight over the lake, they negotiated. The **Stillwater Compact** established shared access: both peoples could draw water, neither could pollute or restrict the source. To enforce this, they carved connecting tunnels.

Those tunnels changed everything. Suddenly two isolated mountain communities could trade, communicate, cooperate. Over centuries, this practical arrangement evolved into political union. Not because either side wanted unity—but because cutting off the tunnels meant cutting off the water.

### The Murthian Tunnels

Miles of passages connect Eynmore and Vastilin through the mountains' hearts, with Lake Stillwater at the center. The tunnels are:

- **Transportation**: The fastest route between the cities, passable even when surface passes are blocked by snow
- **Trade routes**: Goods flow through constantly—food going up to Eynmore, finished products coming down to Vastilin
- **Neutral ground**: The tunnels belong to neither city, governed by separate tunnel-wardens from both communities
- **Emergency refuge**: If either city were threatened, the population could evacuate through the tunnels

The tunnels also contain shrines, way stations, and the great **Chamber of the Compact** where the original agreement is carved into the living rock.

### The Dual Government

Major decisions affecting all of Murth require agreement between Eynmore and Vastilin. This means:

- The High Contemplative and the First Merchant must both approve
- Disputes go to the **Council of Two Mountains**—representatives from both cities meeting in the tunnel system
- Deadlocks can persist for years (the Rhea are patient; the humans are stubborn)

In practice, most matters are handled locally. Eynmore governs Eynmore; Vastilin governs Vastilin. Only questions of trade policy, foreign relations, and shared resources require joint decision.

This works... mostly. The cultural divide creates constant friction:

- Rhea think humans are impatient, shallow, and obsessed with money
- Humans think Rhea are slow, impractical, and disconnected from reality
- Both are right. Both need each other too much to split.

### The Cultural Divide

**What Rhea value:**
- Focus: Choose one thing and master it completely
- Patience: Decades of study before speaking with authority
- Contemplation: Understanding matters more than acting
- Simplicity: Possessions are distractions

**What Vastilin humans value:**
- Results: Does it work? Does it sell?
- Efficiency: Get it done, move on to the next thing
- Growth: More trade, more wealth, more influence
- Comfort: Life should be enjoyed, not merely endured

These values clash constantly. A Rhea teacher might spend thirty years training a single student. A Vastilin merchant might make thirty deals in a month. Neither understands why the other works that way.

And yet: Vastilin's merchants sell Eynmore's teaching. Eynmore's scholars heal Vastilin's sick. The arrangement works not despite the differences but because of them. Each provides what the other cannot.

### Primary Conflicts

**The Trade Imbalance**

Vastilin handles all of Murth's external trade—and takes a cut of everything. Eynmore produces valuable services (education, healing) but Vastilin controls how those services reach the market.

Some Rhea argue this is exploitation. Some humans argue they're just being practical. The tension simmers without resolution.

**The Altitude Question**

Vastilin's population is growing; Eynmore's isn't. More humans means more pressure on shared resources—especially water from Lake Stillwater. Some in Eynmore worry that eventually Vastilin will simply outnumber them into irrelevance.

**The Plains of Oblivion**

Northwest of Murth lie the **Plains of Oblivion**—cursed grasslands that erase memories. The plains creep closer some years, retreat others. No one knows why.

Queen Eranes rules from her palace **Satyrn Gray** somewhere in those plains—a half-titan who enchanted herself to forget a lost love. She's immensely powerful and unpredictable. Murth tries not to attract her attention.

**The Tarkhon Question**

Murth is technically part of Tarkhon, paying tribute to Tarkhetan. But it's far from the strait, produces no strategic resources, and mostly gets left alone.

Some in Vastilin want closer ties to Tarkhon—more trade, more protection, more integration. Some in Eynmore want further distance—less interference, less entanglement, less of everything. The debate continues.

### Notable Figures

**Whisper-of-Still-Waters** (High Contemplative of Eynmore)
An ancient Rhea who has led Eynmore for forty-seven years. She speaks perhaps a dozen words a day, each chosen with care. Her silences communicate more than most people's speeches.

**Aldous Brennan** (First Merchant of Vastilin)
Forty-three years old, inherited his position, but has earned respect through competent administration. He genuinely wants what's best for Murth—he just defines "best" in commercial terms.

**Master Stonefist** (Martial monk of Eynmore)
A Rhea who has spent sixty years mastering unarmed combat. He's old, small, light as a feather—and could kill any ten soldiers who challenged him. He trains the monastery's defenders and occasionally takes students from outside.

**Sera Coldwell** (Tunnel-Warden)
A human woman who oversees the central tunnel network. Nominally neutral, practically essential. She knows every passage, every shortcut, every secret. Both cities trust her—which means neither fully trusts her.

### History

**The Founding (~1000+ years ago)**: Rhea settle Mt. Disyus; humans settle Mt. Arn. Both communities dig for water. Both find Lake Stillwater.

**The Stillwater Compact**: Rather than fight, the communities negotiate shared access. Connecting tunnels are carved.

**The Slow Integration**: Over centuries, trade and cooperation create interdependence. Political union follows economic reality.

**The Tarkhon Era**: Murth becomes part of the growing Tarkhon Empire, trading autonomy for access to broader markets and nominal protection.

**The Present**: Murth continues its strange dual existence—two peoples, two cultures, two mountains, one state. The arrangement works. Mostly.

## Myastor

Tags: state

Very poor. Once shared governance among the three Ofrenian kingdoms; post-fragmentation, it was granted to the Queen of Sylke. Alisandra sees it as a dump and uses it for political prisoners and unofficial exile.

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Colonial administration (under Sylke)

**Primary Inhabitants**: Humans

**Population**: 10,000

**Stability**: Unstable

**Core Values**: Survival, keeping one's head down, minding one's business

- Myastor is ruled by a governor appointed by Queen Alisandra—always someone she wants out of her sight but not quite dead.
- The population is a mix of longtime residents, transported criminals, political exiles, and people who ended up here by accident and never left.
- No one chooses to live in Myastor. You're born here, sent here, or stranded here. Leaving requires money, connections, or both.
- The locals have developed a grim solidarity. Everyone has a past they don't discuss. Questions about how someone arrived are deeply rude.

### Economy

**Size**: Small

**Tech**: Somewhat Developed

**Primary Exports**: Lumber, transshipment services

**Primary Imports**: Prisoners, everything else

- Myastor's economy is almost entirely based on its position. Ships stopping on the way to Sylke need provisions, repairs, and places to offload inconvenient cargo. The island provides all three.
- Lots of money flows through Myastor; almost none of it stays. Merchants arrive, conduct business, and leave. The locals see wealth pass by but can't capture it.
- Lumber from the interior provides some legitimate export, but the forests are thinning and no one invests in replanting.
- The prison economy is grimly important. Feeding, housing, and guarding prisoners employs a significant fraction of the population. When prisoner shipments slow, the whole island feels it.

### Military

**Size**: Very Small

**Quality**: Low

**Enrollment**: Voluntary (desperate)

- The garrison exists to guard prisoners and discourage pirates. It's understaffed, poorly equipped, and stationed here as punishment.
- Sylke's navy calls at Shipton regularly, which provides actual security. The local garrison is largely for show.
- Prison guards are technically military but function more like jailers. The distinction matters to no one except payroll clerks.

### Geography

**Location**: Paluva Amati island, in the Ofrenia Passage east of Ofrenia proper

**Biomes**: Scrubland, thinning forests, rocky coasts

**Named Entities**: Paluva Amati (island name)

**Rivers & Lakes**: Small streams, no significant bodies of water

**Adjacent Waters**: The Ofrenia Passage, the Middle Sea

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Shipton

**Cities**: None

**Towns**: Shipton, Telara, Partsmouth, Pasterton

**Villages**: Scattered fishing and lumber camps

### Primary Conflicts

**The Exile Economy**

Myastor's prosperity—such as it is—depends on Alisandra continuing to send prisoners and exiles. If she conquers Joswik and runs out of political enemies, the island's economy collapses. The governor privately hopes the war drags on forever.

**The Prison Population**

The prisoners outnumber the guards, and everyone knows it. The system works because escape from the island is nearly impossible and because the prisoners include many who've simply given up. But as conditions deteriorate and new arrivals bring fresh grievances, the balance grows more precarious.

**The Sylke Relationship**

Myastor exists at Alisandra's sufferance. The queen sees it as a dumping ground, not a priority. Requests for resources, personnel, or attention go unanswered. The governor has learned to manage without support—but in a crisis, no help is coming.

**The Passing Trade**

Merchants who stop in Shipton could bring prosperity if they stayed. They don't. The locals resent being treated as a waystation, but lack leverage to change anything. Some have begun exploring ways to make Myastor more attractive—or more necessary—to passing ships.

### History

Paluva Amati was settled generations ago as a waystation for ships crossing the Passage. The three Ofrenian kingdoms shared governance, using the island as neutral ground for negotiations and as a convenient place to warehouse people they'd rather forget.

When the old king died and his children divided Ofrenia, no one wanted Myastor. Tornia had enough ports. Joswik had no navy to speak of. Sylke needed a place to send problems. Alisandra claimed it by default, and her siblings were happy to let her.

Under Alisandra's rule, Myastor has become a dumping ground. Political prisoners fill the old warehouses-turned-prisons. Nobles who annoyed the queen find themselves "governing" the island until they die of boredom or despair. The locals have adapted, building an economy around human misery.

The conquest of Tornia has actually benefited Myastor slightly—refugee ships stop here, desperate for supplies and willing to pay premium prices. But the governor knows this prosperity is temporary. Once Alisandra consolidates her gains, the refugee flow will stop, and Myastor will return to its role as a place the world forgets.

## Myorna

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Monarchy (compromised)

**Primary Inhabitants**: Sivakr (Silver Elves)

**Population**: 60,000

**Stability**: Very Unstable

**Core Values**: Mental superiority, memory, influence, secrecy

- Sivakr are gray-skinned elves who spent thousands of years underground. Physical exercise is considered vulgar—status comes entirely from mental acuity and influence.
- Mind manipulation on each other is strictly forbidden, but totally permitted on outsiders, who are viewed as beneath them.
- King Thyolinor nominally rules, but he is being mind-controlled by a breakaway faction within Myorna. The terrorist attacks on neighboring states are state-sanctioned but officially denied.

### Culture

**Memory Manipulation**

The Sivakr can alter memories—a terrifying ability that defines their society. Memory duels settle disputes between equals: both parties interlock fingers and attempt to convince the other they made a mistake in accepting the challenge. Must have a witness.

**Memory Libraries**

Influential households maintain memory libraries—expensive repositories containing preserved memories of historical figures, important events, and cultural traditions. These are status symbols and sources of power.

**Memory Art**

Freeze-frames of memories, rendered visible. The best artists have extraordinary recall. Memory art galleries are prestigious cultural institutions.

**Paper Control**

Paper is highly cherished and was historically used to control the population—records, contracts, debts. The poor, lacking access to paper, couldn't be tracked or controlled as effectively. Now some are using this gap to free themselves from the system.

### Economy

**Size**: Medium

**Tech**: Somewhat Developed

**Primary Exports**: Memory art, Deoric knowledge (secretly), silver, mountain goods

**Primary Imports**: Food, surface goods, paper

- Members of the Aldriktch Trade Alliance, though this membership is increasingly strained as neighbors discover the truth about Sivakr abilities.

### Military

**Size**: Small

**Quality**: High (terrifying)

**Enrollment**: Voluntary

- The Myornan military is small but potentially devastating. Sivakr soldiers can manipulate enemy memories mid-battle—making soldiers forget their training, forget which side they're on, forget they were ever in danger.
- Most Sivakr consider physical combat vulgar, so the military is composed of those willing to dirty themselves for the state.

### Geography

**Location**: Southern slopes of the Kharvorn Mountains, specifically the Grey Mountains sub-range. Borders Camaran (southeast), Erasnus (southwest), barely touches Hephake (northwest).

**Biomes**: Mountain peaks, deep valleys, underground complexes

**Climate**: Alpine—cold, harsh winters, brief summers

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Vad Ilghak

**Cities**: Vad Ilghak, Urkhuk

**Towns**: Scattered mountain settlements, many with entrances to the underground warrens

### The Forbidden Valley

North of Vad Ilghak lies the Forbidden Valley—a massive, impossibly deep chasm in the mountains. At its bottom, the Sivakr keep a **chained giant**, from whom they extract consistent blood sacrifices. This blood powers all Sivakr mind magic.

A massive statue of **Tiira**, their patron goddess, overlooks the valley. The Sivakr cultivated Tiira as a savior figure for their people—but the truth is darker. They effectively brainwashed their own goddess into serving Myornan interests. Even their god is a victim of their manipulation.

### The Deoric Library

Vad Ilghak houses a massive library of **Deoric spellbooks**—texts of secret, sacrifice-based magic. This knowledge is closely guarded but represents one of the largest collections of Deoric lore in existence. Outsiders who learn of it would be horrified.

### Primary Conflicts

**The Breakaway Faction**

A faction within Myorna has seized control of King Thyolinor through mind manipulation. They are directing terrorist attacks against neighboring states while the king officially denies involvement. The faction's goals are unclear—perhaps they want war, perhaps they want Myorna driven back underground, perhaps something worse.

**Neighbor Relations**

Discoveries about Sivakr memory manipulation have made every neighbor hostile. The Trade Alliance members tolerated Myorna for access to silver and mountain goods, but the terrorist attacks are pushing them toward breaking ties entirely. Erasnus is trying to hold things together; everyone else wants Myorna out.

**Internal Division**

Many Sivakr want to return underground. The surface has brought nothing but conflict and exposure. Others—particularly those near the Erasnun border—have begun assimilating into surface culture and want to stay. The kingdom is splitting.

**The Stone Slums**

The poor of Myorna, concentrated in the Stone Slums (foggy, flat, slate-built districts), are increasingly ungovernable. Without paper records, they slip through the system. This is where golems were first discovered and built—desperate people finding desperate solutions.

### History

Thousands of years ago, the Sivakr were driven underground by other elves. In the darkness, they developed their memory manipulation abilities and cultivated Tiira as their goddess—though "cultivated" may mean something more sinister than worship.

Fifty years ago, King Thyolinor decided to bring his people to the surface and engage with the wider world. They joined the Aldriktch Trade Alliance. Relations were tenuous from the start—outsiders found the Sivakr unsettling even before they understood why.

Now the truth is emerging. The terrorist attacks have been traced back to Myorna. Neighbors are learning what memory manipulation really means. The Alliance is fracturing. And somewhere in the Forbidden Valley, a giant bleeds to fuel it all.

## Nashua

Tags: state, lizardfolk, innerrim

The poison country. Nashua survives not through expansion or conquest but through being too costly to take. For generations, the Ix'Vasyla have held this toxic marshland against enemies on two fronts, turning their hostile environment into a weapon and their venomous nature into military doctrine. Every invading army learns the same lesson: Nashua can be entered, but not held. The marshes take what the legions cannot.

Where Gorath represents aggressive expansion and imperial ambition, Nashua represents something older and grimmer: survival at any cost, victory through attrition, and the patient certainty that enemies who enter the marshes will not leave.

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Clan confederation with war council

**Primary Inhabitants**: Ix'Vasyla (dominant), Sylthik (minority), Humans (integrated)

**Population**: ~150,000

**Stability**: Stable (internally); perpetual war (externally)

**Core Values**: Patience, cunning, clan loyalty, territorial defense, pragmatic ruthlessness

#### The Council of Fang and Scale

Nashua is not ruled by a single leader. The Ix'Vasyla organize into clans, each controlling territory within the marshes, and those clans send representatives to the **Council of Fang and Scale** in Tirexonos. The Council coordinates the endless war effort, mediates inter-clan disputes, and handles what passes for foreign policy.

Council seats are earned through demonstrated tactical success. A clan leader who wins battles efficiently—maximum enemy casualties, minimum Ix'Vasyla losses—gains voice and influence. One who wastes warriors on failed offensives loses standing, sometimes permanently. This creates a government optimized for defensive warfare: cautious, patient, and relentlessly focused on cost-benefit analysis.

The Council has no single head. Decisions require consensus among the major clans, which can make the government slow to act on anything not directly war-related. But when war is the constant state of existence, this limitation matters less than it might seem.

#### The Hunt-Masters

Below the Council, military operations are coordinated by **Hunt-Masters**—veteran warriors who have proven themselves across multiple campaigns. Hunt-Masters command no standing forces; instead, they recruit from clan warriors for specific operations, return those warriors when the operation concludes, and then plan the next strike.

This distributed command structure makes Nashua's military difficult to decapitate. Kill a Hunt-Master, and another rises. Destroy a war-band, and the clans simply form another. There is no general whose death ends the war, no army whose defeat opens the country.

#### Clan Society

Everything in Ix'Vasyla life flows through the clan. Birth, training, mating, territory, honor—all are clan matters first, individual matters second. Clan territories are inviolable except in war emergency; clan disputes are resolved through ritualized contests that rarely result in death (warriors are too valuable to waste on internal conflict).

The major clans each hold territory in the central marshes and maintain family compounds in Tirexonos. Lesser clans hold smaller territories or serve in subordinate roles to greater ones. Clanless Ix'Vasyla exist—exiles, criminals, the rare survivors of destroyed clans—but they occupy the margins of society, taking work no clan warrior would accept.

### Economy

**Size**: Small

**Tech**: Developed (specialized)

**Primary Exports**: Alchemical ingredients, exotic venoms, marsh-harvested reagents

**Primary Imports**: Metal goods, textiles, preserved foods

#### The Poison Trade

Nashua's economy runs on toxins. The marshes produce an extraordinary variety of venomous creatures, poisonous plants, and alchemically useful compounds found nowhere else on Alaria. Properly harvested and processed, these resources command premium prices from alchemists, assassins, and researchers across the continent.

The **Arcane Consortium of Nashua** handles much of this trade, serving as intermediary between the clans who harvest the resources and the foreign buyers who want them. The Consortium takes a percentage; the clans get access to markets they couldn't reach alone.

#### Subsistence and Survival

Beyond the poison trade, Nashua's economy is primarily subsistence-based. The marshes provide fish, waterfowl, and edible plants for those who know how to find them. The river corridor supports limited agriculture, worked primarily by the human population. Metal is scarce and must be imported or scavenged from dead enemies.

This economic limitation shapes Nashuan military doctrine. They cannot afford prolonged campaigns that consume resources faster than they're replaced. Every arrow, every blade, every warrior represents an investment that must pay off. Gorathi-style attritional warfare would bankrupt Nashua in a generation—so they make sure Gorath pays the attrition instead.

### Military

**Size**: Medium

**Quality**: Very High

**Enrollment**: Universal (all Ix'Vasyla train for war)

#### Doctrine of Patient Death

Nashuan military doctrine is simple: never fight fair, never fight directly, never fight when you can poison instead.

Every engagement begins with preparation—scouts mapping enemy positions, warriors pre-positioning along ambush routes, poison applied to water sources and food supplies. When the enemy moves, they move into kill zones. When they camp, they camp in poisoned ground. When they retreat, they're hunted.

The Ix'Vasyla's venomous bite is central to this doctrine. A warrior who delivers a single bite and escapes has effectively killed that enemy—the venom will do the rest over the following days. Wounded enemies become liabilities for their comrades, consuming resources and spreading demoralization as they die screaming.

#### Clan War-Bands

Nashua maintains no standing army. Instead, each clan provides warriors when the Council calls, organized into **war-bands** under Hunt-Master command. A typical war-band numbers fifty to two hundred warriors, assembled for a specific campaign and disbanded afterward.

This flexibility has advantages: war-bands can be tailored to specific missions, warriors retain clan bonds and local knowledge, and there's no expensive permanent military to maintain. The disadvantage is coordination—large-scale operations require negotiations between multiple clans, each jealous of their warriors' lives and honor.

#### The River Fleet

Nashua's small navy—really more a collection of armed boats—patrols the Jiji and its tributaries, protects coastal waters, and raids enemy shipping when opportunity presents. The vessels are shallow-draft, easily hidden, and crewed by warriors who can fight equally well on deck or underwater.

The fleet's primary role is defensive: preventing enemies from using the rivers as invasion routes. But it occasionally conducts offensive operations, striking Gorathi coastal positions or intercepting supply ships in the waters south of the Deserted Hills.

### Geography

**Location**: Eastern Inner Rim

**Biomes**: Toxic marshland (dominant), river valleys, coastal scrubland

**Named Regions**: The Toxic Marshes, The River Corridor, The Southern Scrublands

**Rivers**: Jiji River, Torin Creek

**Adjacent Waters**: Eastern coastal seas

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Tirexonos

**Major Towns**: Vosx, Hyobinii, Sipokno, Dolno Jelovce, Nikolici, Poyux

**Lesser Settlements**: Kisava, Lukshax, Sviniste

### Relations

**Gorath**: Active war, decades-long stalemate. The Deserted Hills mark the contested border. Nashua views Gorath as an existential threat; Gorath views Nashua as an inconvenient obstacle to expansion. Neither can defeat the other; neither will make peace.

**Trømgar**: Active war, ritualized conflict. The dwarves raid highland approaches; the Ix'Vasyla raid mountain settlements. Neither side can invade the other's core territory. The conflict has become almost traditional—both sides seem to fight because they always have, not because victory is possible.

**Kyagos**: Complicated. The Sylthik homeland lies to the southeast, and Nashua's Sylthik minority maintains ties there. The relationship is neither alliance nor enmity—a wary coexistence between peoples who share scaled nature but little else.

**Everyone Else**: Nashua has few friends and many enemies. Their reputation as poisoners, ambushers, and merciless hunters makes them poor diplomatic partners. Trade happens through intermediaries; alliances don't happen at all.

### Primary Conflicts

- **The Gorath War**: The primary existential threat. Gorath's resources dwarf Nashua's; only the terrain and Ix'Vasyla defensive doctrine have prevented conquest. If Gorath ever commits its full strength—unlikely given their other fronts—Nashua might fall.

- **The Trømgar Raids**: A constant drain on northern settlements, but manageable. The dwarves cannot take the marshes; the Ix'Vasyla cannot take the mountains. An eternal standoff.

- **Internal Clan Tensions**: The major clans compete for influence on the Council. These competitions are usually ritualized and non-lethal, but resentments simmer. A major military defeat could shatter the clan consensus that holds Nashua together.

### History

The Ix'Vasyla have inhabited the toxic marshlands since before recorded history. When human settlers arrived along the rivers—the ancestors of today's integrated population—the lizardfolk were already ancient.

Early conflicts between humans and Ix'Vasyla ended predictably: the marshes swallowed the invaders. Eventually, a pragmatic accommodation emerged. Humans who submitted to Ix'Vasyla authority were permitted to live, work, and trade. Those who resisted joined the nutrients feeding the marsh ecology.

The wars with Gorath and Trømgar are more recent—centuries old rather than millennia. As both neighboring powers expanded, they encountered Nashua's borders and decided to push through. They're still pushing. They're still failing.

### Culture

#### The Hunt

Ix'Vasyla culture centers on the hunt—the patient stalking, the perfect strike, the kill. This isn't metaphor; it's literal. Every Ix'Vasyla, male or female, is trained from hatching to hunt. The skills transfer directly to warfare: patience, stealth, reading terrain, delivering death efficiently.

Successful hunts are celebrated; failed hunts are analyzed for lessons. The greatest hunters earn prestige that translates to political influence. The worst hunters are relegated to support roles—still valuable, but not honored.

#### Patience as Virtue

The Ix'Vasyla concept of **szrilketh** (roughly "the waiting strike") pervades their culture. Szrilketh is the art of perfect timing—knowing when to act and when to wait, accepting discomfort now for advantage later. A warrior who strikes too soon wastes effort; one who strikes too late misses opportunity. Szrilketh is striking at the precise moment when effort yields maximum result.

This philosophy makes the Ix'Vasyla maddening opponents. They don't respond to provocation. They don't take bait. They wait, and watch, and when they finally move, it's because they've identified the exact moment of maximum advantage.

#### Death and Memory

The Ix'Vasyla don't fear death—they fear meaningless death. A warrior who dies achieving an objective is honored; one who dies uselessly is pitied. The worst fate is to die having accomplished nothing, to have wasted the clan's investment in training and equipping a warrior.

The honored dead are consumed by their clan-kin in ritual meals. The Ix'Vasyla believe this transfers the dead warrior's essence to the living, strengthening the clan. Foreign observers find this practice horrifying; the Ix'Vasyla find foreign burial practices wasteful.

### Hooks & Tensions

**The Poison Scholars**: The Arcane Consortium maintains scholarly interests that extend beyond mere commerce. Their bounty on Yegnoth information suggests research into planar phenomena. What are they actually studying in those marsh laboratories?

**The Human Question**: Nashua's integrated humans occupy an ambiguous position—not enslaved, but not equal. Some advocate for expanding human rights; others see humans as useful tools that shouldn't forget their place. A charismatic human leader could destabilize this balance.

**The Sylthik Temples**: The serpent-folk's religious activities in Dolno Jelovce remain opaque to outsiders. They worship Sythikranos and await her return—but what does that mean for Nashua when/if the serpent goddess awakens?

**Clan Fractures**: The Council holds because external threats demand unity. But old grudges fester beneath the surface. A major defeat—or a major victory that ends one of the wars—could unleash generations of suppressed inter-clan conflict.

**The Southern Vulnerability**: The scrublands are Nashua's weak point. If Gorath ever committed to a sustained campaign there, accepting the casualties needed to push through, they might break into the river corridor. Some in Tirexonos argue for preemptive action; others counsel patience. The debate continues as Gorathi patrols probe ever closer.

## Nektuna

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Feudal monarchy with merchant influence

**Primary Inhabitants**: Humans (dominant), Craven (massive population)

**Secondary Inhabitants**: Dwarblin, Trollkin, Ayblek

**Transient**: Weblin traders

**Population**: ~400,000 (Tarkhetan alone: ~120,000)

**Stability**: Stable but tense

**Core Values**: Wealth, power, prestige, naval supremacy, the eternal flame

- Nektuna is the imperial heartland of Tarkhon, ruled by **King Selron II** from the capital of **Tarkhetan**. His authority is theoretically absolute, but in practice he navigates a web of noble factions, merchant interests, and military commanders.
- The state is dominated by humans, but Craven make up perhaps a third of the population—laborers, sailors, soldiers, and increasingly merchants in their own right. Tensions between human and Craven communities simmer constantly but rarely boil over.
- Smaller populations of dwarblin (dwarven-goblin hybrids), trollkin, and even ayblek add to Nektuna's cosmopolitan character. Weblin traders pass through regularly, their caravans a common sight in Tarkhetan's markets.
- Nektuna is wealthy beyond measure but also paranoid. Everyone wants what they have. Every ally is a potential enemy. Every smile hides a knife.

### Economy

**Size**: Massive

**Tech**: Advanced (maritime, financial, magical)

**Primary Exports**: Services (shipping, banking, insurance), fire magic, luxury goods

**Primary Imports**: Everything (as intermediary)

- Nektuna doesn't produce much—it *taxes* production. Every ship through the strait pays tariffs. Every merchant using Tarkhon roads pays tolls. Every trader wanting access to Tarkhon markets pays fees.
- The great merchant houses of Tarkhetan have made fortunes not by making things but by financing those who do. They insure ships, lend money to kingdoms, and take a cut of every transaction they touch.
- **Besnoumeru**, Nektuna's second city, sits on a time leyline. Its merchants can anticipate market changes before they happen—a massive advantage that has made the city almost as wealthy as the capital.
- This economy is entirely dependent on controlling the strait. If an alternative route opened, Nektuna would collapse within a generation.

### Military

**Size**: Large (navy-focused)

**Quality**: High

**Enrollment**: Professional with conscription reserves

- Nektuna maintains the most powerful navy in the region. Ships that refuse to pay are sunk. Pirates are hunted relentlessly. The sea lanes are safe—for those who pay.
- The **Firemage Corps** is Nektuna's elite military asset. Born on the fire leyline that runs through Tarkhetan, these mages can burn ships from a mile away. A single firemage on the walls can destroy an entire fleet.
- The army is smaller but professional, used primarily to garrison fortresses and project power into troublesome territories.
- Conscription can raise large reserves in emergencies, drawing from the Craven population especially.

### Geography

**Location**: Central Tarkhon, controlling both shores of the Needle (the strait's narrowest point)

**Biomes**: Temperate coastland, Mediterranean hills, island territories

**Climate**: Warm Mediterranean—mild winters, hot summers

**Named Features**: The Needle (narrowest strait point), Tarkhetan (capital), Besnoumeru (time-leyline city), Pyris Island

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Tarkhetan

**Major Cities**: Besnoumeru

**Controlled Territories**: Pyris Island, Astrelle (vassal state)

**Fortresses**: Torsnerhun (across the Needle), Fort Tenze (Pyris, ruined)

### Tarkhetan

The capital of the Tarkhon Empire and seat of King Selron II.

Tarkhetan is a city of extremes. Gleaming palaces rise beside rotting slums. Merchant princes who could buy kingdoms walk streets where beggars die unnoticed. The harbor never sleeps—ships arrive and depart at all hours, their cargoes taxed, inspected, and sent onward.

The city is built on a series of hills overlooking the Needle, the narrowest point of the strait. From the palace walls, you can see clear across to Torsnerhun fortress on the opposite shore. Between them, nothing passes without Tarkhetan's permission.

**The Old City** occupies the highest hills—noble estates, the royal palace, the great cathedral where the Evertorch burns. Here the wealthy live behind high walls, attended by servants and protected by private guards.

**The Middle City** spreads across the lower slopes—merchant houses, guild halls, respectable taverns, the homes of successful craftsmen. This is where business happens, where deals are made, where fortunes rise and fall.

**The Waterfront** sprawls along the harbor—warehouses, shipyards, sailor's taverns, brothels, and the cramped tenements where workers live. Craven make up the majority here. The smell of fish, tar, and humanity mingles with salt air.

**The Undercity** exists in the spaces between—tunnels, cellars, forgotten passages. Smugglers, thieves, and those who want to disappear find their way here. The city guard doesn't patrol the Undercity. Some say things live down there that have never seen the sun.

### The Evertorch

In the great cathedral at Tarkhetan's heart burns the **Evertorch**—an eternally burning flame that has never been extinguished since its lighting over six centuries ago.

The torch is Tarkhon's most sacred symbol, representing eternal dominion and unbroken continuity. Emperors are crowned in its light. The most binding oaths are sworn before it. Ritual magic of time and fire occurs at its shrine.

What most humans have forgotten—or choose not to remember—is that the Evertorch is a **Neferati creation**. The same tradition of eternal flames that burns in the Kingdoms of Fire. Lit by Neferati hands, sustained by Neferati magic.

The Neferati remember.

### The Fire Leyline

A leyline of fire runs directly through Tarkhetan, its power concentrated beneath the Old City. Children born here sometimes manifest fire attunement—and those who do are claimed by the **Firemage Corps**.

The Corps is both military asset and political faction. Firemages are trained from childhood in the Citadel of Flames, emerging as weapons of terrifying power. A single trained firemage can burn a ship to the waterline from the city walls. A squad of them can destroy a fleet.

This makes the Corps essential to Nektuna's defense—and dangerously influential in its politics. The **Pyremaster**, who commands the Corps, holds a seat on the king's council. Wise rulers keep the firemages loyal. Foolish ones learn why the previous dynasty fell.

### Besnoumeru

Nektuna's second city, built where a **time leyline** surfaces. Besnoumeru is almost as wealthy as Tarkhetan—not from controlling trade, but from predicting it.

Merchants born on the time leyline sometimes develop a peculiar gift: they sense market changes before they happen. Not prophecy exactly—more like an instinct for when to buy and when to sell, when ships will arrive, when prices will shift. The **Oracle Merchants** of Besnoumeru have made fortunes from this gift.

The city is quieter than Tarkhetan, more orderly, with an almost eerie sense of calm. The merchants here don't rush—they already know what's coming.

### Pyris Island

A moderate-sized island southwest of the strait, technically part of Nektuna. Pyris is home to an old population—humans who've interbred with dwarves over centuries, producing a stocky, hardy folk who mostly want to be left alone.

The Pyrisi are farmers and fishers, content with their simple lives. They pay their taxes, send their young to serve in the navy, and try not to attract attention from the capital.

**Fort Tenze**, on the island's eastern coast, guards a secondary chokepoint—not as critical as the Needle, but significant. The fortress has been in ruins for nearly three centuries, ever since the Severance.

### Fort Tenze: The Cursed Fortress

Fort Tenze was a functioning fortress until the **Severance**—the event that ended direct Neferati rule of Tarkhon.

When the last Neferati-blooded emperor died without clear heir, the succession war that followed was brutal. Fort Tenze's garrison chose the wrong side. When the victors came to take the fortress, something went wrong.

The details are disputed. Some say the garrison's firemages lost control during the final assault. Others say Neferati loyalists performed some desperate ritual. What's certain is that the fortress burned—not normal fire, but something that left the stones themselves wrong. Twisted. The flames were extinguished, but the wrongness remained.

Three times since, the crown has ordered Fort Tenze rebuilt. Three times, the workers suffered: accidents, disappearances, madness. Equipment failed. Stones wouldn't set properly. Workers reported whispers, figures in their peripheral vision, dreams of burning.

Now the fortress sits empty. The Pyrisi avoid it. The crown has stopped trying. Smugglers use the ruins as a waypoint, though even they don't stay long.

Whatever happened at Fort Tenze, the fire hasn't quite gone out.

### King Selron II

The current ruler of the Tarkhon Empire, forty-three years old and in the seventeenth year of his reign.

Selron is intelligent, cautious, and deeply aware of how precarious his position is. He inherited a stable empire and has worked to keep it that way—managing the noble factions, maintaining the trade relationships, avoiding the wars that would drain the treasury.

His critics call him weak, indecisive, a king who rules by compromise rather than command. His supporters call him wise, patient, a king who understands that Tarkhon's strength is wealth, not war.

**Appearance**: Average height, running to fat in middle age. Brown hair going gray. Shrewd eyes that miss nothing. Dresses simply by royal standards—he prefers to seem approachable.

**Family**: Married to Queen Vethira of Astrelle (a political match that secured the vassal state). Three children: Prince Hathan (19, the heir), Princess Lyselle (16), Prince Doran (12).

**Governing style**: Selron rules through his council, balancing factions against each other. He rarely makes dramatic pronouncements, preferring to let decisions emerge through negotiation. This makes him seem weak but keeps anyone from becoming strong enough to threaten him.

**Greatest fear**: That the Kingdoms of Fire will remember they have a better claim to the Evertorch than he does.

### The Royal Council

Selron governs through a council of powerful figures, each representing a major interest:

**Lord Gavren Holt** — Master of Coin. Controls the treasury and has the merchant houses' ear. Fat, jolly, and ruthless about money.

**Admiral Kessa Thorn** — Commander of the Fleet. The navy is her domain. Respected by sailors, feared by pirates, and dangerously popular with the common folk.

**Pyremaster Valdros Kaine** — Commander of the Firemage Corps. Gaunt, intense, speaks rarely. When he does speak, people listen. The Corps' loyalty to him is absolute.

**Lord Armund Castor** — Warden of the Marches. Responsible for land defenses, including the fortresses. Old military family, traditional values, suspicious of anything that smells like change.

**High Priestess Salenne** — Keeper of the Evertorch. Leads the cathedral clergy. Her authority is religious, but in Tarkhon, the Evertorch is politics. She knows more secrets than anyone.

**Duchess Ysmera of Astrelle** — Speaks for the vassal state. Also the queen's aunt. Navigates the awkward position of representing Astrelle while her niece is married to its overlord.

### The Neferati Legacy

Six centuries ago, Tarkhon was founded by **Neferati conquerors** who understood that controlling the Needle meant controlling trade. They brought fire magic, the tradition of eternal flames, and the military power to seize the strait.

For nearly three centuries, Tarkhon was ruled by Neferati emperors or their descendants. They lit the Evertorch. They established the Firemage Corps. They built the foundations of everything that makes Tarkhon powerful.

But the Neferati line diluted over generations. Marriages to local humans, the practicalities of ruling a diverse population, the slow drift of blood and culture. By the end, the "Neferati" emperors were mostly human—fire-touched, perhaps, but not truly of the flame.

The **Severance** came when Emperor Valdric III died without legitimate heir. His children by his Neferati mistress were passed over for his nephew—fully human, with no fire in his blood. The Neferati faction resisted. The war that followed was brief but vicious.

The human faction won. The remaining pure Neferati withdrew to the Kingdoms of Fire. The Evertorch stayed—too sacred to move, too dangerous to extinguish. But its keepers changed.

This is why the Kingdoms of Fire stay in the empire despite having the power to leave. They don't see themselves as tributaries—they see themselves as founders in exile. The Evertorch is theirs. Tarkhon is theirs. The humans just haven't realized it yet.

And someday, perhaps, the fire will remember who lit it.

### Primary Conflicts

**The Succession Question**

Prince Hathan is heir, but he's untested and some say weak. Princess Lyselle is sharper, more ambitious—and some whisper she'd make a better ruler. Selron is healthy, but he's not young. The factions are already positioning for what comes next.

**The Firemage Problem**

Pyremaster Valdros is loyal—for now. But the Corps' power has grown over generations, and some fear what happens when a less scrupulous Pyremaster takes command. The firemages could make or break any succession crisis.

**The Neferati Shadow**

The Kingdoms of Fire have been patient for three centuries. But patience isn't infinite. If the right opportunity arose—a succession crisis, a military defeat, a weakened throne—they might remember their claim. High Priestess Salenne has noticed certain Neferati ambassadors spending a lot of time in the cathedral, studying the Evertorch's flames.

**The Naval Rivalry**

Admiral Kessa is popular. Too popular. Selron needs the navy, but he also fears what happens if Kessa decides she wants more than command of a fleet. For now, she seems content with her ships. But ambition has a way of growing.

**Fort Tenze**

The cursed fortress is embarrassing. A functional Fort Tenze would significantly strengthen the western approaches. But every attempt to rebuild has failed. Some on the council want to try again. Others say the cost isn't worth the risk. And some whisper that certain parties benefit from the fortress staying ruined...

### Vassal: Astrelle

Astrelle was absorbed into Nektuna's orbit two centuries ago—peacefully, through a combination of marriage alliances and economic pressure. The current arrangement makes Astrelle a vassal state: self-governing in internal matters but subordinate to Tarkhetan in foreign policy and defense.

Astrelle hosts two critical fortresses: **Torsnerhun** (directly across the Needle from Tarkhetan) and **Sharvatunis** (watching the eastern approach). This makes Astrelle strategically vital—and gives its duchess leverage she wouldn't otherwise have.

Duchess Ysmera walks a careful line: loyal enough to keep Tarkhetan happy, independent enough to maintain Astrelle's dignity. Her niece's marriage to the king complicates things. Is she family or subject? Both, and the tension never quite resolves.

### History

**The Founding (~600 years ago)**: Neferati warlords seize the Needle, establishing control over the strait. The Evertorch is lit in what will become Tarkhetan.

**The Neferati Era (~600-300 years ago)**: Neferati emperors rule from Tarkhetan, expanding the empire through trade dominance rather than conquest. The Firemage Corps is established. Besnoumeru rises on its time leyline.

**The Dilution (~400-300 years ago)**: Neferati bloodlines mix with human through generations of political marriages. The ruling family becomes increasingly human—fire-touched perhaps, but not truly of the flame.

**The Severance (~300 years ago)**: The last fire-blooded emperor dies. Succession war between human and Neferati factions. Humans win. Pure Neferati withdraw to the Kingdoms of Fire. Fort Tenze is destroyed in the conflict. The Evertorch stays—too sacred to move, too dangerous to extinguish.

**The Human Era (~300 years ago - present)**: Human dynasties rule, maintaining the traditions and symbols of Neferati founders while slowly forgetting their origins. Emperors become kings. The Kingdoms of Fire remain within the empire, waiting.

**The Present**: King Selron II maintains stability through careful balance. But the old tensions remain—Neferati legacy, naval ambitions, firemage power, and the eternal question of succession.

## Pelaria

Tags: state

Inhabited by Kendrel. A member of the Kendrel Kingdoms.

Huge chunk of population is fire attuned. Steam mages, geysers, etc. 

Underwater volcanic activity dots the area.

## Phiora

Tags: state, major island

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Fraternal monarchy

**Primary Inhabitants**: Verucan (fire dwarves)

**Population**: 40,000

**Stability**: Stable

**Core Values**: Humor, wit, passion, smithing, craftsmanship

- The Verucan are fire dwarves—obsidian-black skin with glowing red veins that pulse with inner heat. Born from volcanic forges, they built their civilization within active volcanoes, harnessing geothermal energy.
- Like volcanoes, the Verucan are complacent most of the time, but will occasionally begin to bubble beneath the surface, only to explode with fiery temper at some unexpected moment. Their loves burn as hot as their hatreds.
- Phiora is ruled by siblings under a fraternal monarchy. The elder sibling has more executive power, but when succession comes, it passes to the children of the younger sibling. This unusual arrangement prevents power from concentrating in one branch and forces the ruling siblings to cooperate—or at least to limit their conflicts.
- Despite being master weaponsmiths, the Verucan are surprisingly non-militaristic. They view anger as a sacred flame that drives innovation and excellence in craft, not conquest.

### Economy

**Size**: Medium

**Tech**: Developed

**Primary Exports**: Weapons, metalwork, volcanic glass, geothermal crafts

**Primary Imports**: Food, timber, textiles

- The forges of Mount Kajiit produce weapons of exceptional quality. Phioran steel is sought across the Middle Sea, and wealthy warriors pay premium prices for blades tempered in volcanic fire.
- The island's volcanic soil is poor for farming, and the Verucan have little interest in agriculture. They import most of their food in exchange for metalwork.
- The economy runs hot and cold, matching Verucan temperament. Production surges during periods of inspiration; work slows when the collective mood turns contemplative.

### Military

**Size**: Small

**Quality**: Medium

**Enrollment**: Voluntary

- Despite being expert weapon craftsmen, the Phioran populace is largely non-militaristic. Most have never fought in a war. They make the tools of war; others use them.
- Verucan generally dislike the sea—something about the cold water conflicts with their fiery nature. The Phioran navy is pitiful, barely sufficient to patrol local waters.
- Defense relies on geography. The caldera of Mount Kajiit is virtually impregnable, and any invader would have to fight uphill through volcanic terrain against defenders who know every tunnel and lava flow.

### Geography

**Location**: Pii Island, in the Forgotten Sea east of the Ofrenia Passage

**Biomes**: Volcanic island, geothermal vents, obsidian fields

**Named Entities**: Mount Kajiit, Kedari Emnath

**Rivers & Lakes**: Geothermal pools, lava flows

**Adjacent Waters**: The Forgotten Sea, the Middle Sea

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Mereiki (within Mount Kajiit's caldera)

**Cities**: Mereiki

**Towns**: None

**Villages**: Doga (coastal)

### Primary Conflicts

**Sibling Rivalry**

The fraternal monarchy ensures that ruling siblings must work together, but it doesn't ensure they'll like each other. Court drama erupts regularly when the elder and younger clash over policy, pride, or petty grievances. The explosions are spectacular—sometimes literally, given Verucan tempers—but the system has survived for generations.

**Arms Dealing Ethics**

Phiora sells weapons to anyone who can pay, which means their blades often appear on both sides of the same war. This creates complicated diplomatic situations and occasional moral qualms. Some Verucan argue for restricting sales; others point out that a blade doesn't choose its wielder. The debate smolders but never quite ignites into policy change.

**Isolation vs. Engagement**

The Verucan dislike the sea and generally prefer to stay on their island, but trade requires engagement with the wider world. Younger Verucan increasingly question whether isolation serves their interests, while elders point out that every time Phiora has gotten involved in mainland politics, it's ended badly.

**The Kajiit Legacy**

Mount Kajiit was once forcibly erupted by a follower of Dyos to end the daemon wars, causing a volcanic winter and multi-millennia ice age that killed millions. The Verucan live with this history—literally, within the caldera of that catastrophic eruption. Some view it as ancient history; others believe the mountain remembers and might one day remind the world of its power.

### History

The Verucan emerged from the volcanic forges of southern peaks in ages past, and eventually found their way to Pii Island. They recognized Mount Kajiit as kin—a living volcano that matched their fiery nature—and made their home within its caldera.

The fraternal monarchy developed as a solution to succession crises that nearly destroyed early Phiora. When two siblings both claimed the throne, the compromise that prevented civil war became permanent tradition: share power, but ensure it passes to a different branch each generation. The system creates tension but prevents tyranny.

Phiora's reputation as a weapons source grew over centuries. The combination of volcanic heat, Verucan craftsmanship, and obsessive attention to quality produced blades that outlasted their wielders. Kings, generals, and assassins all sought Phioran steel. The Verucan sold to all of them and stayed out of the fights their weapons fueled.

The island's historical tragedy—the Kajiit eruption—predates Verucan settlement but shapes their worldview. They live in a place that once ended an age. They've built their civilization around a force that could destroy it at any moment. This awareness gives Verucan culture its characteristic intensity: life is short, the volcano is eternal, so work with passion while you can.

## Phirexes

Tags: state, emerald coast, swamp

A fog-shrouded swampland at the southeastern edge of the Emerald Coast, ruled by the gorgon queen Phendexelas the Beautiful. What appears to be an absolute monarchy is something stranger: a nation of willing captives who praise their jailer nightly, trapped not by walls but by magical addiction to the very mists that imprison them.

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Absolute monarchy (de facto theocratic cult)

**Primary Inhabitants**: Dengar (swamp halflings)

**Population**: ~30,000 (concentrated in Maurevelious; several hundred refugees in hiding)

**Stability**: Stable (superficially); deeply unstable (beneath the surface)

**Core Values**: Gratitude, unity, devotion to the queen, "the worse it gets, the better it was"

The gorgon Phendexelas the Beautiful has ruled Phirexes for sixty years, having manufactured the crisis that brought her to power and positioned herself as savior. She does not need to rule through fear—the Dengar culture of finding silver linings in suffering has been weaponized into mass Stockholm syndrome. Citizens genuinely believe they are fortunate to live under her protection, because the alternative (the fog-maddened swamp she created) is so much worse.

Every evening, Phendexelas walks the raised boardwalk through Maurevelious's central district. Every citizen who can attend does attend, kneeling with heads bowed as she passes, listening to her speak of her love for them. Those who miss the Queen's Walk are noted. Those who miss it repeatedly are visited by her agents. Those visits end in one of two ways: renewed devotion or disappearance.

The refugees—a few hundred Dengar who escaped Maurevelious and cannot return—hide in Old One's Wood, sustained by smugglers and the Sweet Water River. They are sick, all of them; the fog-binding that makes the queen's subjects unable to leave also afflicts those who've fled. But they endure, waiting for something to change, holding onto the memory of what the Dengar were before Phendexelas came.

### Economy

**Size**: Medium

**Tech**: Somewhat developed (exceptional alchemy)

**Primary Exports**: Medicines, alchemical compounds, "swamp spirits" (alcohol)

**Primary Imports**: Metals, metal goods, preserved foods, textiles

The Dengar are master alchemists, a tradition predating the queen by centuries. Their still-houses produce medicines that no other culture can match: salves for infections that resist magical healing, elixirs that dull pain without clouding the mind, compounds that can purge exotic poisons. They also produce "swamp spirits"—a violently alcoholic brew that doubles as solvent, antiseptic, and (the Dengar insist) a perfectly reasonable breakfast drink.

Phendexelas has captured this economy without destroying it. She controls access to rare ingredients by controlling access to Duskwood Forest where they grow. She monitors what formulas are produced, confiscating anything that might counteract fog-binding. She takes her cut of all exports. But she lets the Dengar work, lets them profit, lets them feel like they're thriving under her rule. Happy workers are productive workers, and productive workers don't ask questions.

The swamps prevent heavy industry—no mining, no large-scale metalwork, no foundries. Everything metal must be imported, which gives the queen another lever of control. She decides what comes in and from whom.

### Military

**Size**: None (officially)

**Quality**: N/A

**Enrollment**: Forbidden

Phendexelas forbids any military force in Phirexes. She and the swamp itself, she argues, are sufficient defense against any invasion. This is not empty boasting—the Croaking Briars have repelled every Trømgar assault, and the fogs would make conventional warfare impossible even if an army could reach Maurevelious.

The real reason for the prohibition is control. An armed populace might get ideas. The queen's personal power—her gorgon gaze, her sorcery, her control over the fogs—is more than sufficient to handle any internal dissent. External threats simply don't exist in meaningful form.

The watching ships that patrol the Gulf of Tears are not military vessels; they're classified as "customs enforcement." The agents who visit those who miss the Queen's Walk are not soldiers; they're "concerned citizens ensuring community wellness." The distinctions are technical but important—the queen maintains the fiction that Phirexes needs no military because Phirexes has nothing to fear.

### Geography

**Location**: Southeastern Emerald Coast, Rimihuica

**Biomes**: Swamp, marsh, fog-shrouded wetland, ancient forest

**Named Regions**:
- Misty Marshes (central wetlands)
- Cragwood Swamp (fog-touched nightmare zone)
- Old One's Wood (primordial forest, refugee hideout)
- Sweetwoods (northern timber forest)
- Duskwood Forest (southwestern twilight forest, rare alchemical ingredients)
- Croaking Briars (western thorn-barrier, border with Trømgar)
- Whispering Mangroves (eastern coast)
- Ogzwad Swamp (southeastern, dragon territory)
- Grove of Migwam (sacred site, now queen's shrine)
- Hag's Pasture (mysterious clearing)

**Rivers & Lakes**:
- Sweet Water River (clean freshwater, refugee lifeline)
- Mud Run (fog-infused, hallucinogenic)
- Groaning Creek (mysterious, constantly moaning)

**Adjacent Waters**:
- Gulf of Tears (northwest)
- Crocodile Coast (east)
- Sea of Seven Snakes (south)

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Maurevelious

**Cities**: None besides Maurevelious

**Towns**: None (all population concentrated in capital)

**Villages**: Scattered work camps (logging, harvesting), refugee camps in Old One's Wood

Phirexes is unusual in having essentially one settlement. Before the queen came, the Dengar lived throughout the swamp in small communities. Phendexelas consolidated them into Maurevelious "for their protection"—creating a population center she could monitor and control. The old village sites are now ruins slowly sinking into the bog, occasionally visible when the fog thins.

### Borders & Neighbors

**West (Trømgar)**: The Croaking Briars form an impassable living wall. The Strømgodden battle dwarves have tried repeatedly to breach it; the briars grow back overnight, faster where blood is spilled. An uneasy non-relationship exists—neither side can reach the other, so neither side bothers with diplomacy.

**South (Kyagos)**: The Cloud Mountains separate Phirexes from the lawless Shacklands to the south. Little contact exists; Kyagos has its own problems.

**Northwest (Emerald Coast nations)**: Trade relationships exist with Eoga and Vystrilik, though heavily controlled. The queen permits enough commerce to maintain her economy but discourages any cultural exchange that might give her subjects ideas.

**Southeast (Ogzwad/Pfustias)**: The dragon Pfustias controls this territory in all but name. The queen and the dragon have some kind of arrangement—neither moves against the other, but neither acknowledges the other as ally.

### Primary Conflicts

**The Queen vs. The Refugees**: Several hundred Dengar have escaped Maurevelious and hidden in Old One's Wood. They cannot truly leave (fog-binding), cannot return (the queen would destroy them), and cannot live openly (the queen cannot tolerate visible defiance). The queen walks a careful line: she must maintain her image as savior while suppressing those who've rejected salvation. So far, she's content to let them suffer in hiding, trusting that their sickness and hardship will eventually break them.

**The Queen vs. Old One's Wood**: Something in the ancient forest hates Phendexelas with cold patience. Her fogs penetrate but don't control it. Her creatures enter and don't return. The forest shelters her enemies and resists her power. She hasn't moved against it directly—perhaps she can't, or perhaps she's waiting for the right moment.

**The Queen vs. Pfustias**: The dragon arrived a decade after Phendexelas. Their relationship is unclear to outsiders—cold war? Mutual observation? Some kind of game? Pfustias knows something about the queen that she'd prefer stayed secret. What leverage that gives the dragon, and how she might use it, remains to be seen.

**Internal Tension**: Not all Dengar have fully surrendered to the cult of gratitude. Some remember what life was like before, or have heard stories from grandparents. Quiet dissent exists, carefully hidden, waiting for something to change. The queen's agents work constantly to identify and neutralize these elements before they can organize.

### History

Sixty years ago, the Dengar lived throughout the swamp in scattered communities. They knew its dangers and respected them; they'd negotiated relationships with its creatures and spirits over generations. Life was hard but sustainable. They were free.

Then the gorgon came.

No one knows where Phendexelas came from or why she chose Phirexes. Some say she was fleeing something worse. Others say she was drawn by the swamp's latent magic. What matters is what she did: within months of her arrival, the fogs descended.

At first, the mists seemed merely weather. Then the swamp beasts began to go mad. Creatures the Dengar had lived alongside for generations turned savage. The spirits withdrew or went hostile. The carefully negotiated peace collapsed into chaos.

The Dengar fled their villages, gathering in the only safe place they could find: a patch of high ground where a strange gorgon was building a city with impossible speed. Phendexelas welcomed them with open arms. She'd prepared, she said. She'd seen this coming. She would protect them.

Within a year, Maurevelious stood complete, and thirty thousand Dengar lived within its walls. They were grateful—so grateful. The queen had saved them from a catastrophe she herself had created, and they had no way of knowing. The fog-binding was subtle at first, a dependency that grew so slowly it seemed natural. By the time anyone realized they couldn't leave, it was far too late.

Sixty years later, two generations have grown up knowing nothing but the queen's rule. The elders who remember freedom are dying off. The refugees who carry that memory are hunted and sick. And Phendexelas walks her boardwalk every evening, accepting the worship of a people who believe she is all that stands between them and oblivion.

### Notable Figures

**Phendexelas the Beautiful**: Gorgon queen, sorceress, architect of the catastrophe. See [dramatis_personae/Phendexelas](../dramatis_personae/Phendexelas.md) for full entry.

**Pfustias**: Swamp dragon dwelling in Ogzwad Swamp. Patient, philosophical, watching. See [bestiary/dragons/Pfustias](../../bestiary/dragons/Pfustias.md) for full entry.

### Player Hooks

**The Smuggler's Run**: A Vystrilik smuggling captain needs crew for a supply run to the refugees. The pay is excellent. The route goes through the Crocodile Coast. Survival is not guaranteed.

**The Silent Grove**: An elderly Dengar exile approaches the party with a request: investigate the Grove of Migwam and find out why the ancestors stopped speaking. What happened to the spirits when the fogs came? Are they trapped? Dead? Something worse?

**Dragon's Bargain**: Pfustias has information about Queen Phendexelas—something that could shift the balance of power in Phirexes. She'll share it. For a price. The price is never gold.

**The Cure**: A brilliant Dengar alchemist claims to have developed a treatment for fog-binding. She needs rare ingredients from Duskwood Forest, which means getting the queen's permission—or going without it. She also needs test subjects willing to risk everything on an unproven formula.

**The Queen's Secret**: Rumor among the refugees: Phendexelas cannot leave Phirexes either. The fogs bind her too, or something does. She's as trapped as her subjects, ruling a prison she can never escape. If true, this changes everything. If false, investigating it means drawing the queen's attention.

**Heart of the Wood**: Something lives in the center of Old One's Wood—something that hates the queen and has been waiting sixty years for the right allies. The refugees speak of it in whispers. Pfustias speaks of it not at all, which might be more telling. Finding it means navigating a forest that thinks.

## Postronamas Empire

Tags: ruins, state, fallen, westwilds

An ancient civilization that rose to greatness through mastery of twyl crystals, built an empire spanning the western Westwilds, and collapsed into madness and civil war when they pushed too deep into their own power.

### Overview

The Postronamas dominated the Piktiniti Desert and surrounding regions for centuries, perhaps millennia. Their civilization was built on twyl—a crystalline mineral that produces oxygen and, when concentrated, resonates at frequencies that can enhance mental abilities, enable long-distance communication, and amplify magical power.

At their height, the Postronamas constructed the Chakatann pillars: massive stone columns containing twyl crystal cores, spaced ten miles apart in a grid across the western desert. The pillar network allowed them to project power across continental distances.

Then they pushed too deep into the crystal caverns beneath their capital, Enimogos. The music of the deepest crystals broke their leaders' minds. The madness spread through the resonance network, cascading from pillar to pillar. Within a generation, the empire collapsed.

### Culture (What Survives)

**Aesthetic:** Egypt + Japan + Tlingit. Geometric line art, flowing garments, an emphasis on symmetry and pattern. Postronamas artifacts are immediately recognizable—clean lines, insect motifs, crystal inlays.

**Insect Partnership:** The Postronamas worked closely with the giant insects of the Piktiniti. They bred enormous dung beetles whose wing vibrations could harvest twyl at precise frequencies. They wore armor crafted from insect chitin—beautiful and effective. Their art featured insects prominently.

**Crystal Meditation:** Postronamas leaders used massive crystal caves as meditation chambers, achieving enhanced perception and magical sensitivity. This practice was their greatest achievement and their downfall.

### The Collapse

The crystal caverns extend far underground, and the deeper crystals sing differently. The Postronamas leaders who sought the deepest power found it—a resonance that permeates the mind, overwhelming thought, erasing identity.

The madness spread through the pillar network. Civil war erupted as factions blamed each other, as leaders descended into psychosis, as the empire tore itself apart. Survivors scattered. Most died. A few found refuge—on the pillars (becoming the Seyiki), in the musical forest (becoming the Melodians), or into the mysterious Woods of Systoril (fate unknown).

### Legacy

**The Chakatann Pillars:** Still standing, now colonized by Seyiki gnomes. Most are broken or depleted; some still hum.

**Enimogos:** The shattered capital, still resonating with maddening intensity. A death trap for treasure hunters.

**Melodia:** A forest where Postronamas-engineered trees still sing.

**The Seyiki:** Gnomes who merged with Postronamas survivors and inherited fragments of their knowledge.

**Artifacts:** Postronamas relics—crystal-powered devices, insect-chitin armor, resonance tools—command enormous prices. Most are dangerous.

### What They Knew

The Postronamas understood harmonics and resonance at levels modern mages don't match. Their twyl-harvesting technique (using dung beetle wing vibrations at specific frequencies) has never been replicated. Their pillar network demonstrated engineering capabilities that seem impossible.

Whether this knowledge is lost or simply waiting to be rediscovered in Enimogos is a question that draws scholars and fools to the Piktiniti.

## Poum-Titch

Tags: state

Located in Terrenia, south of the Green Mountains and east of Aal Salma. Inhabited by Scalawags. A huge civil war has recently broken out—total disaster, as the northern nation declares independence from the rest of the state. Total chaos, lots of death. Armies are assembling and marching on each other.

## Pyonokraus

Tags: city, state

Home to some Ayblek.

This city is cursed—none of the inhabitants can ever leave, including those who enter from the outside. Built into a titan skull on the mountainside, it has layers upon layers of city built on top of itself, since there's nowhere to go but down and on top of existing buildings. 

It has a similar feel to the mining town in guardians of the galaxy where they meet the bioengineer

It has existed for millenia, and contains secrets completely unknown to the outside world. Getting them, however, is quite difficult; no one who enters can ever leave. You can greet people at the border, but you have to be able to offer something fantastic to make them willing to share—after all, they're screwed, and they have no reason to help you if you can't offer something incredible in return.

## Qet Yemani

**Primary Inhabitants**: Ulvsjael

**Core Values**: Loyalty, heritage, strength

### Military

**Quality**: High

**Enrollment**: Voluntary

- Nearly everyone is capable of fighting, so their entire population doubles as their army.
- There is no discipline or unity across tribes, and they have never had to fight together for a common cause.
