Psychedelic substances have been discovered—flora that grows in the deeper parts of the forest. Some Ezuri use them for spiritual experiences or creative inspiration. The council has not approved, viewing them as dangerous or corrupting. The debate is quiet but persistent.

**Isolation vs. Engagement**

The outside world is increasingly chaotic—mad queens in Thespia, silvertongue plagues in Ubrik, dragon standoffs. Some younger Ezuri think Stipen should engage more, help their neighbors, participate in the wider world. Elders argue that leaving the forest means death, and involvement brings only trouble.

### History

The Ezuri came to these forests long ago, fleeing the Mad Gorehorn disease that ravaged the Jungles of Titania. They climbed into the trees to escape and never came down. Over centuries, they bonded with the forest until their lives became intertwined with it.

Now Stipen is an ancient, peaceful realm where gnomes live for centuries among the branches. They want nothing from the outside world, and hope the outside world wants nothing from them.

## Sylke

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Absolute monarchy

**Primary Inhabitants**: Oznak, Tikhaya

**Population**: 300,000

**Stability**: Very Stable

**Core Values**: Duty, privacy, minding one's own business, nihilism

- Ruled by Queen Alisandra the Merciful—a title dripping with irony. She's calculating, cruel, and has no qualms about massive human sacrifice to power Deoric magic for the throne.
- The population has learned not to ask questions. Eyes and ears are everywhere. Neighbors inform on neighbors. The queen knows everything, and then some.
- Sylke functions with brutal efficiency. Taxes are collected, roads are maintained, criminals are punished. The cost is freedom, privacy, and anyone who draws the queen's attention.
- Recently conquered Tornia in a swift, "fairly bloodless" war. Now Alisandra rules two of Ofrenia's three kingdoms—with Joswik clearly next on her list.

### Economy

**Size**: Large

**Tech**: Very Developed

**Primary Exports**: Lumber, manufactured goods, ships

**Primary Imports**: Grain, minerals, slaves (through intermediaries)

- Sylke's forests are legendary—dense, well-managed, and producing timber that builds ships across the Middle Sea.
- The economy runs on Deoric magic, which runs on human sacrifice. The Ivory Hand ensures a steady supply of victims, disguised as criminals, prisoners, and the inconvenient.
- With Tornia now under her control, Alisandra has access to Gem Crest Bay's trade routes and Besnoumeru's financial networks. She's moving quickly to integrate these assets.
- Myastor serves as Sylke's shipping hub and dumping ground for those who displease the crown but don't quite merit execution.

### Military

**Size**: Large

**Quality**: Medium

**Enrollment**: Mandatory

- Every citizen serves. No exceptions, no bribes, no escape. The military reflects Sylke's values: dutiful, efficient, and unquestioning.
- The army that conquered Tornia was well-drilled and well-supplied. It faced minimal resistance and secured the kingdom in weeks.
- Now that same army occupies hostile territory, stretched thin across two kingdoms while watching Joswik's border.
- The navy is growing rapidly, incorporating captured Tornian vessels. Alisandra understands that controlling Ofrenia means controlling the surrounding waters.

### Geography

**Location**: Western Ofrenia, the island at the heart of the Middle Sea

**Biomes**: Dense forests, river valleys, coastal lowlands, hilly interior

**Named Entities**: Gilded Pass (ley line corridor)

**Rivers & Lakes**: Multiple rivers flowing from the interior to the western coast

**Adjacent Waters**: The Middle Sea, Tykon Channel (west)

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Helmsbridge

**Cities**: Helmsbridge, Scarnett

**Towns**: Shimmercreek Falls, Seavault, Cat Fell, Fool's Keep, Exralhorn, Mapleburg, Bridgeton

**Villages**: Numerous logging and fishing villages throughout

### Primary Conflicts

**Occupying Tornia**

Conquest was the easy part. Alisandra's armies hold Tornia's cities and patrol its roads, but the countryside burns with resistance. The rebels she once cultivated have turned against her. Every week brings ambushes, assassinations, and supply disruptions. The occupation is bleeding resources faster than expected.

**The Joswik Question**

One kingdom remains. Prince Edric of Joswik watches his sister's expansion with growing terror. He lacks the military strength to resist and the political cunning to negotiate. Alisandra could crush Joswik tomorrow—but she's learning from Tornia that rapid conquest creates lasting problems. Some advisors urge patience; others want to finish reunification while momentum holds.

**The Ivory Hand**

Alisandra is a member of the Ivory Hand, a secretive organization that maintains global slave trafficking networks to fuel Deoric magic. Her throne runs on human sacrifice. If this became public knowledge, even Sylke's cowed population might rebel. The Hand protects its own, but Alisandra's rapid expansion has drawn attention she'd prefer to avoid.

**Internal Surveillance**

The network of informants that keeps Sylke stable is expensive, paranoid, and occasionally wrong. Innocent people disappear. Useful people are denounced by rivals. The system works, but it breeds a sullen, fearful population that follows orders without initiative or loyalty. In a crisis, would they fight for their queen—or simply stop pretending to?

### History

Sylke was always the poorest of Ofrenia's three kingdoms. When the old king divided his realm, Alisandra received the western forests—valuable for lumber, but lacking Tornia's rich farmland or Joswik's mineral wealth. She was the middle child, overlooked and underestimated.

She made that everyone else's problem.

Within a year of her father's death, Alisandra had consolidated absolute power in Sylke. The nobility who opposed her vanished. The merchants who questioned her policies found their businesses destroyed. The common folk learned to keep their heads down and their mouths shut.

She discovered Deoric magic through the Ivory Hand—power fueled by suffering. The organization welcomed a queen willing to provide both victims and protection. In exchange, Alisandra gained access to magic that no legitimate ruler would touch.

For years she watched her brothers squander their inheritances. Aldric drowned Tornia in decadence. Edric let Joswik stagnate. Alisandra built her military, cultivated agents in both kingdoms, and waited.

When she finally moved against Tornia, the war lasted weeks. Now she rules two-thirds of Ofrenia, with the third clearly in her sights. The girl her father overlooked is becoming the queen who reunites the island—not through diplomacy or marriage, but through conquest, surveillance, and blood magic.

## Ta Minn

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Theocracy

**Primary Inhabitants**: Oznak (Humans)

**Population**: 40,000

**Stability**: Stable

**Core Values**: Pride, personal life and secrets, horses, speed, courage, exploration

- Small, dispersed settlements each controlled by a local priest, who report to the Kazigh—the chief horse shaman ruling from the great temple in Büüli Umén.
- The Kazigh is attended by a select group of servants who spend their lives in servitude and are killed when they turn 30.
- **Selection ritual:** Each year, eligible teenagers stand in a ring with outstretched hands full of grass. A blindfolded horse walks among them and eats from one child's hand, selecting the next servant to be sent to the temple.
- When the Kazigh is deemed unable to survive another week, they declare their successor, who is immediately appointed. The old shaman is then killed.
- Many Ta Minn develop an attunement with the winds that whip across the plains.

### Economy

**Size**: Small

**Tech**: Somewhat developed

**Primary Exports**: Weaving, horse hides, horse products

**Primary Imports**: Metal goods, lumber

- The plains are slightly magical—wind attunement seeps into everything, including the horse hides used in nearly all Ta Minn craftsmanship.
- Products from Ta Minn carry a faint enchantment of speed and air.

### Military

**Size**: Large

**Quality**: High

**Enrollment**: Voluntary

- It is an honor to serve in the military. Ta Minn cavalry are legendary—fast, skilled, and utterly fearless.
- The horse warriors of Ta Minn once aggressively expanded across the plains before running into established civilizations.

### Geography

**Location**: Western Middle Sea coast, west of the Crags of Geth (Griselia), south of the Browthiel Hills

**Biomes**: Grassy steppe, prairie, occasional hills, river valleys

**Climate**: Continental steppe—harsh winds, hot summers, cold winters

**Named Features**: Kanüli Daha Plains (north), Cercesa Plains (southeast)

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Büüli Umén (central plains, site of the great temple)

**Cities**: Büüli Umén, Ta Akikis (west), Toh Hural (north), Avar Sonnon (east), Limoste (southwest coast)

### The Coastline

Ta Minn's southern border is a jagged coastline along the Middle Sea, with several inlets and natural harbors. The Chedwin Strait lies along the southwestern coast. Limoste is the main coastal settlement.

### The Northern Plains

The Kanüli Daha Plains in the north are flat, fertile ground—and contested territory. A river flows from Anarak through a gap in the mountains between the Kharvorn and Griselia, providing a route for Anarak forces to reach Ta Minn. The northern plains are where the two nations clash.

### Primary Conflicts

**The Anarak War**

Ta Minn and Anarak are locked in increasingly violent skirmishes over the northern plains. Anarak's forces come through the mountain gap via the river route; Ta Minn cavalry meet them on the open steppe. Neither side has achieved decisive victory, but the fighting grows bloodier each season.

Tepheranos wants Ta Minn's territory. The Ta Minn refuse to yield their ancestral plains. The war will likely escalate.

**Expansion Halted**

The Ta Minn once aggressively expanded across the plains, their cavalry unstoppable in open terrain. They've since run into other civilizations—Griselia to the east, Thespia to the southwest, Anarak to the north—and been forced to pause. The proud horse warriors chafe at the constraint.

### History

The Ta Minn arrived from the West, speaking Ashakri like many western peoples. They found the windswept plains and made them home, bonding with the horses and the winds. For generations, they expanded freely, their cavalry sweeping across the steppe.

Then they hit the mountains, the sea, and other nations. The expansion stopped. Now they hold their territory against Anarak's encroachment and dream of the days when the plains had no borders.

## Tamadrez

Tags: state, shacklands

Tamadrez is not a nation. It is what's left.

The island of Pesalolo stretches a thousand miles from northeast to southwest, bisected by the Freedom Mountains and divided by Gorathi violence. The south belongs to the slavers—occupied territory where Gorathi ships collect their human cargo. The north belongs to no one in particular—a scattering of villages and towns that call themselves "Tamadrez" because they need a name when foreigners ask. There is no king, no council, no capital. There is only the shared understanding that Gorath could crush them whenever it chose, and the desperate hope that it won't.

Three centuries ago, Gorathi explorers discovered Pesalolo and the Drasnian dwarves who had lived there for millennia. Within a generation, the slave trade had transformed both societies. Gorath occupied the southern coast by force; the northern settlements survived because they weren't worth conquering. The mountains are too rugged, the villages too poor, and Gorath's military too stretched thin on other fronts. So the empire takes what it wants from the south and leaves the north alone—as long as the north stays out of the way.

Gorath's terms are simple: the empire operates freely in the south. The north does not interfere. Any village that harbors escaped slaves burns. One northern town learned this lesson permanently when Gorathi warships firebombed it to ash for sheltering hundreds of escapees. The Drasnians never agreed to these terms—there was no negotiation, no treaty, no signing. Gorath simply announced how things would be, and the alternative was extermination.

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: None (loose confederation of autonomous villages)

**Primary Inhabitants**: Drasnian dwarves

**Population**: ~200,000 (north); unknown thousands in the south under Gorathi control

**Stability**: Unstable

**Core Values**: Duty, custom, pragmatic survival, wealth as security

#### The Non-Government

Tamadrez has no central authority because it never did. The Freedom Mountains made unification impractical long before Gorath arrived—villages on opposite coasts might as well be in different countries. Each settlement governs itself through elder councils, hereditary headmen, or simple consensus depending on local tradition.

This fragmentation happens to frustrate Gorath. When the empire demands that "Tamadrez" crack down on escape networks, there is no one to receive the demand. When a village defies Gorath's terms, other villages can honestly claim they had no knowledge and no control. Gorath would prefer a central authority to threaten and negotiate with. The Drasnians have no intention of providing one—not as resistance, but because creating a unified government would be difficult, expensive, and would only make them easier to coerce.

When coordination is necessary—which is rarely—representatives meet in Yava. These meetings produce no binding agreements, no formal resolutions, no accountable decisions. Just talk, and whatever informal understanding the participants carry home.

#### The Drasnian Dwarves

The Drasnian dwarves are the eldest and most widespread of dwarven heritages, found in vast numbers at nearly every cultural hub across Alaria. The Pesalolo Drasnians are one branch of this diaspora—darker-skinned from generations in the tropical climate, but otherwise recognizable to their continental kin.

Drasnian culture values education, money, and the preservation of their elaborate customs. Their religious and social traditions govern worship, relationships, and daily life in intricate detail—which prayers for which occasions, which foods at which meals, which obligations between which relatives. These customs persist in Tamadrez despite three centuries of Gorathi predation, maintained with characteristic Drasnian stubbornness.

The Drasnians are pragmatic about survival. They value wealth not for luxury but for security—coin hidden away means options when disaster comes. They count, they plan, they prepare. The arrangement with Gorath is distasteful, but Drasnians have survived worse through careful calculation. They will endure this too.

In the south, Drasnian customs survive in fragments—abbreviated prayers, simplified rituals, the small observances that remind the enslaved who they are. In the north, the full weight of tradition continues, adapted where necessary but never abandoned. A Drasnian wedding in Yava still follows the same seventeen steps as one in distant Drasnia, even if the specific prayers now include petitions for absent family members who will never return.

### Economy

**Size**: Small

**Tech**: Somewhat Developed

**Primary Exports**: Fish, tropical hardwoods, dyes, Yava's port services

**Primary Imports**: Metal goods, weapons (quietly), information

#### The Two Economies

The south has no economy—it has extraction. Drasnian dwarves are the product, collected and shipped like timber or ore. Whatever the captives produced before their capture becomes Gorathi property.

The north survives on fishing, subsistence farming, and the mountain forests that Gorath has never managed to exploit. Villages trade among themselves using barter and informal credit. Coin is rare outside Yava.

Yava itself operates differently. The port city trades with the wider world—Ethadia, Shir, Windori, whoever sails through Screamstrait. This trade provides the foreign goods that filter into the rest of Tamadrez, and the foreign contacts that make certain... arrangements... possible.

### Military

**Size**: None

**Quality**: n/a

**Enrollment**: n/a

Tamadrez has no army. It cannot have one. Any organized military force would give Gorath the excuse it needs to invade.

What Tamadrez has instead:
- Village militias for local protection (bandits, wildlife, occasional Gorathi "inspection teams" that get too aggressive)
- Hunters who know the mountain passes better than any Gorathi patrol
- A population that has spent three centuries learning to disappear when soldiers come looking

The Freedom Mountains themselves are Tamadrez's best defense. Gorathi expeditions have repeatedly failed to establish permanent control of the highland routes. The terrain favors those who know it.

### Geography

**Location**: Island of Pesalolo, Shacklands region

**Biomes**: Tropical jungle (lowlands), highland forest (mountain slopes), scrubland (Ryujilin Hills)

**Named Entities**: Freedom Mountains (Apuindi, Gesichi, Tishkung sections), Ryujilin Hills, Slaver's Coast, Yava

**Rivers & Lakes**: Numerous rivers draining from the Freedom Mountains to both coasts

**Adjacent Waters**: Divinity Passage (east), Torgan Passage (southeast), Gindrik Sea (south), Screamstrait (southwest)

See [Pesalolo](../../atlas_of_alaria/shacklands/Pesalolo.md) for detailed geographic information.

### Political Geography

**Capital**: None (Yava serves as informal meeting point)

**Cities**: Yava (~30,000)

**Towns**: Scattered along both coasts and in mountain valleys

**Villages**: Dozens, mostly unnamed on foreign maps

#### Yava

The only real city, at the island's southwestern tip. Yava survives because destroying it would destabilize trade across the Gindrik Sea. Every major trading power has made clear that burning Yava would have consequences. So Gorath pretends it's a minor fishing town, and Yava pretends it doesn't shelter escapees.

See [Pesalolo - Yava](../../atlas_of_alaria/shacklands/Pesalolo.md#yava) for details.

#### Slavewatch

The Gorathi fortress in the central Gesichi Mountains, officially monitoring the passes for escaped slaves. In practice, Commander Kassander Volso runs a profitable corruption operation that takes bribes from all sides.

See [Slavewatch](../../atlas_of_alaria/shacklands/Slavewatch.md) for details.

### Primary Conflicts

**Compliance**: Every day, Tamadrez must choose between obeying Gorathi demands and risking annihilation for defiance. Most villages comply just enough to avoid attention. Some take greater risks.

**The Underground Railroad**: Escaped slaves flee north through the mountain passes. Someone is organizing the routes, providing safe houses, bribing Slavewatch patrols. Gorath wants the network found. Many Tamadrezans quietly support it. A few actively participate.

**Agtakkeri**: The dragon hunting Gorathi ships in the northern waters has accidentally become Tamadrez's greatest protector. But the dragon kills slaves along with slavers, and its methods are monstrous. Supporting it means enabling a torturer. Opposing it means helping Gorath.

**The South**: The Drasnians in occupied territory are still kin. The north survives by staying out of the way while the south is harvested. Some northerners rationalize this as necessary pragmatism. Others fund the underground railroad. A few argue for open war, regardless of the cost. The division runs through families.

**Internal Fractures**: Some villages want open resistance. Others counsel patience. A few have been thoroughly compromised by Gorathi informants. Trust is scarce.

### History

**Before Contact**: The Drasnian dwarves settled Pesalolo millennia ago, building a civilization in the mountains and along both coasts. They were never unified under a single government—the Freedom Mountains made that impractical—but they shared language, culture, and trade networks.

**The Tamadrez Contact (~300 years ago)**: Gorathi explorers discovered the island and its inhabitants. Initial contact was peaceful. Trade began. Then Gorath realized how valuable Drasnian labor could be.

**The First Raids**: Gorathi slave ships began taking captives from coastal villages. The Drasnians resisted, but their village militias couldn't match Gorathi legions. Coastal settlements fell or fled into the mountains.

**The Occupation**: Gorath seized the southern coast and established the Slaver's Coast—a chain of ports for collecting and shipping human cargo. The northern settlements were too poor and too difficult to conquer, and Gorath's military was already stretched thin. So the empire announced its terms: the south belongs to Gorath; the north stays out of the way; any interference results in destruction. The Drasnians never agreed to this. They simply survived it.

**Three Centuries of Extraction**: The arrangement has persisted because it remains profitable for Gorath and survivable for the north. Periodic Gorathi violence reinforces the terms—the firebombing that destroyed Kalashev being the most dramatic example. Smaller punishments occur regularly. The Drasnians adjust their calculations accordingly.

**The Present**: Emperor Veramus maintains the current arrangement because full invasion would overstretch Gorath's already-thin military. The underground railroad operates despite Slavewatch—some say because of Slavewatch's corruption. Agtakkeri hunts the northern waters. And the Drasnian dwarves continue what they have always done: count the costs, preserve what they can, and plan for better circumstances.

### Hooks

- **The Network**: The party is asked to move escaped slaves through the mountain passes. Success means saving lives. Failure means Gorathi retribution on the villages that helped.

- **Kalashev's Ghosts**: The firebombed town left survivors—scattered, angry, with nothing left to lose. They're planning something. It might be resistance. It might be revenge. It might get everyone killed.

- **The Southern Question**: A Drasnian leader in the north wants to establish contact with resistance cells in Gorathi-controlled territory. The mission would require traveling into the Slaver's Coast itself.

- **Yava's Secret**: Someone in Yava is selling information to Gorath—escape routes, safe house locations, network contacts. Finding the informant means navigating the port city's tangled politics.

- **The Dragon Dilemma**: Gorath has finally assembled a serious dragonslaying expedition against Agtakkeri. If it succeeds, the northern escape routes close forever. If it fails, the dragon continues killing innocents along with slavers. The party might be hired by either side—or might have to choose for themselves.

## Tangiern

Tags: state, human, crimson-coast

A human kingdom on the Crimson Coast, Tangiern has survived for centuries in the shadow of the Winter Elves—paying tribute, keeping quiet, and building strength in the vast Fragenstor Mielthøn forest. The elven civil war has given them unexpected freedom. What they do with it will determine whether their kingdom thrives or burns.

### Overview

Tangiern occupies the western two-thirds of the Crimson Coast, bounded by the Dragon's Spine mountains to the north and the Void to the south. The land is dominated by the enormous Fragenstor Mielthøn—a dark conifer forest that has shaped Tangier culture as much as any king or god. The people are foresters, hunters, and trappers who have learned to find wealth in the endless woods while avoiding the attention of their powerful neighbors.

Capital: **Nøsen** (~4,000 population)

### Government

**King Halvard III** rules Tangiern, the sixth in a dynasty established when his ancestors unified the scattered forest clans. The kingdom functions as a loose confederation—jarls control the major towns and owe military service to the crown, but local governance remains local. The king's authority extends mainly to foreign relations, military coordination, and the settlement of disputes between jarls.

The current situation demands more centralization than tradition allows. Halvard has been quietly expanding royal authority, positioning loyalists in key positions and building a standing force separate from the jarls' levies. This hasn't gone unnoticed; some jarls grumble that the king is using the elven crisis as an excuse to seize power.

**Succession** follows male primogeniture with provision for regency. Halvard has three sons; the succession is secure unless the elves decide to remove him.

### Culture

The Tangier people are practical, taciturn, and deeply connected to their forest. They worship nature spirits and ancestors without formal priesthoods—each family maintains its own shrines, and sacred groves scattered through the forest serve as communal holy sites. The elves' daemon-worship seems alien and slightly repulsive to them; they cooperate with elven religion as little as possible.

**Festivals** mark the seasons: the Return of Light (spring equinox, celebrating survival of another winter), the Great Hunt (autumn, a kingdom-wide hunting competition), and the Long Dark (winter solstice, a somber acknowledgment of the hardest season). These celebrations are the rare occasions when the scattered forest communities gather.

**Social structure** is based on skill and contribution. A master woodsman outranks a wealthy merchant; a successful hunter outranks both. Titles exist but carry less weight than demonstrated competence. This meritocratic tendency frustrates outside traders who can't figure out who to bribe.

### Economy

Timber and furs drive Tangiern's economy. The Fragenstor Mielthøn provides seemingly endless lumber, and Tangier woodsmen have developed techniques for selective harvesting that maintain forest health while meeting demand. Furs—bear, wolf, fox, and the prized winter ermine—command premium prices in markets around the Void.

Agriculture is limited. The growing season is short, the soil acidic, and cleared land tends to revert to forest. Most grain is imported, creating vulnerability that Halvard is working to address through forest-edge farming initiatives.

The kingdom has no significant mining—the Dragon's Spine contains ore, but the mountains are too dangerous to work. Metal goods are imported, making Tangiern dependent on trade relationships that the elven civil war has disrupted.

### Military

Tangiern fields approximately 2,000 fighters when fully mobilized—jarls' levies plus a small royal guard. They're skilled in forest warfare: ambush, tracking, and survival in difficult terrain. In open battle against disciplined elven forces, they'd likely lose. In their own forest, they'd make any invader pay dearly for every mile.

**The Forest Guard** is Halvard's attempt to build a professional core. Currently perhaps 300 strong, these full-time soldiers train year-round and answer directly to the crown. Their existence annoys the jarls, who see it as a threat to their traditional military role.

### Relations

**With Klevnaf**: Cautiously neutral. Taoinor has made overtures—alliance against Istora in exchange for reduced tribute—but Halvard hasn't committed. He doesn't trust elven promises and suspects any alliance would leave Tangiern worse off than neutrality.

**With Istora**: Carefully neutral. Lamenrae has also made overtures, emphasizing her reformist agenda and hinting that a progressive elven kingdom might be easier to live beside than the traditional alternative. Halvard is skeptical; a nastier Istora under a vengeful queen might be worse than old-style elven rule.

**With the Dragon's Spine Coast**: Minimal contact. The mountains block easy travel, and whatever lurks beyond them isn't Tangiern's problem yet.

### History

Tangiern's history is one of survival through accommodation. When the Winter Elves arrived millennia ago, the scattered human clans faced extinction or submission. They chose submission—paying tribute, providing labor, and staying out of elven affairs. In exchange, they were left to govern themselves within their forest.

The unification came three hundred years ago when Halvard's ancestor, Bjorn the Builder, convinced the clans that a unified human voice would negotiate better terms than individual supplication. He was right; the unified kingdom negotiated reduced tribute and formal recognition of Tangier sovereignty within the forest.

The current crisis is unprecedented. For the first time in living memory, no elven power demands tribute. Halvard's challenge is converting this temporary freedom into permanent independence—without triggering elven retaliation that his kingdom can't survive.

### What Outsiders Notice

- The smell of pine resin everywhere
- Suspicious stares from locals who don't see many strangers
- Wooden construction even in the capital—stone is rare and expensive
- The casual competence with which even children handle axes and bows
- References to "the elves" delivered with careful neutrality

### Adventure Hooks

- Halvard needs deniable agents to gather intelligence on both elven factions
- Something in the deep Fragenstor Mielthøn has woken up, and the foresters can't handle it alone
- A jarl is secretly negotiating with one elven faction; find out which and what they're promising
- The ruins of Hildaneir have become active; Tangiern needs outsiders to investigate without elven notice

## Tarkhon Empire

Tags: state, empire

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Imperial monarchy with tributary states

**Primary Inhabitants**: Humans, Craven, Neferati, Dwarves, Halflings (varies by region)

**Population**: ~2,000,000 (across all territories)

**Stability**: Stable but fragile

**Core Values**: Trade, prosperity, imperial continuity, the eternal flame

- The Tarkhon Empire is ruled by **King Selron II** from the capital of **Tarkhetan** in Nektuna. His authority is absolute in the core territories but dilutes rapidly as distance from the strait increases.
- The empire holds together through economic incentive rather than military force. Subsidiary states receive preferential trade terms in exchange for fealty, tribute, and open roads. This arrangement is stable as long as Tarkhon remains wealthy—but it means loyalty is always conditional.
- Tarkhon's diversity is a strength and weakness. The empire contains humans, Craven, Neferati fire-kingdoms, dwarven city-states, and an immortal halfling kingdom. They have little in common except profit.

### Economy

**Size**: Massive

**Tech**: Advanced (maritime, financial)

**Primary Exports**: Everything (as intermediary)

**Primary Imports**: Everything (as intermediary)

- Tarkhon controls the **Tarkhon Strait**—the only sea passage between the Middle Sea and the open western ocean. All maritime trade between the Middle Sea kingdoms and the wider world passes through Tarkhon-controlled waters.
- The empire doesn't produce much itself. It *taxes* production. Every ship that passes through pays tariffs. Every merchant who uses Tarkhon roads pays tolls. Every trader who wants access to Tarkhon markets pays fees.
- This makes Tarkhon fabulously wealthy—and deeply dependent on maintaining its chokehold on trade. If an alternative route opened, the empire would collapse within a generation.

### Military

**Size**: Large (navy-focused)

**Quality**: High

**Enrollment**: Professional

- Tarkhon maintains a powerful navy to control the strait. Ships that refuse to pay are sunk. Pirates are hunted relentlessly. The sea lanes are safe—for those who pay.
- The army is smaller but professional, primarily deployed to protect key assets and project power into tributary states that forget their obligations.
- Nektuna's fire leyline produces powerful **firemages** who serve as the empire's elite military asset. A single firemage can burn a ship from a mile away.

### Geography

**Location**: Straddles the strait between Clueanda (north) and Rimihuica (south)

**Biomes**: Temperate coastlands (north), arid highlands (south), volcanic mountains, fertile river valleys

**Climate**: Mediterranean to semi-arid

**Named Features**: Tarkhon Strait, Eronia Range, Fleimrut Mountains, Stone Forest, Sea of Merchants

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Tarkhetan (in Nektuna)

**Core Territories**: Nektuna, Enymu, Kerwin

**Tributary States**: Astrelle, Yaif, Kabir, Gissemari, Wadiyah

**Allied City-States**: Üod, Blvnird, Melaia (First Brotherhood dwarves)

**Other Holdings**: Murth, Vogenfeld (northern shield), various smaller territories

### The Evertorch

In Tarkhetan's great cathedral burns the **Evertorch**—an eternally burning flame that has never been extinguished since its lighting six centuries ago. The torch is Tarkhon's most sacred symbol, representing the empire's eternal dominion and unbroken continuity.

The Neferati founders kindled it from sacred fire brought north from Yaif when they established Tarkhetan. It has burned in the same cathedral ever since—through the Neferati dynasty, through the Severance, through three centuries of human rule. The torch doesn't care who sits on the throne. It just burns.

Ritual magic of time and fire occurs at the Evertorch shrine. The empire's most important oaths are sworn before it. Emperors—now called kings—are crowned in its light. The Kingdoms of Fire have never forgotten that it burns with their fire.

### Subsidiary States

**Northern Holdings (Clueanda)**
- **Nektuna**: The imperial heartland. Controls the strait, produces firemages, generates most of the empire's wealth.
- **Enymu**: Farming state east of Nektuna. Loyal but poor. Ruled by a long line of honorable kings.
- **Kerwin**: Halfling kingdom ruled by Ulyas the Immortal. Nominally tributary; practically independent.
- **Astrelle**: Vassal state of Nektuna. Fully integrated into the empire.

**The Kingdoms of Fire**
- **Yaif**, **Kabir**, **Gissemari**, **Wadiyah**: Four Neferati monarchies that act as a bloc. They maintain internal independence but coordinate on external matters.

**Dwarven City-States**
- **Üod**, **Blvnird**, **Melaia**: Leadership cities of the First Brotherhood. Their relationship with Tarkhon is complex—they're tributary but also exercise influence over dwarves across the world.

**Other Territories**
- **Murth**: Dual-capital state (Eynmore and Vastilin)
- **Vogenfeld**: Uline dwarf settlements holding the northern passes against Hedroscobb's orc hordes. The Vogenfeld Pact is ancient but increasingly strained.
- **Chykum** and various smaller holdings

### Klor the Blood Lord

Two hundred years ago, the **Eronia Range**—the mountains forming Tarkhon's southern boundary—was infested with a massive confederation of mountain clans. Orcs, goblins, and worse had raided Tarkhon's southern territories for generations. Caravans were ambushed. Villages burned. The problem seemed intractable.

**Klor** was a Tarkhon general, brutal and effective. He proposed a solution: systematic extermination. The empire gave him an army and a mandate.

The campaign lasted a decade. Klor earned his title—the Blood Lord—through the sheer scale of slaughter. He didn't negotiate, didn't accept surrenders, didn't distinguish between combatants and civilians. He cleared the mountains the way a farmer clears brush: thoroughly, methodically, without mercy.

When it was done, the Eronia Range was empty. Safe for Tarkhon travelers, at least. Klor died in the final campaign—some say heroically in battle, some say assassinated by his own officers who could no longer stomach the killing.

Tarkhon honors Klor as a necessary monster. The southern territories are safe because of what he did. Whether the cost was justified depends on who you ask—and whether they lived south of the mountains or in them.

### Primary Conflicts

**The Tenuous Grasp**

Tarkhon holds its empire through trade benefits, not loyalty. Every subsidiary state is calculating whether the advantages of membership outweigh the costs. If Tarkhon's wealth falters, if an alternative trade route opens, if the navy weakens—the empire will fragment within a generation.

**The Immortal Problem**

King Ulyas of Kerwin has outlived every Tarkhon ruler for five centuries. He remembers the Neferati founders, the old bargains, the Severance. He was ancient when Tarkhon was young—his kingdom predates the empire by centuries. His continued existence is an embarrassment to imperial narratives of progress and a reminder that some things in the empire are older than the empire itself. Worse, he knows secrets the current dynasty would prefer stayed buried.

**The Kingdoms of Fire**

The four Neferati monarchies act as a bloc, which makes them powerful enough to negotiate collectively with Tarkhetan. If they ever decided to leave the empire together, Tarkhon would have difficulty stopping them. So far, the trade benefits have kept them loyal. So far.

### History

**The Founding (~600 years ago)**

Neferati warlords from Yaif recognized that the Tarkhon Strait could be controlled—and that whoever controlled it would control trade across half the world. They brought sacred fire north, founded Tarkhetan on the Needle, and lit the Evertorch. From the beginning, Tarkhon was built on commerce.

**The Neferati Dynasty (~600-300 years ago)**

For nearly three centuries, Neferati emperors ruled from Tarkhetan. They expanded through trade agreements and tributary arrangements rather than conquest. Kerwin was already ruled by the immortal Ulyas; rather than fight him, the empire negotiated. Ulyas accepted nominal fealty in exchange for autonomy—an arrangement that has held for five centuries.

**The Dilution (~400-300 years ago)**

Neferati bloodlines mixed with human through generations of political marriages. The ruling family became increasingly human—fire-touched perhaps, but not truly of the flame.

**The Severance (~300 years ago)**

The last fire-blooded emperor died without legitimate heir. His children by his Neferati mistress were passed over for his fully human nephew. The Neferati faction resisted. The war that followed was brief but vicious. The human faction won. The pure Neferati withdrew to the Kingdoms of Fire. The Evertorch stayed—too sacred to move, too dangerous to extinguish. But its keepers changed.

**The Klor Campaign (~200 years ago)**

Klor's brutal clearing of the Eronia Range secured the empire's southern frontier but left a moral stain that some believe has never washed clean. The mountains are safe now. The price was measured in tens of thousands of lives.

**The Present Day**

King Selron II rules an empire held together by profit rather than loyalty. The system works—for now. Trade flows, taxes are paid, the navy maintains order. But the foundations are fragile, the subsidiaries are calculating, and the immortal halfling in Kerwin remembers everything the current dynasty has forgotten.

## Tarn

Tags: state, orc, westwilds

A nation of orcs who are very difficult to kill—not because of armor or numbers, but because their souls refuse to leave their bodies. The Tarni control the most valuable stretch of the Grand Tolkarsus river and fight their wars with weapons that cut spirit as easily as flesh.

### Overview

The Tarni are called the Darkeyes for their solid black eyes that seem to look through flesh to the soul beneath. They've developed a unique understanding of the boundary between spirit and body, learning to anchor their own souls so firmly that death struggles to claim them. Their warriors fight on after wounds that would kill other orcs, and their spirit weapons bypass armor entirely to attack the essence within.

Tarn's territory is strategic—they control the middle reaches of the Grand Tolkarsus where the river passes through the Plenjorn Swamp, meaning they share claim to the healing waters with Glivornax. This makes them wealthy, dangerous, and perpetually at odds with their neighbors.

### Government

**Type:** Spirit Council

The Tarni are ruled by a council of elder spirit-seers—those who have learned to see beyond flesh and commune with the ancestors who linger. Political power comes from spiritual authority; military command follows spiritual rank.

**The Spirit Council:**
- **First-Seer Vurkoth** — Eldest of the council, over eighty years old. She speaks with ancestors three generations dead and has "died" twice herself, only to return.
- **War-Seer Gothnak** — Commands the warriors. His spirit-sight allows him to target enemy souls directly; he teaches the war-priests their craft.
- **River-Seer Thulmis** — Oversees the Tolkarsus trade and the healing waters. The most diplomatic of the council; handles negotiations with outsiders.
- **Shadow-Seer Yulthrek** — Youngest member. Responsible for intelligence and the spirit-scouts who observe enemy movements in ways conventional scouts cannot.

Decisions are made through ritual consensus. The council enters a trance state together, communing with ancestral spirits, and emerges with unified purpose. Outsiders find this process unnerving—the council members' eyes roll back, they speak in voices not their own, and sometimes the ancestors disagree.

### Culture

**The Tarni** have dark eyes with no visible whites—solid black orbs that seem to absorb light. Their skin ranges from deep gray to charcoal, and many bear pale ritual scars that mark their spiritual accomplishments. They're not physically larger than other orcs, but they carry themselves with unsettling certainty.

**Core Values:**
- **The Soul Is the Self** — The body is temporary; the soul is eternal. Physical scars mean nothing; spiritual wounds are everything.
- **Death Is a Door, Not a Wall** — The ancestors watch, guide, and sometimes return. Death is transition, not ending.
- **The River Carries All** — The Tolkarsus connects the living world to the spirit realm. Those who control the river control the boundary.
- **Strike the Essence** — Physical victory without spiritual victory is incomplete. True warriors kill souls, not just bodies.

**Society:** Tarni society revolves around spiritual rank. At the bottom are those who have never touched the spirit world—children and outsiders. Above them are those who have glimpsed beyond the veil. Higher still are the spirit-touched who can see and speak with the dead. At the top are the spirit-seers who walk between worlds.

Every Tarni undergoes a spirit-trial at age fifteen—a ritual ordeal that pushes them to the edge of death. Those who return with spirit-sight advance; those who return without it remain common warriors; those who don't return... sometimes come back later, changed.

### Economy

**Size:** Medium
**Tech:** Somewhat Developed

**Primary Exports:**
- River passage (tolls for trade along the Tolkarsus)
- Healing water (controlled access to Plenjorn Swamp, in competition with Glivornax)
- Spirit-blessed items (weapons and talismans touched by ancestral power)
- Information (the spirit-scouts see things others cannot)

**Primary Imports:**
- Metal (the Tarni are not smiths)
- Food (the swamps don't farm well)
- Luxury goods (the spirit-seers have expensive tastes)

Tarn's position on the river makes them natural middlemen. Trade flows through their territory, and they extract tolls from everyone. The healing waters provide additional leverage—Tarn and Glivornax both control access, creating an awkward shared monopoly.

### Military

**Size:** Small
**Quality:** Extremely High
**Enrollment:** Volunteer (only the spirit-touched serve)

The Tarni don't field large armies. They don't need to. Their warriors are individually devastating—nearly impossible to kill and wielding weapons that ignore physical defenses.

**Spirit Warriors:** The core of Tarni military power. These orcs have trained their souls to cling to their bodies beyond normal limits. Where other warriors die, they keep fighting. Where other warriors heal slowly, they recover quickly because their spirit refuses to release the body. Each spirit warrior carries weapons blessed to cut essence as well as flesh.

**Spirit-Scouts:** The Tarni intelligence apparatus. These orcs can project their awareness beyond their bodies, observing distant locations, passing through walls, seeing in darkness. They're invaluable for reconnaissance and nearly impossible to detect.

**War-Priests:** Battlefield commanders who can see the spiritual state of everyone present. They direct spirit warriors to focus on enemies whose souls are wavering, target leaders whose death would shatter morale, and shore up their own warriors' flagging spirits.

**Weaknesses:**
- Small numbers. A Tarni warrior is worth ten ordinary soldiers, but they can still be overwhelmed.
- The spirit weapons don't work on the soulless—constructs, certain undead, creatures that have traded their spirits away.
- The Glivornaxi have learned that targeting spirit warriors with multiple attackers forces them to choose which soul to defend.
- Physical exhaustion still matters. The soul may be willing, but the flesh has limits.

### Geography

**Location:** North-central Wildwood, along the middle Grand Tolkarsus

**Biomes:** River valley, flood plains, edges of Plenjorn Swamp

**Key Locations:**
- **Tarns-Hollow** — The capital, built where the Tolkarsus widens into a series of lakes. The water is sacred here; the boundary between worlds is thin.
- **The Spirit Gates** — Stone pillars along the river where the ancestors are said to enter the mortal world. Major ritual sites.
- **The Contested Shore** — The stretch of Plenjorn Swamp that Tarn and Glivornax both claim. Fighting happens here regularly.

**Borders:**
- North: Grieb (the lakemen; minimal contact)
- Northwest: Uhionai (the tree-orcs; occasional border friction)
- West: Glivornax (hostile; the Water War)
- South: Hedroscobb (neutral; little interest in each other)
- East: Shazuihn (hostile; they raid everyone)

### Relations

**Glivornax:** The Water War. Both states claim Plenjorn Swamp and its healing waters. The Tarni spirit weapons can damage Glivornaxi souls directly—but the Glivornaxi can heal from physical wounds in the swamp. It's a brutal stalemate. Neither side can afford to lose.

**Shazuihn:** The boar riders raid Tarni territory too, though less successfully. Spirit warriors are hard to kill quickly, and the Shazuihni prefer quick raids. Still, they come.

**Uhionai:** Occasional friction over the border where Ryunimir Forest meets Tarni river territory. The tree-orcs are defensive; the Tarni don't particularly want their land. Skirmishes happen when young warriors need to prove themselves.

**Hedroscobb:** Minimal contact. The Tarni have nothing the Hedroscobbi want, and vice versa.

**Grieb:** Respectful distance. The Tarni spirit-seers can sense something old and powerful in the northern lakes. They don't fear the Griebi exactly—but they understand that some neighbors are better left alone.

**Vogenfeld:** No direct contact. The dwarves are too far south.

**The Orc Moot:** The Tarni attend and participate more than most. Their spirit-seers provide neutral ground for negotiations—they can tell when someone is lying.

### Conflicts

**The Water War:** The central conflict. Plenjorn Swamp's healing waters are priceless, and both Tarn and Glivornax claim them. The Tarni have the advantage in direct combat—spirit weapons are devastating—but the Glivornaxi have home-field advantage in the swamps. Neither side can win decisively.

**The Inheritance Question:** First-Seer Vurkoth is old, and the question of succession looms. Shadow-Seer Yulthrek is ambitious; War-Seer Gothnak is conservative. If the council fragments, Tarn's enemies will notice.

**The Fading:** Some spirit-seers whisper that the boundary between worlds is weakening. More spirits linger than before. More Tarni return from death. This sounds like good news until you ask: where are all these spirits coming from? What is pushing them into the mortal world?

### History

The Tarni discovered their spiritual gifts generations ago when a great shaman named Tarn (for whom the state is named) nearly died in battle and found his soul caught between worlds. Instead of passing on, he learned to cling to his body—and to see others' souls as they truly were.

Tarn taught his techniques to his children, and they taught theirs. Within generations, the Tarni had developed spirit-sight as a cultural inheritance. They claimed the river because Tarn had died beside it; they believe the Tolkarsus carries souls downstream to whatever comes after.

The Water War with Glivornax began when both states realized the healing waters existed. It has continued, on and off, for over sixty years.

### Player Hooks

- Seek a spirit-seer's help to contact a dead loved one
- Negotiate the Water War between Tarn and Glivornax
- Undergo the spirit-trial and gain Tarni abilities (or die trying)
- Investigate the Fading—why are so many spirits lingering?
- Steal a spirit-weapon (incredibly difficult; they're spiritually bound to their wielders)
- Use Tarn's position as neutral ground to negotiate between other orc states

## Teku

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Council oligarchy (founding families)

**Primary Inhabitants**: Mixed humans (descended from multi-cultural shipwreck survivors)

**Population**: ~8,000 (fluctuates with trade seasons)

**Stability**: Stable (external threats unite the population)

**Core Values**: Survival, adaptation, shark-mastery, community resilience

Teku exists because its founders couldn't leave and their descendants learned not to want to. The city-state occupies Survivor's Island in the heart of the Sea of Sharks—waters so dangerous that normal ships can't cross them. The inhabitants have spent generations developing techniques to survive where nothing should.

The population is remarkably diverse. The founding refugees came from a dozen different cultures; their descendants have blended into something uniquely Tekuan—a people defined not by ancestry but by their relationship with the sharks.

### Economy

**Size**: Small (but essential to regional trade)

**Tech**: Standard, advanced in shark-resistance technology

**Primary Exports**: Safe passage, shark products, salvage goods, navigation services

**Primary Imports**: Metal (for hull reinforcement), food variety, manufactured goods

Teku's economy is built on being the only safe harbor in the Sea of Sharks. Ships that must cross the shark waters—carrying goods between the Shattered Sea and southern regions—stop at Teku and pay whatever the city charges.

The shark-hunting industry provides secondary income: shark hide, teeth, oil, and meat all have value. Salvage from wrecked ships supplements the economy; Teku salvagers are experts at recovering cargo from shark-infested waters.

### Military

**Size**: Small

**Quality**: Exceptional in shark waters

**Enrollment**: Shark-hunters serve as de facto military

Teku has no formal military because it doesn't need one. The Sea of Sharks is the city's defense. Any attacking fleet would have to cross shark-infested waters, losing ships and crews before reaching the island.

The shark-hunters serve as the city's warriors when needed. They're experts at operating in conditions that would kill normal fighters—small boats in dangerous waters, close combat with marine predators, the psychology of survival.

### Geography

**Location**: Survivor's Island, central Sea of Sharks

**Biomes**: Rocky tropical island surrounded by shark-infested waters

**Climate**: Warm, humid, tropical

**Named Features**: Survivor's Island, the Barrier Harbor

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Teku (the only significant settlement on Survivor's Island)

### The Shark Council

Teku is governed by the **Shark Council**—representatives from the twelve founding families who've held power since the city's desperate early days. Council positions pass within families, though demonstrated incompetence can trigger replacement.

The Council manages:
- Harbor fees and trade regulations
- Shark defense maintenance
- Hunter coordination
- Dispute resolution

**Council Head**: **Admiral Kess Ironhull**, elected from among the Council members based on demonstrated shark-killing prowess and administrative competence.

### Primary Conflicts

**The Isolation Question**

Some younger Tekuans wonder if the city should expand—claim more territory, build more ships, become a regional power. Elders argue that Teku's strength is its isolation; trying to be more would risk everything.

**The Metal Shortage**

Teku depends on imported metal for hull reinforcement. The supply chains are vulnerable to disruption from Shattered Sea politics. Finding reliable suppliers is a constant concern.

**The Breeding Grounds**

Why are the sharks in the Sea of Sharks so numerous and aggressive? Some Tekuans want to find the breeding grounds and control the population permanently. Others argue this would destroy the natural defense that keeps Teku safe.

### Notable Figures

**Admiral Kess Ironhull** — Council Head and legendary shark-hunter. She's personally killed more sharks than anyone else alive and maintains her position through continued demonstration of competence.

**Salvage Master Dorek Finch** — Runs the salvage operations that recover cargo from wrecked ships. He knows every wreck site in the Sea of Sharks and has strong opinions about territorial claims.

**Old Coral** — A shark-hunter who survived being swallowed by a massive shark and cut his way out from inside. He's mostly retired now but still trains young hunters.

### History

**The Founding** (~400 years ago): Refugee ships fleeing an unknown war were blown into the Sea of Sharks. Most were destroyed. Survivors established a settlement on the only significant island.

**The Desperate Years**: Early Teku barely survived. Each generation learned from the sharks, developed new techniques, and passed knowledge to the next.

**The Harbor**: Construction of the Barrier Harbor—a protected lagoon with underwater barriers—transformed Teku from survivor camp to functioning city.

**The Present**: Teku at equilibrium—not growing, not declining, simply persisting in a place that should be uninhabitable.

## Tenches

Tags: state

Inhabited by Ezuri. Live in towering tree in center of island, many miles across. Entire island is trapped to shit.

## Thespia

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Absolute monarchy (in chaos)

**Primary Inhabitants**: Humans

**Population**: 50,000

**Stability**: Very Unstable

**Core Values**: (currently: survival)

- The Thespian king was recently overthrown by **Queen Akta**, a mercenary from the south. She is a powerful magic user and absolutely fucking bonkers.
- The kingdom is in chaos. Akta's rule is violent and unpredictable. No one knows what she wants or how long she'll last.
- Before the coup, Thespia was a quiet, underdeveloped agricultural kingdom that kept its head down to avoid angering the dragon to the northwest.

### Economy

**Size**: Small

**Tech**: Undeveloped

**Primary Exports**: Grains

**Primary Imports**: Textiles, metals

- Thespia is primarily agricultural—rolling farmland between the Salty Hills and the mountains.
- Trade is difficult. The mountains to the west are dragon territory. The main routes run east toward Stipen and north toward Ta Minn.
- The current chaos is disrupting what little trade existed.

### Military

**Size**: Small

**Quality**: Low

**Enrollment**: Mandatory

- The Thespian army was historically kept small to avoid provoking Morgnor, King of the Mountains, the dragon overlord to the northwest.
- Queen Akta is reportedly building up forces, though whether for defense, conquest, or sheer chaos is unclear.

### Geography

**Location**: Western Middle Sea region, east of Morgnor's mountains, north of Glorin, west of Stipen, southwest of Ta Minn

**Biomes**: Rolling farmland, hills, river valleys

**Climate**: Temperate—mild seasons, good for agriculture

**Named Features**: Salty Hills (running north-south through the center)

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Geordon (center)

**Cities**: Geordon

**Towns**: Waterrun, Amerstad, Telford, Yunbery, Cricklade (west/northwest); Dadleigh, Syozlus (north); Tutton, Embrulton (east); Ronnymede, Wediton, Everdein (south-center); Camerdon, Lewes, Fellsay (south)

### Primary Conflicts

**Queen Akta's Reign**

The kingdom is in chaos. Akta seized power through violence and magic, and rules through the same. She's unpredictable, powerful, and possibly insane. The old nobility are dead, fled, or in hiding. Common people are terrified.

No one knows what Akta wants. She came from the south as a mercenary—her origins and motivations are unclear. Some think she's after something specific in Thespia. Others think she just wanted a kingdom to burn.

**The Dragon Shadow**

Morgnor, King of the Mountains, rules the peaks to the northwest. Thespia has always lived in his shadow, keeping their army small and their ambitions smaller. The previous king paid tribute and caused no trouble.

Akta has not continued the tribute. Whether this is madness, confidence, or simply not caring is unknown. Morgnor has not yet responded. When he does, it may be the end of Thespia—or the end of Akta. Or both.

**Neighbor Relations**

Glorin to the southwest and Stipen to the southeast are watching nervously. A mad queen on their border is bad enough. A mad queen who might provoke a dragon is worse.

### History

Thespia was always a quiet, unremarkable kingdom—farmers tending fields in the shadow of dragon mountains. They paid their tribute to Morgnor, traded grain for goods, and caused no trouble.

Then Akta came. No one knows exactly how she did it—the coup was fast and brutal. The king and his family are dead. The army capitulated or died. Now Thespia belongs to a madwoman, and everyone waits to see what happens next.

## Thorum

Tags: state

Links: States

The smallest of Ve's mountain states, Thorum clings to the Steadfast Mountains with the obstinacy of lichen on granite. Six settlements, one lake, endless pride. The Thorumni are a people apart—their language shares no roots with Shyona's elegant syllables, their gods answer to different names, and their customs strike lowlanders as either charmingly archaic or barbarously stubborn, depending on who's asked.

Shyona could conquer Thorum. Everyone knows this. The Thorumni know it best of all. But the Steadfast Mountains earned their name—every pass is a killing ground, every valley a trap, and the Thorumni have spent generations ensuring that any invasion would cost more than it could ever gain. Shyona's generals have done the math. The numbers don't work. So Thorum endures: too poor to covet, too fortified to break, too proud to bend.

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Elective Voivodeship

**Primary Inhabitants**: Humans (Thorumni)

**Population**: 8,000

**Stability**: Stable

**Core Values**: Honor, hospitality, independence, ancestral tradition

- The Voivode is elected for life by the heads of the six major clans, one from each settlement. Upon a Voivode's death, the clans convene at Churup Lake to select a successor—a process that has occasionally taken years.
- Clan allegiance matters more than settlement residence. Marriages between clans require elaborate negotiations, and blood feuds can simmer for generations.
- Hospitality law is sacred. A guest under your roof is inviolate; harming them brings shame upon your entire clan. This extends even to enemies—if a Shyonan soldier stumbles wounded to a Thorumni door, custom demands he be fed, healed, and released unharmed. Then you may hunt him again.
- The Thorumni calendar diverges from Shyona's. They mark time by the Auris moon alone, considering Nyxara ill-omened. Hollownight is spent indoors with doors barred; they believe the dark moon draws hungry spirits from the peaks.

### Economy

**Size**: Very Small

**Tech**: Somewhat Developed

**Primary Exports**: Iron ore, copper, furs, mercenaries

**Primary Imports**: Grain, salt, manufactured goods, weapons

- Thorum survives on three pillars: mining, tolls, and blood.
- The southern slopes of the Sunrise Mountains hold iron and copper deposits that Thorum works with grim determination. The ore quality is decent, the conditions brutal. Mines operate only in summer; winter buries them entirely.
- The mountain passes between Shyona and the southern states funnel through Thorum's territory. Officially, the passes are "neutral." In practice, Thorum extracts tolls from any merchant foolish enough to travel without Shyonan military escort—and sometimes from those with one.
- Thorumni mercenaries command premium rates across Ve. They're not the most skilled fighters on the continent, but they're among the most reliable: a Thorumni sellsword who breaks contract brings shame on their entire clan. Employers trust that.

### Military

**Size**: Very Small

**Quality**: High

**Enrollment**: Universal (all adults)

- There is no standing army. There is no need for one. Every adult Thorumni trains from childhood in mountain warfare—ambush, rockfall, the patient art of making an invader bleed for every step.
- The Steadfast Guard, a rotating militia of roughly 200 warriors, patrols the passes and maintains the border watchtowers. Service is mandatory: one year in five for every able-bodied adult.
- Thorum's defensive doctrine is simple: make conquest prohibitively expensive. The passes are studded with prepared positions, hidden caches, and terrain features that turn deadly with minimal effort. Thorumni children learn which boulders are load-bearing before they learn to read.
- In living memory, no one has tested this doctrine seriously. The Thorumni consider this proof of its effectiveness.

### Geography

**Location**: Northeastern Widebarrow Mountains, bordered by Shyona (north), Dern (south), and Meadow Sound coastline (southeast)

**Biomes**: Alpine mountains, highland valleys, mixed forest

**Named Entities**: Steadfast Mountains, Dappled Forest (shared border zone)

**Rivers & Lakes**: Churup Lake, Torokovo River, Kremisch River

**Adjacent Waters**: Whisper Bay (Meadow Sound)

- The Steadfast Mountains dominate everything. Jagged peaks, treacherous passes, valleys that see sun for only hours each day in winter.
- Churup Lake sits in a highland bowl west of Dorlev, fed by snowmelt and drained by the Torokovo River. The Thorumni consider it sacred—clan councils meet on its shores, and the old Voivodes are buried in cairns along its western edge.
- The Dappled Forest marks the southwestern border with Shyona. Neither state claims it; both use it. Secret meetings happen here, duels are fought, and a hermit community tends a shrine to Melera that predates either nation.

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Dorlev
**Cities**: Pichor
**Towns**: Winiza, Kiten
**Villages**: Stefanovo, Gorskiy

**Dorlev** — The capital perches in a mountain valley at the heart of the Steadfast range. More fortress than city, its stone buildings cluster around the Voivode's hall. Population perhaps 2,000. The architecture is practical: thick walls, steep roofs to shed snow, small windows to conserve heat. Visitors note the absence of inns—hospitality law means travelers stay in private homes, which locals consider more civilized anyway.

**Pichor** — The largest settlement and Thorum's window to the world. Pichor sits in the western lowlands where the mountains begin to flatten toward Shyona. Most trade passes through here; most Thorumni mercenaries depart from here. The city has grown almost cosmopolitan by local standards, which means foreigners can now find a tavern that serves something other than fermented mare's milk.

**Winiza** — A mining town on Churup Lake's southern shore. Iron and copper come down from the slopes; processed ore goes out to Pichor. The work is hard, the winters long, and the Winizani have a reputation for dour fatalism even by Thorumni standards.

**Kiten** — Guards the eastern passes toward Meadow Sound. A strategic chokepoint that has changed hands between Thorum and Shyona three times in recorded history. The current arrangement leaves it Thorumni, but Shyonan patrols watch the roads closely.

**Stefanovo** — A shepherding village in the southwestern valleys. Known for wool, cheese, and a fierce local variety of dog bred to fight wolves.

**Gorskiy** — A village below Dorlev, existing primarily to support the capital. Farms the limited arable land in the central valley.

### Primary Conflicts

- **Shyona**: The eternal tension. Contested passes, competing patrols, generations of border incidents that never quite escalate to war. Shyona's size makes them the existential threat; Thorum's terrain makes them the perpetual irritant. Both sides maintain the fiction of neutrality while preparing for the day it fails.
- **Dern**: Relations are cool but functional. Dern has its own problems (the Mez, the Lyzine raids) and no interest in adding Thorumni mountain warfare to the list. Trade flows; diplomacy is minimal.
- **Internal**: Clan rivalries simmer constantly. The current Voivode, Aleksar Gorovich, has held power for eighteen years by carefully balancing clan interests—but he's aging, and no clear successor has emerged. The next election could fracture the nation.

### History

The Thorumni origin is disputed. They claim descent from refugees who fled a great catastrophe in the distant past, finding shelter in the Steadfast Mountains when no one else would have them. Shyonan historians dismiss this as myth, suggesting the Thorumni are simply a splinter population from an older, now-vanished lowland culture.

What's certain: Thorum has been independent for at least eight centuries. Multiple Shyonan expansion attempts failed in the passes. The most serious, the War of Three Winters (approximately 400 years ago), saw a Shyonan army of 12,000 enter the mountains. Fewer than 3,000 left. Since then, Shyona has pursued diplomatic containment rather than military conquest.

The current détente dates to the Treaty of Dappled Stones, signed 200 years ago. The treaty established the neutral passes, formalized the border, and created the Dappled Forest buffer zone. Both sides have violated its spirit countless times while maintaining its letter.

### Hooks

- **The Succession Crisis**: Voivode Aleksar is dying. The clans are positioning. An outsider who wins favor with the right clan head could shape Thorum's future—or become a pawn in someone else's game.
- **The Melera Shrine**: The hermits in Dappled Forest know things. They've watched both nations for generations from their neutral ground. What secrets have they accumulated? What would they trade them for?
- **The Lost Mine**: Rumor speaks of a sealed mine in the high peaks, closed after something was found that the old Voivodes decided was better left buried. The Winizani know where it is. They won't say.
- **Shyonan Overtures**: A faction in Shyona's court is pushing for renewed expansion. They need an incident to justify military action. Someone in Thorum might be willing to provide one—for the right price.

## Tornia

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Occupied monarchy

**Primary Inhabitants**: Humans, mixed

**Population**: 400,000

**Stability**: Very Unstable

**Core Values**: Tradition, wealth, spectacle (pre-occupation); resistance, resentment (current)

- Tornia was ruled by King Aldric, eldest son of the late King of Ofrenia who once held all three kingdoms united. Aldric was more interested in the Gem Crest Races than governance, leaving the state to rot from neglect.
- Queen Alisandra of Sylke recently invaded in a "fairly bloodless war"—Tornia's hollowed-out military offered little resistance. The king fled or was captured; the situation remains unclear.
- Sylke's occupation has transformed simmering popular discontent into active rebellion. Alisandra's agents had been stoking revolution for years, but now that she's the occupier, the rebels have turned against her too.
- The nobility are split—some collaborate with Sylke for survival, others fund resistance cells, and many simply fled to Joswik or the mainland.

### Economy

**Size**: Large (collapsing)

**Tech**: Developed

**Primary Exports**: Timber, ships, luxury goods, preserved fish, temporal services (illicit)

**Primary Imports**: Grain, wine, mercenaries, luxury goods

- The economy was already bleeding from King Aldric's obsession with the Gem Crest Races. Occupation has accelerated the collapse.
- The races continue—Alisandra hasn't stopped them, recognizing their value as distraction—but gambling houses now operate under Sylke supervision, and profits flow west.
- Besnoumeru's time-gangs have adapted to occupation with characteristic pragmatism. They're playing both sides, selling information to Sylke authorities while quietly supporting rebels who can pay.
- Trade routes are disrupted. Merchants avoid Ofrenia entirely when they can, routing through Myastor or the mainland.

### Military

**Size**: Small (remnant)

**Quality**: Low

**Enrollment**: Mandatory (under Sylke command)

- What remains of the Tornian military has been absorbed into Sylke's occupation force or disbanded. Loyalist units fled south to Joswik or scattered into the countryside.
- The navy was captured largely intact—ships are valuable, and Sylke needed them.
- Resistance cells operate throughout the countryside. They're poorly coordinated but growing, drawing from disaffected soldiers, dispossessed nobles, and common folk who've had enough.

### Geography

**Location**: Northern Ofrenia, the island at the heart of the Middle Sea

**Biomes**: Temperate forests, coastal lowlands, river deltas, agricultural plains

**Named Entities**: Glowbud Forest, Shadewood Forest, Gem Crest Bay, Blue Lake

**Rivers & Lakes**: Blue Lake, the Catalina River delta

**Adjacent Waters**: The Middle Sea, Gem Crest Bay, the Passage (south)

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Catalina (under occupation)

**Cities**: Catalina (including Besnoumeru), Mithras, Highwater

**Towns**: Port Edott, Northpoint, Ryerton, Bexley, Ylidor, Oakheart, Meadowlea, Gerstown Rapids, Lowwater, Goodlawn, Tall Woods, Blank Point, Thenbury, Minos, Watertown

**Villages**: Numerous fishing villages along the coast

### Primary Conflicts

**The Occupation**

Sylke's armies hold Tornia, but holding isn't the same as controlling. Alisandra's troops garrison the major towns and patrol the roads, but the countryside seethes with resistance. Every week brings reports of ambushed supply wagons, assassinated collaborators, and occupation soldiers found dead in ditches.

**The Failed Revolution**

Alisandra spent years stoking revolution in Tornia, planning to sweep in as liberator once the old regime fell. Instead, she invaded before the revolution matured—and now the rebels she cultivated have turned against her. They wanted freedom, not a different queen.

**The Time-Gang Opportunism**

Besnoumeru's time-gangs see opportunity in chaos. They're selling intelligence to everyone, manipulating markets more brazenly than ever, and quietly acquiring the properties of fled nobles. Some suspect they're positioning themselves to emerge from the occupation as the real power in Tornia.

**Glowbud Forest**

The royal menagerie's escaped jaguars have transformed Glowbud Forest into a death trap. The great cats hunt humans now. Occupation forces avoid the forest; rebels use its edges as refuge, accepting the risk.

### History

Tornia was once the seat of power for all Ofrenia. The previous king—father to Aldric, Alisandra, and their brother in Joswik—united the island through diplomacy, marriage, and occasional war. Under his rule, Ofrenia prospered. The Gem Crest Races were prestigious events, not gambling dens. The time and darkness ley lines that cross Tornia were studied by respected scholars, not exploited by criminals.

When the old king died, he divided Ofrenia among his three children, expecting them to rule in harmony. Instead, they turned on each other within a year.

Tornia received Aldric, the eldest—handsome, charming, and utterly uninterested in governance. He inherited the richest kingdom and the strongest claim to reunification, then squandered both on pleasure and spectacle. The races consumed his attention. The treasury drained. The borders weakened.

Alisandra watched from Sylke, patient as a spider. She sent agents to fan revolutionary sentiment, bribed border commanders, and waited for the perfect moment. When she finally moved, Tornia's military collapsed in weeks. The "bloodless war" was bloodless because there was barely anyone willing to fight for Aldric.

Now Tornia is occupied territory, and Alisandra is learning that conquest is easier than rule. The land remembers better days—ancient roads built by forgotten empires, temples to half-forgotten gods, pre-human ruins beneath Catalina where the time-gangs learned their craft. That history doesn't belong to Sylke, and Tornia's people haven't forgotten it.

## Trømgar

Tags: state, dwarves, innerrim

The mountain fortress. Trømgar is a dwarven nation where warfare has become religion, where armor is sacred art, and where how one dies matters more than how one lived. The Strømgodden have carved their civilization into the Thunderdark Peaks, creating fortress-cities that have never fallen and forging a culture that measures worth in battle-scars and glorious endings.

This is not mere militarism—the Strømgodden genuinely believe that combat is holy, that sacrifice in battle honors the gods, and that a spectacular death redeems any life. Their spiked armor transforms each warrior's body into a weapon; their charge attacks trade damage given for damage taken, accepting wounds to deliver devastation. They are simultaneously the most honorable and the most terrifying warriors on Alaria.

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Military meritocracy (Warcouncil)

**Primary Inhabitants**: Strømgodden (battle dwarves)

**Population**: ~50,000

**Stability**: Very stable

**Core Values**: Sacrifice, fury, glory, battle, bravery, "full heart"

#### The Warcouncil

Trømgar is ruled by the **Warcouncil**, a body of twelve war-leaders who have proven themselves through exceptional deeds in battle. Seats are earned, not inherited—a warrior who achieves sufficient glory may challenge for a position, and the Council regularly loses members to combat deaths (as expected and honored).

The Warcouncil makes decisions by consensus when possible, by combat when necessary. Disputes that cannot be resolved through debate are settled in the **Ring of Judgment**, where the disagreeing parties fight until one yields or dies. This sounds chaotic to outsiders, but it produces remarkably efficient governance—the Strømgodden don't waste time on debates that could be settled by blade.

The current Council includes warriors from each major fortress-city, ensuring regional representation, plus several "wandering seats" held by heroes whose deeds transcend local affiliation.

#### The High Forge-Master

A unique position outside the Warcouncil: the **High Forge-Master** oversees all armor-smithing in Trømgar. This role is spiritual as much as practical—the Forge-Master ensures that sacred techniques are preserved, that the gods of war receive their due honor in every piece of armor created, and that no inferior work leaves the forges.

The current High Forge-Master, **Valdrik Ironvein**, has held the position for forty years. His armor is worn by half the Warcouncil, and his word on matters of smithing tradition carries more weight than any warrior's blade.

#### Strømgodden Society

Strømgodden society is organized around the concept of **drengskald**—roughly translated as "warrior-worth" or "battle-reputation." Every adult Strømgodden accumulates drengskald through combat, craftsmanship (especially armor-smithing), and sacrifice. Those with high drengskald command respect; those with low drengskald are pitied rather than scorned.

Children begin combat training at age ten. By fifteen, they've forged their first piece of spiked armor—a coming-of-age ritual that marks the transition to adulthood. By twenty, most have seen their first real combat against Ix'Vasyla raiders or in the ritual challenges that settle personal disputes.

Women fight alongside men in Strømgodden culture; the gods care only for courage, not gender. Some of the most legendary warriors in Trømgar's history have been women, and their names are carved in the Hall of Glorious Ends alongside any man's.

### Economy

**Size**: Small

**Tech**: Developed (specialized)

**Primary Exports**: Weapons, armor, metalwork, mercenary services

**Primary Imports**: Food, textiles, luxury goods

#### The Forge Economy

Trømgar's economy runs on metal and war. The Thunderdark Peaks provide abundant iron, copper, and the rare alloys needed for superior armor-smithing. Strømgodden metalwork commands premium prices across Alaria—their weapons never break, their armor never fails, and their spiked designs are both functional and terrifying.

Beyond equipment, the Strømgodden export their services. Strømgodden mercenaries are expensive but worth it—disciplined, fearless, and bound by personal honor to fulfill their contracts. They're especially valued for desperate situations where other soldiers would break and run.

#### Economic Limitations

Food is Trømgar's weakness. The mountains don't support significant agriculture, and the population depends on trade for grain, vegetables, and anything that doesn't grow in stone. This vulnerability is mitigated by extensive stockpiles—every fortress-city maintains years' worth of preserved food—but a prolonged siege or trade embargo would eventually bite.

The Strømgodden are aware of this weakness and deeply resentful of it. Their dependence on lowland food is considered slightly shameful, a necessary compromise with a world that doesn't cooperate with dwarven ideals.

### Military

**Size**: Medium

**Quality**: Extremely High

**Enrollment**: Universal

#### The Spiked Doctrine

Strømgodden combat doctrine is unique: their armor is their primary weapon. Every warrior wears custom-fitted armor embedded with spikes, blades, and protrusions designed to turn the body into a weapon. The signature **spiked charge** involves building momentum and slamming into enemies body-first, the armor's spikes doing the killing.

This fighting style is inherently sacrificial. The impact damages the charger as well as the target. Warriors accept wounds to deliver wounds, trading their own blood for enemy blood. Against most opponents, this exchange favors the armored dwarf—but the Strømgodden would use the tactic even if it didn't, because sacrifice itself is holy.

#### Organization

The Strømgodden military is organized by fortress-city. Each settlement maintains its own garrison and can field warriors for offensive operations when the Warcouncil calls. A full muster of all fortress-cities would produce perhaps 15,000 warriors—small compared to nations like Gorath, but each Strømgodden fighter is worth several ordinary soldiers.

Elite units include:
- **The Venom-Scarred**: Warriors who have survived Ix'Vasyla bites, specialists in anti-lizardfolk combat
- **The Tunnel-Breakers**: Experts in underground warfare, maintaining the tunnel network and fighting in its depths
- **The Storm-Riders**: Warriors who fight during thunderstorms, using the lightning and chaos to their advantage
