#### Every Citizen a Soldier

Military service in Trømgar isn't mandatory because it doesn't need to be—the entire culture is military. Every adult Strømgodden trains for combat, maintains their armor, and stands ready to fight when called. There is no distinction between "soldier" and "civilian" because the concept of civilian doesn't exist.

### Geography

**Location**: Eastern Inner Rim (Thunderdark Peaks)

**Biomes**: Mountain (dominant), highland forest, coastal mangroves (claimed but unoccupied)

**Named Regions**: Thunderdark Peaks, Duskwood Forest, Whispering Mangroves, Croaking Briars (border)

**Rivers**: Several unnamed rivers flowing from the peaks

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Levke

**Fortress-Cities**: Andvik, Kavnendal

**Outposts**: Traut

### Relations

**Nashua**: Eternal war. The Ix'Vasyla and Strømgodden have fought for generations in a conflict that has become almost ritualized. Neither side can conquer the other—the dwarves can't survive in the toxic marshes, the lizardfolk can't take the mountain fortresses. Both sides seem to find this arrangement... acceptable. The enemy you know, and all that.

**Gorath**: Cold war heating up. The Strømgodden are furious about Gorath's enslavement of Drasnian dwarves—distant kin, but kin nonetheless. Diplomatic protests have been ignored. Trade sanctions have been ineffective. More direct action is being discussed in the Warcouncil, though Gorath's sheer size makes open war inadvisable.

**Phirexes**: Barrier relationship. The Croaking Briars prevent meaningful contact. The Strømgodden know something lies beyond the briars, ruled by some queen the traders whisper about, but they can't reach it and it can't reach them. A frustrating stalemate for a people who prefer problems they can hit.

**Other Dwarven Nations**: Complicated kinship. The Strømgodden consider themselves the truest dwarves—the ones who remember what it means to be warriors. They view other dwarven cultures with a mixture of kinship and contempt, respecting their craftsmanship while deploring their softness.

### Primary Conflicts

- **The Nashua War**: Endless but contained. Seasonal campaigns, ritual raids, acceptable casualties. Neither side wants to escalate because neither can win.

- **The Gorath Question**: How to respond to the enslavement of Drasnian kin? Open war is suicide against Gorath's numbers. Doing nothing is dishonorable. The Warcouncil debates while young hotheads agitate for action.

- **The Briars**: A frustration rather than a conflict. The Strømgodden hate that they can't breach the Croaking Briars through force. It offends their worldview.

### History

The Strømgodden arrived in the Thunderdark Peaks in an era now lost to exact record—at least eight centuries ago, possibly more. They came from somewhere else, fleeing or conquering or simply wandering, and found mountains that suited them.

The first fortress-cities rose within decades. The wars with the Ix'Vasyla began almost immediately and have never truly stopped. The culture of sacred warfare developed over generations, crystallizing into its current form roughly three centuries ago when the **Prophet Bjornir** codified the theology of glorious death.

Recent centuries have been stable—if "stable" can describe a nation in perpetual war. The Strømgodden population remains steady, deaths roughly balanced by births, the eternal conflict with Nashua providing both threat and meaning. The rising tension with Gorath over the Drasnian question is the first significant change in generations.

### Culture

#### Glorious Death

The Strømgodden believe that how one dies determines one's fate in the afterlife. A glorious death—in battle, through sacrifice, achieving something worthy—earns a place in the eternal feast-halls of the war-gods. An inglorious death—from old age, disease, or cowardice—condemns one to... something worse. The theology is vague on exactly what, but no Strømgodden wants to find out.

This belief shapes everything. The elderly seek death in combat rather than fade away. The sick volunteer for suicide missions. No Strømgodden retires, ever. They fight until they can't, then they find a way to die well.

#### The Armor-Soul

Strømgodden believe that a warrior's soul partially inhabits their armor. The forging process isn't just metalworking—it's spiritual binding, weaving the wearer's essence into the steel. This is why Strømgodden armor is never passed down or inherited; when a warrior dies, their armor is either buried with them or melted and reforged with the next generation's spirit.

Damaging a Strømgodden's armor is not just practical injury—it's spiritual violation. Warriors have killed over scratches to their plate.

#### The Full Heart

To act with a "full heart" (**hjartenful**) is the highest Strømgodden virtue: to commit completely, to hold nothing back, to throw oneself entirely into battle, craft, love, or anything worth doing. Half-measures are contemptible. If something is worth doing, it's worth dying for.

This philosophy produces warriors of terrifying commitment—and a society that struggles with nuance, compromise, and the kind of patient diplomacy that other nations practice.

### Hooks & Tensions

**The Drasnian Underground**: Some Strømgodden are not content to wait for the Warcouncil to act on the Gorath situation. An underground network is forming, planning to strike at Gorathi slave operations directly. The Warcouncil officially disapproves. Unofficially, some members are sympathetic.

**The Briar-Breakers**: A young warrior named Astrid Thornsdaughter has sworn to breach the Croaking Briars or die trying. She's gathering followers, studying the patterns of the briars, and planning an assault that veterans consider suicidal. She might be mad—or she might succeed where generations have failed.

**The Old Tunnels**: The tunnel network beneath the Thunderdark Peaks connects to passages older than the Strømgodden presence. Something lives in the deepest levels. The dwarves have sealed those passages, but seals don't last forever.

**The Peace Faction**: A small but growing group questions the eternal war with Nashua. What if peace were possible? What if both sides simply... stopped? This heresy is dangerous to voice, but the whispers spread nonetheless.

**The Foreign Forges**: Strømgodden armor-smithing techniques are closely guarded. But someone has been selling secrets to outsiders—inferior copies of Strømgodden designs have appeared in distant markets. The High Forge-Master has sworn to find and execute the traitor.

## Tykos

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Slaver aristocracy

**Primary Inhabitants**: Minotaurs, humans (enslaved)

**Population**: 35,000 (including slaves)

**Stability**: Stable

**Core Values**: Strength, dominance, tradition, hierarchy

- Tykos is ruled by minotaur clans who've practiced slavery for as long as anyone can remember. The strong rule; the weak serve. This isn't philosophy to them—it's simply how the world works.
- The minotaur aristocracy controls all land, all trade, and all decision-making. Humans and other races exist as property, workers, or (rarely) freed servants with limited rights.
- The clan system determines everything. Each major settlement is controlled by a clan, and inter-clan politics drive most conflicts. Marriages, alliances, and betrayals follow patterns as old as the islands themselves.
- Outsiders view Tykos with disgust, but the minotaurs don't care. They trade with anyone willing to buy or sell, and many are willing—Tykos slaves are well-trained and relatively cheap.

### Economy

**Size**: Medium

**Tech**: Developed

**Primary Exports**: Slaves, labor, mercenaries, livestock, stone

**Primary Imports**: Luxury goods, weapons, grain

- The slave trade is Tykos's primary industry. Captives from raids, purchased prisoners, and the children of existing slaves flow through Tykos's markets to buyers across the Middle Sea.
- The minotaurs themselves are sought after as mercenaries—massive, disciplined, and terrifying in battle. Clans hire out warriors for premium prices.
- Quarries in the rocky islands produce quality building stone, extracted by slave labor and shipped throughout the region.
- Agriculture is limited by the terrain; Tykos imports much of its grain and pays with the products of forced labor.

### Military

**Size**: Medium

**Quality**: High

**Enrollment**: Mandatory (for minotaurs)

- Every minotaur male trains for war. Military service is a coming-of-age requirement and a lifelong obligation. The clans compete through martial prowess as much as political maneuvering.
- The Tykos navy is formidable—fast raiding ships designed to strike coastal settlements, take captives, and escape before organized resistance can form.
- Slave soldiers exist but are used carefully. Armed slaves are a risk, and the minotaurs prefer to do their own fighting when possible.

### Geography

**Location**: Island chain south of Erpeus, in the Middle Sea

**Biomes**: Rocky islands, scrubland, limited arable land

**Named Entities**: Tiber's Passage (north), Tykon Channel (east)

**Rivers & Lakes**: Limited freshwater; cisterns and wells are critical

**Adjacent Waters**: The Middle Sea (all directions), Tiber's Passage, Tykon Channel

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Slavos (the largest settlement and primary slave market)

**Cities**: Slavos

**Towns**: Toros, Skoldar, Fynol, Alyzon, Pyndar, Stonebreach

**Villages**: Scarr, Seaview, numerous smaller settlements

### Primary Conflicts

**Inter-Clan Rivalry**

The clans compete constantly for status, territory, and slaves. Open warfare is rare—it damages valuable property and weakens everyone—but raids, assassinations, and political maneuvering are constant. The current balance of power is always temporary.

**The Abolition Movement**

Some outsiders, particularly in Lier and the United Free Nations, argue that Tykos's slave trade should be ended by force. So far, no one has been willing to pay the cost of such a war. But as the moral arguments grow louder and Tykos's neighbors grow stronger, the calculation may change.

**Escaped Slaves**

Slaves who escape Tykos have nowhere safe to go on the islands—but some manage to reach the sea, steal boats, or swim to passing ships. The minotaurs hunt escapees relentlessly; a successful escape encourages others. The underground network that helps slaves flee is small, secretive, and constantly hunted.

**The Ofrenia Disruption**

Alisandra's conquest of Tornia has disrupted regional trade, including Tykos's slave markets. Some buyers can't reach the islands; others are distracted by war. The clans are adapting, but the uncertainty makes them nervous.

### History

The minotaurs came to these islands in an age before human memory, fleeing something they don't discuss. They found rocky terrain, limited resources, and a strategic position at the crossroads of Middle Sea trade. They adapted.

Slavery emerged naturally—or so the minotaurs claim. Raiding coastal settlements for workers solved the labor shortage. Selling surplus captives created trade relationships. The system grew, formalized, became tradition. By the time other civilizations developed moral objections, Tykos was too entrenched and too profitable to change easily.

The clan structure evolved to manage competition without constant warfare. Rules about raiding, about treatment of slaves, about territorial boundaries—these developed over generations, creating a society that's brutal but stable. The minotaurs see themselves as honest about what every civilization practices covertly: the strong exploit the weak. At least Tykos doesn't pretend otherwise.

Modern Tykos is much as it's always been. The slave markets operate. The clans compete. The minotaurs prosper while their property suffers. Outsiders condemn them and continue trading. The system continues because no one has yet found a way to stop it that doesn't cost more than they're willing to pay.

## Ubrik

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Democracy

**Primary Inhabitants**: Uline (Chain Dwarves)

**Population**: 30,000 (and falling)

**Stability**: Catastrophic

**Core Values**: Wealth, honor, determination, grit

- Class ranking determined by land ownership. Wealthy mine-owners at top, landless workers at bottom—trapped in debt, working the mines to survive.
- Uline are stubborn, pragmatic, and respect authority. The democracy functions through councils of landowners; the landless have no vote.
- Even before the outbreak, Ubrik was a powder keg—brutal class disparity, cruel working conditions, and simmering resentment.

### Economy

**Size**: Medium (collapsing)

**Tech**: Somewhat developed

**Primary Exports**: Metals (formerly)

**Primary Imports**: Food, luxury items for the rich

- Member of the Aldriktch Trade Alliance, though the alliance is straining under Ubrik's crisis.
- The wealthy lived in luxury while miners lived in destitution. Now the wealthy are fleeing with their gold while the poor are left to deal with the infected.
- Most mines have been abandoned or overrun by silvertongues.

### Military

**Size**: Small

**Quality**: Very low

**Enrollment**: Mandatory

- The Ubrik military consists of conscripted peasants with little training and no desire to fight.
- Completely inadequate to contain the silvertongue outbreak. Military units sent into infected mines rarely return.

### Geography

**Location**: Middle Sea coast, between Camaran (east) and Bestacia (west)

**Biomes**: Mountainous highlands, mining valleys, sparse forests

**Climate**: Temperate continental, cold in the mountain heights

### Political Geography

**Capital**: Grothak (partially evacuated)

**Cities**: Grothak, various mining settlements (many abandoned or overrun)

**Towns**: Refugee camps forming along southern borders

### The Silvertongue Outbreak

**Slick Silver** is a corrupted mineral discovered in Ubrik's deepest mines—a shimmering, mercury-like substance that calls to those who see it. Miners who touched it felt compelled to taste it. Those who consumed it transformed.

The infection spreads through ingestion. Victims' mouths fill with liquid silver that coats their teeth and tongue, eventually spreading through the bloodstream. The silver drives them into cannibalistic madness—they lose all reason, attacking and consuming the living. Their eyes turn metallic, their veins visible as silver threads beneath the skin.

**The silvertongues** retain enough cunning to hunt. They don't just wander—they pursue, ambush, and overwhelm. Worse, they seem driven to spread the infection, forcing Slick Silver down victims' throats.

The outbreak started in the northern mines. Poor miners were exposed first—the wealthy owners didn't go underground. By the time anyone understood what was happening, entire mining communities had turned. Now the silvertongues are spreading beyond the mines, raiding nearby settlements and even crossing into neighboring states.

There is no known cure. Quarantine and extermination are the only containment measures, and they're failing.

### Primary Conflicts

**The Spreading Plague**

Silvertongues have escaped the mines and now terrorize the countryside. Their numbers grow with every settlement they overrun. Ubrik's military cannot contain them. The infected are spreading into Bestacia and threatening Camaran's eastern border.

**The Refugee Crisis**

Thousands of Ubrik dwarves have fled south and west, pouring into Bestacia, Camaran, and other neighboring states. They bring nothing but fear and desperation. Host countries are overwhelmed; some are closing borders. Rumors that any Ubrik dwarf might be infected are causing persecution and violence against refugees.

**Political Fallout**

The Aldriktch Trade Alliance is fracturing. Erasnus is desperately trying to hold it together, but member states blame each other for the crisis. Camaran is using the outbreak to justify further isolationism. Bestacia is dealing with both refugees and silvertongue incursions.

**Internal Collapse**

What remains of Ubrik's government has retreated to the southern regions. The landowners who caused the brutal conditions that made the outbreak worse are now safe behind private guards while the common people suffer. Some refugees are more angry at their own nobility than at the silvertongues.

### History

Ubrik was founded by Uline dwarves who discovered rich mineral veins in the mountains. For centuries, the mines produced iron, copper, and precious metals that made the landowners wealthy. The workers who actually dug the ore saw little of this wealth—trapped in cycles of debt, they had no path to land ownership and no political voice.

The class system was always brutal, but it was stable. Then prospectors struck something new in the deep northern mines—Slick Silver. It glittered beautifully. It seemed valuable. The first miners who touched it couldn't resist tasting it.

Within months, the northern mines went silent. Rescue parties didn't return. By the time the surface understood what had happened, it was too late. The silvertongues emerged hungry, and Ubrik began to die.

## Uhionai

Tags: state, orc, westwilds

A nation of orcs who become trees when they die—and sometimes wake again. The Uihonaii control the ancient Ryunimir Forest in the far northwest of the Wildwood, where the groves of their ancestors stand silent and watchful, and weapons carved from sacred wood carry the spirits of those who came before.

### Overview

The Uihonaii are the oldest of the Wildwood orcs in a literal sense: their elders have lived for centuries, dying and being reborn from their tree-forms in cycles that span generations. They call themselves the Wooden Men, and their connection to the Ryunimir Forest is not metaphorical. Their bloodline is bound to the trees. When a Uihonaii dies, they become a tree. When the time is right, they may wake again.

This makes Uhionai society profoundly different from other orc states. They take the long view because they have no choice—the same leaders, the same ancestors, the same conflicts echo across centuries. They're defensive because their sacred groves cannot be moved. They're patient because time means something different when you've already lived three lives.

### Government

**Type:** Grove Council

The Uihonaii are governed by a council of the Reborn—those who have died, become trees, and awakened again. Political authority flows from accumulated wisdom; those who have lived longest and remembered most guide the nation.

**The Grove Council:**
- **First Root Yorunax** — Has been reborn four times across seven centuries. Speaks rarely; when he does, others listen. His memories stretch back to before the other orc states existed.
- **Second Root Vethani** — Three lives, four centuries. The most active voice on the council; handles day-to-day governance while Yorunax contemplates deeper matters.
- **Third Root Sulthek** — Two lives, two centuries. The youngest Reborn. Still adjusting to his accumulated memories; sometimes forgets which life he's in.
- **The Waking Grove** — A collective voice representing trees that are stirring but not yet fully awakened. Their semi-conscious input is channeled through ritual.

Below the Grove Council are the Living Elders—Uihonaii who have not yet died and been reborn. They manage practical affairs and will eventually take their place among the trees.

### Culture

**The Uihonaii** have bark-like patches on their skin that grow more prominent with age. Their eyes are amber or deep brown, and their hair often takes on the color of autumn leaves. In tree form, they're indistinguishable from ancient oaks or ironwoods until you notice the faint outline of a sleeping face in the bark.

**Core Values:**
- **The Grove Is Eternal** — Individual lives are temporary; the grove endures forever. All decisions must consider centuries, not years.
- **Memory Is Sacred** — The Reborn carry memories across lifetimes. Forgetting is worse than death.
- **The Soil Remembers** — Only specific soil can support the transformation. Protecting these sacred sites is the highest duty.
- **Blood and Sap Are One** — The trees are not metaphors for ancestors; they are ancestors. Harming a tree is harming family.

**Society:** Uihonaii society is divided into the Reborn (who have died and returned), the Elders (who are nearing their first death), the Living (ordinary adults), and the Seedlings (children). Social mobility is inevitable—everyone eventually becomes a tree. Status comes from accumulated wisdom, not wealth or martial prowess.

Death is not mourned but celebrated. When an Elder feels their time approaching, they journey to a sacred grove and take root. Their family tends the new tree until they wake—which might take years or centuries.

**The Weapons:** Blades carved from Uihonaii sacred wood carry the spirits of those trees. A sword made from Third Root Sulthek's first-life tree would carry echoes of his memories and personality. These weapons are sentient, powerful, and deeply personal. They're never sold—only gifted to those who have earned the right.

### Economy

**Size:** Small
**Tech:** Somewhat Developed (in woodcraft), Undeveloped (in everything else)

**Primary Exports:**
- Sacred wood artifacts (extremely rare, only traded in exceptional circumstances)
- Herbal medicines from the deep forest
- Wisdom (the Reborn sometimes consent to advise outsiders, for a price)

**Primary Imports:**
- Metal (the Uihonaii don't mine)
- Food during lean seasons
- Nothing else—they're remarkably self-sufficient

The Uihonaii don't trade much. They don't need to. The Ryunimir Forest provides everything they require, and they've learned over centuries to live within their means. When they do trade, they prefer services and knowledge to goods.

### Military

**Size:** Very Small
**Quality:** High
**Enrollment:** Universal (but only when the groves are threatened)

The Uihonaii military doctrine is simple: don't start fights, but finish them. Their warriors carry weapons of sacred wood—swords that whisper advice, spears that remember where enemies are vulnerable, shields that warn of incoming attacks. A Uihonaii warrior with an ancestral blade is worth five ordinary soldiers.

**The Grove Guard:** Standing defenders of the sacred groves. Small in number, but they know every tree in the forest and can disappear into the woods like ghosts. They don't fight conventional battles; they ambush, harass, and wait for invaders to make mistakes.

**The Awakening:** In times of true crisis, the grove can wake. Trees that were once warriors can temporarily animate, fighting alongside the living. This hasn't happened in two centuries, but the threat alone deters most attackers.

**Weaknesses:**
- Tiny numbers. The Uihonaii cannot sustain prolonged conflict.
- Immobile assets. The sacred groves cannot be moved; if enemies destroy them, the Reborn are lost forever.
- Fire. The forest burns. The ancestors burn.
- They're terrible at offense. Defending the forest is one thing; projecting power beyond it is nearly impossible.

### Geography

**Location:** Far northwest Wildwood, the Ryunimir Forest

**Biomes:** Ancient temperate forest, unusually dense, with clearings where the sacred groves stand

**Key Locations:**
- **The First Grove** — The oldest sacred site, where Yorunax and the earliest Reborn took root. Forbidden to outsiders.
- **Waking Hollow** — Where trees on the verge of reawakening are tended. A place of strange whispers and half-heard voices.
- **The Boundary Oaks** — Ancient trees along the southern border that mark where Uhionai territory begins. Crossing them without permission is considered an act of war.
- **The Speaking Glade** — Where the Grove Council meets and where outsiders may petition for audience.

**Borders:**
- South/Southeast: Tarn (occasional friction)
- East: Grieb (distant, minimal contact)
- North: Unclaimed wilderness, eventually the Northlands
- West: More forest, eventually the Walking Forest

### Relations

**Tarn:** Occasional border conflicts. The Tarni want access to certain forest resources; the Uihonaii refuse to let them cut trees. Neither side seeks war, but young warriors from both nations sometimes clash. The Spirit Council and the Grove Council have maintained an uneasy peace through mutual respect—both cultures revere the dead, just differently.

**Hedroscobb:** Almost no contact. The Black Orcs are too far south, and they have nothing the Uihonaii want.

**Glivornax:** Distant respect. The Glivornaxi understand guardianship of sacred places. Occasional diplomatic contact.

**Shazuihn:** The boar riders don't attack Uhionai. The forest is too dense for boars, and the Uihonaii have made it clear that entering Ryunimir means war. After one disastrous raid three generations ago, the Shazuihni learned to leave the Wooden Men alone.

**Grieb:** Distant neighbors. The Uihonaii and Griebi have little reason to interact—and the Grove Council's ancient memories suggest the lakemen are best left alone.

**The Orc Moot:** The Uihonaii send representatives but rarely advocate for anything. Their concerns are local; what happens in the southern Wildwood matters little to them as long as the Ryunimir remains safe.

### Conflicts

**The Long Memory:** The Reborn remember old grudges across centuries. Conflicts that other orcs have forgotten still simmer in Uhionai memory. First Root Yorunax remembers when the Tarni were raiding tribes, before they developed spirit-sight. Some grievances never truly heal.

**The Fading Groves:** Some sacred groves are producing fewer viable transformations. Trees die but don't awaken. Is the magic fading? Is the soil exhausted? Or is something darker happening?

**The Outsiders' Interest:** Word is spreading that Uihonaii weapons are extraordinarily powerful. Adventurers, mercenaries, and foreign powers are becoming more interested in Ryunimir. The Grove Council debates whether isolation can be maintained.

### History

The Uihonaii were the first orcs to settle the Wildwood, long before the other tribes arrived. They discovered the tree-bond by accident—an elder who should have died instead woke years later from an oak that hadn't been there before.

Over centuries, they refined the bond, identified the sacred soils, and built a society around the cycle of life, death, and rebirth. When the other orc nations formed, the Uihonaii withdrew into their forest and made it clear that their borders were not to be crossed.

They've watched empires rise and fall. They've seen the Wildwood change hands a dozen times. They endure because they take the long view—and because their ancestors are always watching.

### Player Hooks

- Seek an audience with the Reborn to learn forgotten history
- Commission a sacred wood weapon (requires proving yourself worthy across years)
- Investigate the Fading Groves—why are some trees refusing to awaken?
- Mediate the ancient grudge between Uhionai and Tarn
- Protect a sacred grove from mercenaries seeking to harvest weapons
- Accompany an Elder on their final journey to take root

## United Free Nations

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Confederate city states

**Primary Inhabitants**: Halfling, gnomes, goblins, dwarves, Swuigrach

**Population**: 25,000

**Stability**: Somewhat stable

**Core Values**: Freedom

- The United Free Nations, or UFN are a confederacy of allied city states. Each city state is a metropolis consisting of a multitude of races, treated as equals.
- Many consist of banished, once enslaved, or oppressed races. The cities welcome anyone who needs a home.
- Although the cities are allied and have promises to defend each other, they are technically totally independent.


### Economy

**Size**: Medium

**Tech**: Developed

**Primary Exports**: Each city is different

**Primary Imports**: Refugees

- The economies of the city states thrive. Most cities are managed by competent capitalists.
- Those with money are most powerful in society.


### Military

**Size**: Small

**Quality**: Medium

**Enrollment**: Mandatory

- Each city is required to meet a quota of military members at all times throughout the year. They are expected to be kept at a certain level of skill, and each city state's militaries train together once a year.


### Geography

**Location**: 

**Biomes**: 

**Named Entities**:

**Rivers & Lakes**: 

**Adjacent Waters**: 


### Political Geography

**Capital**: 

**Cities**: 

**Towns**: 

**Villages**: 


### Primary Conflicts

- Some cities believe that there should be a more unified government for all the cities, one that could manage the military more efficiently, and also orchestrate better trade deals so that states weren't competing with each other. 
- Others believe that there should be even less government, as they don't want to see control over their cities given away to people they view as outsiders.

## Urzula

Tags: state, city_state, elder_wilds

A city-state built beneath massive waterfalls in the Seyiy region of the Elder Wilds—the only significant settlement in the region outside L'Coth D'hari.

### Overview

Urzula clings to cliff faces and occupies caves behind curtains of falling water. The city exists in perpetual mist, the roar of waterfalls a constant backdrop to daily life. Climbers hang from ropes along the cliffside, harvesting the rare plants that grow only in this unique microclimate—medicinal mosses, exotic herbs, bioluminescent fungi.

Access is difficult by design. The only approaches are dangerous climbing routes or navigation of the treacherous rivers that drain from Seyiy's heights. This isolation has kept Urzula independent and relatively safe from the dangers of the Elder Wilds.

### The Titan Ruins

Beneath modern Urzula lie the remains of an ancient titan city—one of the few titan settlements documented in Aboyinzu. The current inhabitants occasionally find artifacts, strange inscriptions, and chambers of unknown purpose in the depths below their homes.

The ruins have never been fully explored. The depths are dangerous—unstable, partially flooded, and occasionally disgorging creatures or energies that the Urzulans have learned to contain rather than investigate. They are more interested in surviving the present than excavating the past.

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Council (elected representatives from major guilds)

**Primary Inhabitants**: Humans, with small populations of other races

**Population**: Approximately 3,000 permanent residents

**Stability**: Stable

The city is governed by a council drawn from its major guilds—the Climbers' Guild, the Herbalists' Collective, the Traders' Circle, and the Guardians (who maintain the city's defenses and contain threats from the depths).

### Economy

**Size**: Very Small

**Tech**: Developed (sophisticated rope-work, climbing gear, and preservation techniques)

**Primary Exports**: Rare medicinal plants, bioluminescent compounds, waterfall-grown herbs

**Primary Imports**: Metal goods, grain, textiles, weapons

Urzula's economy depends entirely on what grows in the mist. Their medicinal exports command high prices from distant markets, but the difficulty of reaching the city limits trade volume.

### Relations

- **L'Coth D'hari**: Cautious respect. The Gamori occasionally trade at Urzula's edges but view the Seyiy region as their hunting grounds. Territorial disputes occur.
- **Dalizi Confederation**: Primary trading partners. Dalizi merchants are the most common outsiders in Urzula.
- **The Wider World**: Urzula is known but rarely visited. Its exports travel far, but its location deters casual contact.

### Dangers

The Archfalls lie to the south—a maze of waterfalls, ancient stonework, and death. Water hags, pterodactyls, brain-eating amoebae, and treacherous terrain make the southern approaches nearly impassable.

The depths below the city harbor unknown threats from the titan ruins. Occasionally something emerges that requires the Guardians' attention.

The jungle surrounding Urzula contains the standard dangers of the Elder Wilds—though the apes rarely venture this far south into Seyiy.

See: [Elder Wilds - Urzula](../../atlas_of_alaria/elder_wilds/_intro.md#urzula)

## Vetral

Tags: state, alrock ocean, theocracy, triton, underwater

An ancient triton theocracy claiming sovereignty over the entire Alrock Ocean. The Vetralians fled Adron in an age so distant that even the naga have forgotten why. Now they are reclusive, arrogant lords of the deep—and they are losing a war they cannot afford to lose.

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Theocracy

**Primary Inhabitants**: Triton

**Population**: Unknown (estimates range from 50,000 to 200,000)

**Stability**: Strained

**Core Values**: Divine mandate, oceanic sovereignty, ancestral tradition, secrecy

**The Depths Conclave**: Vetral is ruled by a council of high priests who interpret the will of their sea-gods. The eldest serves as Voice of the Deep, speaking for the Conclave in matters requiring a single authority. Succession is determined through elaborate divination rituals that reportedly take months.

**The Sovereignty Claim**: Vetral claims the entire Alrock Ocean as sacred territory—from the seabed to the surface, from Adron's eastern coast to Ve's western shores. This claim is ancient, largely symbolic, and until recently, enforced only near Vetralian waters. Surface nations have never recognized it. The tritons have never needed recognition; they've needed only enforcement.

**The Old Lanes**: For millennia, Vetral maintained order through a simple arrangement. Ships that follow the "Old Lanes"—ancient, twisting routes that avoid triton holy sites and breeding grounds—sail safely. Ships that stray experience accidents: uncharted reefs, freak storms, vessels that simply never arrive. Nobody calls it piracy. The tritons take nothing. Ships just... have bad luck.

### The Bfaspeik War

The conflict with the Bfaspeen has ground on for longer than surface nations have kept records. Two underwater civilizations with incompatible interests, fighting over territory that neither can afford to cede.

**What Vetral Wants**: Ordered seas. The Old Lanes system depends on predictable surface activity. Ships following approved routes means the tritons can manage what happens above their domain. Control is everything.

**What the Bfaspeen Want**: Chaos. The Bfaspeen thrive on shipwrecks—every merchant vessel that sinks adds to their glittering hoards. Orderly trade lanes protected by triton "accidents" are bad for the brood mothers' treasure piles.

**The Current State**: Vetral is losing. Slowly, but losing. The Bfaspeen breed faster, fight dirtier, and don't care about casualties. Every triton offensive follows the same pattern: initial victories, then grinding attrition, then withdrawal. The brood mothers retreat into volcanic vents the tritons cannot follow, then resurge.

Worse, the broods have started coordinating—something Bfaspeen historically don't do. Multiple matriarchs working together, sharing intelligence, targeting triton supply lines. Someone or something is organizing them.

**The Desperation**: The war has pushed Vetral to expand enforcement of their sovereignty claims. They've begun sending formal notices to distant surface nations—demands for vessel registration, adherence to approved routes, traditional respects. It's a bid to build alliances, to pressure the Bfaspeen from above while fighting them below. So far, the responses have been... disappointing.

### Economy

**Size**: Unknown

**Tech**: Advanced (underwater)

**Primary Exports**: Forgecrab metal, deep-sea salvage, navigation agreements

**Primary Imports**: Surface metals, certain foods, intelligence

**Forgecrab Dependence**: Vetral's military power rests on forgecrab metal—living alloy harvested from massive crustaceans that migrate up from volcanic vents to die on Vetralian shelves. The shells grow and heal, making forgecrab armor and weapons extraordinarily durable. But the forgecrabs spawn near Bfaspeik, and the war has disrupted the harvest.

**The Salvage Trade**: Tritons know where every ship has sunk in the Alrock for the past thousand years. Occasionally they'll trade salvage rights to surface nations—for a price, and only for wrecks in "approved" waters. It's one of the few ways surface folk interact with Vetral directly.

### Military

**Size**: Medium

**Quality**: High

**Enrollment**: Religious obligation

The triton military is a temple force—warriors blessed by sea-priests, wielding forgecrab weapons, trained from youth in underwater combat. On their home ground, they're nearly unbeatable. The problem is, war with the Bfaspeen isn't fought on their home ground. It's fought in volcanic trenches, thermal vents, and the lightless deep where the brood mothers lair.

**The Depth Riders**: Elite warriors mounted on trained sea creatures—sharks, rays, and stranger things. They serve as scouts, messengers, and shock troops. Depth Riders are the tritons' answer to Bfaspeen mobility, but there aren't enough of them.

### Geography

**Location**: Central Alrock Ocean (underwater)

**Biomes**: Coral cities, kelp forests, abyssal trenches

**Named Entities**: The Coral Throne (capital complex), the Breeding Shallows, the Old Roads (underwater highways)

**Adjacent Waters**: Alrock Ocean (claimed entirely)

### Political Geography

**Capital**: The Coral Throne—a vast underwater complex grown from living coral over millennia. The Depths Conclave meets here. Surface ambassadors have never been permitted entry.

**Cities**: Numerous underwater settlements, names unknown to surface cartographers

### Primary Conflicts

**The Bfaspeik War**: The defining struggle of modern Vetral. The tritons are losing slowly, and they know it. The Conclave debates whether to seek surface allies (humiliating), abandon outlying territories (unthinkable), or continue the grinding attrition (unsustainable).

**The Alliance Question**: Keletus has the finest navy in the world. Vetral has approached them repeatedly. King Varrosh has refused repeatedly. The insult stings, but the tritons need allies too badly to escalate. For now.

**Internal Fractures**: Younger tritons question the Conclave's strategy. Some advocate abandoning the sovereignty claims entirely—focus on core territory, let the surface do what it wants. Others want total war against the Bfaspeen, regardless of cost. The Conclave tries to navigate between these factions while presenting unified purpose.

**The Breeding Shallows**: Vetral's greatest secret and greatest vulnerability. Every seventeen years, tritons from across the Alrock return to specific thermal vents to spawn. If surface nations—or the Bfaspeen—learned when and where this happens, they could exterminate the species in a single coordinated attack. The Conclave's refusal to explain *why* certain waters are sacred has cost them diplomatic credibility. But explaining would cost them everything.

### History

The tritons fled Adron in prehistory. Why they left, what they were fleeing, what they abandoned—all lost to time. Even the naga, who have long memories, recall only that the tritons were there, and then were not.

The Alrock became their new home. They built coral cities, established the Old Lanes, claimed sovereignty over all the waters they could reach. For ages, this worked. Surface nations learned to respect the routes. The sea was orderly.

Then the Bfaspeen population exploded—no one knows why, perhaps a shift in volcanic activity providing more thermal habitat. What had been occasional skirmishes became constant warfare. The tritons have been fighting for three generations now, and they're running out of forgecrab metal, running out of Depth Riders, running out of options.

### Player Hooks

- **The Desperate Embassy**: Vetral has sent an envoy to a surface nation. They need allies. They're offering things they've never offered before—salvage rights, safe passage guarantees, perhaps even forgecrab metal. But they won't explain why their situation is so dire. Players could serve as intermediaries, translators, or spies.

- **The Breeding Shallows**: Someone has learned the tritons' secret. Now they're selling it—to Keletus, to Bfaspeik, to the highest bidder. The Conclave wants this person silenced before the knowledge spreads. Players might be hired to find the leak, or to buy the information themselves.

- **Behind Bfaspeen Lines**: The Conclave suspects someone is organizing the brood mothers. They need surface agents—people who can breathe air, survive the volcanic waters with the right magic, and investigate without being identified as triton allies. Suicidal? Yes. Necessary? Also yes.

- **The Old Wreck**: A Vetralian salvage priest has offered coordinates to a ship that sank carrying something valuable—truly valuable, nation-changing valuable. The catch: it's in waters the Bfaspeen now control. The tritons can't retrieve it themselves. They need surface divers willing to risk brood mother territory.

## Vogenfeld

Tags: state

### Government & Peoples

**Government Type**: Council of Thanes (dwarven elders)

**Primary Inhabitants**: Uline Dwarves (Chain Dwarves)

**Population**: ~12,000

**Stability**: Stable internally, increasingly resentful of Tarkhon

**Core Values**: Duty, tradition, defense, memory, the old oaths

- Vogenfeld is governed by the **Council of Thanes**—the eldest and most respected dwarves from each of the three settlements. Major decisions require consensus. Minor decisions fall to local authority.
- The Uline of Vogenfeld are "chain dwarves"—underground dwellers who use elaborate systems of chain-operated air vents to survive in the deep. They're rough, tough, pragmatic, and stubborn beyond measure. They've done things the same way for thousands of years. Change is not welcome.
- Every Uline child learns to fight. The monsters of the deep—shadereavers and worse—are a constant threat in the tunnels. Iron blades and hammers are part of daily life.
- The Vogenfeld dwarves consider themselves Tarkhon's shield. For centuries, they've watched the northern passes, sending patrols into the Wildwood, keeping vigil against the orcish hordes of Hedroscobb. This duty defines them.

### Economy

**Size**: Small

**Tech**: Developed (mining, metallurgy, fortification)

**Primary Exports**: Iron, weapons, armor, gems

**Primary Imports**: Food, cloth, luxuries

- Vogenfeld's economy is based on mining and metalwork. The mountains are rich in iron and gems; the dwarves extract both and trade the surplus.
- Most trade goes south to Tarkhon—iron for Nektuna's shipyards, weapons for its armies, gems for its nobles. In return, Vogenfeld receives food (the mountains don't support agriculture) and manufactured goods.
- The trade is necessary but insufficient. Vogenfeld survives; it doesn't prosper. The dwarves remember when Tarkhon paid properly for their service.

### Military

**Size**: Medium (for population)

**Quality**: High

**Enrollment**: Universal (all adults trained)

- Every Uline is a warrior. Children train from young ages to wield the heavy iron blades and hammers that are the dwarven signature. By adulthood, every dwarf can fight.
- The **Vogenfeld Guard** is the professional force—~2,000 warriors who do nothing but patrol, train, and watch. They rotate through the surface patrols that scan the northern forests.
- In emergencies, the entire adult population can mobilize—perhaps 8,000 warriors, armed with dwarf-forged iron and fighting from prepared positions in mountain tunnels.

### Geography

**Location**: The mountains between Tarkhon and Hedroscobb, north of the Wurn Mountains

**Biomes**: Mountain peaks, underground caverns, fortified passes

**Climate**: Alpine on the surface; controlled underground

**Named Features**: The three settlements, the Pass of Oaths, countless unnamed tunnels

### Political Geography

**Capital**: None (council rotates between settlements)

**Settlements**: Atlangsow, Kaisa, Glashof

### The Three Settlements

**Atlangsow**
The westernmost and largest settlement, home to perhaps 5,000 dwarves. Built into a mountain that overlooks the main pass between Tarkhon and the Wildwood. This is where the Council of Thanes most often meets.

**Kaisa**
The central settlement, smaller but strategically vital. Kaisa's tunnels extend furthest north—scouts from here can emerge in the Wildwood itself, watching orc movements without being seen.

**Glashof**
The easternmost settlement, controlling the approaches from the Wurn Mountains. Glashof maintains the closest ties to the Stone Men who live in the Wurns—not friendship exactly, but mutual respect between mountain peoples.

### The Vogenfeld Pact

Centuries ago, when Tarkhon was young and the orcish threat was real, the empire made a pact with the Uline of Vogenfeld.

The terms were simple:
- The dwarves would hold the northern passes
- They would patrol the Wildwood's edge
- They would warn Tarkhon of any orcish movement
- They would fight and die if the orcs came south

In exchange:
- Tarkhon would pay tribute—gold, food, supplies
- Tarkhon would honor the dwarves as defenders of civilization
- Tarkhon would remember the sacrifices made

For centuries, the dwarves kept their oath. Generations lived and died on the northern watch. The stone tablets in Atlangsow list every dwarf who fell fighting orcs—thousands of names, carved in iron-hard tradition.

The orcs stopped coming. The great invasions ended. The tribal states of Hedroscobb turned inward, fighting each other instead of pushing south.

And Tarkhon forgot.

### The Broken Promise

The tribute payments have dwindled over generations. What was once substantial is now insulting. What was once paid with respect is now paid with resentment.

Young humans in Tarkhetan ask: "Why are we paying dwarves to sit in mountains and drink?"

The dwarves have a different question: "Why have we held this watch for centuries while Tarkhon grows rich and forgets?"

The current Council of Thanes is divided:
- **Thane Gorveth of Atlangsow** (eldest) counsels patience. The pact is the pact. The dwarves swore to hold the passes, and they will hold them.
- **Thane Brunhild of Kaisa** argues for renegotiation. Tarkhon should be reminded what the dwarves do and why it matters.
- **Thane Keldris of Glashof** (youngest) speaks what others only think: Why should Vogenfeld keep an oath that Tarkhon has already broken?

### The Northern Threat

The orcs of Hedroscobb are not gone. They've merely turned their violence inward.

Six great tribal states dominate the Wildwood:
- **Glivornax** — directly north of Vogenfeld
- **Tarn** — northeast, around the central lakes
- **Grieb** — east, near the swamps
- **Uhionai/Ryunimir** — northwest, in the deep forest
- And others whose names the dwarves track carefully

These states war constantly among themselves. Territory, resources, honor—the reasons shift but the fighting never stops. This is why they haven't pushed south in centuries. They're too busy killing each other.

But the dwarves remember. They remember when the orcs stopped fighting each other and turned south. They remember the battles in the passes, the tunnels filled with dead, the desperate stands that held the line.

If the orcs ever united—if one warlord rose powerful enough to forge them into a single force—they could sweep south with hundreds of thousands of warriors. Tarkhon, grown soft and complacent, would fall in months.

Only Vogenfeld stands in the way. And Vogenfeld is asking why it should bother.

### The Secret Tunnels

The Uline have dug tunnels for thousands of years. The official maps show the main passages—the routes used for trade and travel. The unofficial maps show much more.

Secret tunnels extend deep into the Wildwood. Emergency passages connect the three settlements. Hidden exits emerge in unexpected places throughout the mountains.

Some of these tunnels could serve a darker purpose. If Vogenfeld decided to stop defending Tarkhon—decided instead to help the orcs—the secret passages could guide orcish armies through the mountains, bypassing the defended passes entirely.

No dwarf speaks of this possibility openly. But Thane Keldris has been spending time in the deep tunnels lately. And some of the younger dwarves have been asking questions about the northern exits.

### Primary Conflicts

**The Tribute Question**

The Council of Thanes has sent three delegations to Tarkhetan in the past decade, requesting restoration of proper tribute. Each delegation has been treated politely, promised consideration, and ultimately ignored.

Patience is running out. If Tarkhon doesn't respond meaningfully soon, the Council will have to decide: Do they continue serving an empire that has forgotten them? Or do they withdraw to their caverns and let the north take care of itself?

**The Succession Crisis**

Thane Gorveth is old—even by dwarven standards—and will not live forever. When he dies, the balance of the Council shifts. Brunhild's caution and Keldris's radicalism will no longer be moderated by Gorveth's patience. What happens then depends on whether Tarkhon has remembered its obligations.

**The Orcish Stirring**

Reports from the northern patrols are concerning. The usual tribal warfare has paused in some areas. Unusual gatherings have been observed. Someone or something is moving among the orcish states, meeting with chiefs, speaking of unity.

It might be nothing. The orcs have had would-be unifiers before, and they've always failed.

But the dwarves are watching. Because if they're wrong, and the orcs are finally uniting, the passes of Vogenfeld will be the only thing between Hedroscobb and Tarkhon.

And right now, the dwarves are asking themselves: Why should that be our problem anymore?

### History

**The Deep Past**: Uline dwarves settle in the mountains, building the first tunnels, fighting the monsters of the deep.

**The Pact** (~500 years ago): Tarkhon, facing orcish raids, negotiates with Vogenfeld. The dwarves agree to defend the passes in exchange for tribute and honor.

**The Great Invasions** (~500-200 years ago): Multiple orcish incursions test the passes. Thousands of dwarves die holding the line. Tarkhon survives because of Vogenfeld's sacrifice.

**The Quiet Centuries** (~200 years ago - present): The orcs turn inward. The invasions stop. Tarkhon slowly forgets. The tribute dwindles.

**The Present**: Vogenfeld keeps the watch, but resentment builds. The Council debates whether the Pact still binds them. In the north, something stirs among the orcs.

Home to the Vyko elves. Gorgeous city, starlit, lots of planar materials, and periolously perched at the tip of the mountain.
